The Early Students and Expansion of the Hanafi School
Biographical survey of students and school expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key students of Abu Hanifa and describe the geographical spread of the Hanafi school as recorded in 'Umdat al-Ri'aya.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's students excelled in distinct disciplines, and his school spread from Iraq to Central Asia and beyond.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a biographical sketch of Abu Hanifa's most prominent students and recounts the early expansion of the Hanafi school. Understanding this historical foundation is essential for appreciating the school's authority, continuity, and the scholarly chain that transmitted its rulings.

Guided Path
1
List the prominent students
Identify each student mentioned and note the specific expertise attributed to them (e.g., Abu Yusuf in hadith, Zufar in qiyas).
Focus on the connection between their specialty and the school's methodology.
2
Examine the praise from other imams
Read the quoted statements from Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i. Understand what they affirm about Abu Hanifa's scholarly standing.
These statements serve as external validation of the school's prominence.
3
Trace the geographical spread
List the regions and cities mentioned. Observe how the school expanded from Iraq (Baghdad) to Khurasan, Transoxiana, Persia, and India.
This dispersion explains the diversity of Hanafi scholarship.
4
Connect to the school's authority
Reflect on how the chain of students and their dispersal established the Hanafi school as a major madhhab with a wide following.
The biographical details reinforce the reliability of the transmitted fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشاهير العلماء المجتهدين، واجتماع أحزابه المختلفين إلى مجلسه من جماهير الفضلاء المتقدمين كأبي يوسف المتقدّم في الأخبار واللسان، ومحمد المتقدم في الفقه والإعراب والبيان، وزفر الفقيه النبيه في القياس، وحسن بن زياد المتقدم في السؤال والتفريع ، وعبد الله بن المبارك الصائب في رأيه ، ووكيع بن الجراح المفسر الزاهد، وحفص بن غياث بن طلق الفطن الذكي في القضاء بين الخلق، ويحيى بن زكريا بن أبي زائدة في الحديث وضبط الفروع ، وأسد بن عمرو القاضي ، ونوح بن أبي مريم الجامع ، وأبي مطيع البلخي ، ويوسف بن خالد السمتي، وغيرهم. ثم أقر بفضله الخصوم، وسلّموا له كلّ العلوم، حتى قال الإمام مالك حين سئل عن أبي حنيفة : رأيته رجلاً لو كلّمك في هذه السارية أنها ذهب لقام بحجته». وقال أيضاً : «إنّ أبا حنيفة لأهل الفقه خير مؤنس»، وقال الشافعي : «الناس كلهم عيال على أبي حنيفة في الفقه»، فأصحابنا الحنفية – عاملهم الله باللطافة الخفية - هـم السابقون في الفقه والاجتهاد ، ولهم الرتبة العليا في الرأي والحديث». وقال أيضاً : (إن كثيراً من أصحابنا تفرقوا في القرى والبلاد : فمنهم : أصحابنا المتقدمون في العراق كبغداد، فإنها دار الخلافة ودار العلم والإرشاد. ومنهم مشايخ بلخ خراسان، ومشايخ سمرقند، ومشايخ بخارا. ومنهم مشايخ من بلاد أخرى كالري وشيراز وطوس وزنجان وهمدان واستراباد وبسطام ومَرغينان وفَرِّغان و دامغان وغير ذلك من المدن الداخلية في إقليم ما وراء النهر، وخُراسان وأذربيجان ومازندران وخَوَارَزْم وغَزّنة وكِرْمان إلى بلاد الهند وجميع
Famous scholars and mujtahids, and the gathering of various groups around his assembly from the multitudes of virtuous predecessors, such as Abu Yusuf, advanced in hadith and language; Muhammad, advanced in fiqh, grammar, and eloquence; Zufar, the jurist, prominent in qiyas; Hasan ibn Ziyad, advanced in questioning and furu'; Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, correct in his opinion; Waki' ibn al-Jarrah, the exegete and ascetic; Hafs ibn Ghiyath ibn Taliq, shrewd and intelligent in judgment among people; Yahya ibn Zakariyya ibn Abi Za'ida in hadith and mastery of branches; Asad ibn Amr, the judge; Nuh ibn Abi Maryam al-Jami'; Abu Muti' al-Balkhi; Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti; and others. Then the opponents acknowledged his merit and surrendered all knowledge to him, until Imam Malik said when asked about Abu Hanifa: 'I saw a man who, if he spoke to you about this pillar being gold, he would establish proof for it.' He also said: 'Abu Hanifa is the best companion for the people of fiqh.' And al-Shafi'i said: 'All people are dependent on Abu Hanifa in fiqh.' So our Hanafi companions—may Allah treat them with hidden kindness—are the foremost in fiqh and ijtihad, and they have the highest rank in opinion and hadith. He also said: 'Indeed many of our companions dispersed in the villages and cities: among them are our earlier companions in Iraq like Baghdad, for it is the seat of the caliphate and the abode of knowledge and guidance. Among them are the shaykhs of Balkh in Khurasan, and the shaykhs of Samarqand, and the shaykhs of Bukhara. Among them are shaykhs from other lands like Rayy, Shiraz, Tus, Zanjan, Hamadan, Astarabad, Bastam, Marghinan, Farghana, Damghan, and other cities within the region of Transoxiana, and Khurasan, Azerbaijan, Mazandaran, Khwarazm, Ghazna, Kirman to the lands of India, and all.'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, part of the introduction celebrating Imam Abu Hanifa's legacy. It lists the most prominent students of Abu Hanifa, each noted for a specific excellence: Abu Yusuf in hadith and language, Muhammad al-Shaybani in fiqh and grammar, Zufar in analogical reasoning (qiyas), Hasan ibn Ziyad in questioning and furu' (subsidiary matters). Then it adds more names: Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, known for correct opinion; Waki' ibn al-Jarrah, an exegete and ascetic; Hafs ibn Ghiyath, a sharp judge; Yahya ibn Zakariyya, strong in hadith and mastering furu'; Asad ibn Amr, a judge; Nuh ibn Abi Maryam, called al-Jami' for collecting Abu Hanifa's fiqh; Abu Muti' al-Balkhi, who transmitted al-Fiqh al-Akbar; and Yusuf ibn Khalid al-Samti. The passage then relates that even opponents acknowledged Abu Hanifa's superiority, quoting Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i in praise. Imam Malik said Abu Hanifa could argue convincingly that a pillar is gold. Al-Shafi'i stated that all people are dependent on Abu Hanifa in fiqh. The author then notes that the Hanafi companions (ashabuna al-hanafiyya) are the foremost in fiqh and ijtihad. Finally, it describes how Hanafi scholars spread across many lands: Iraq (Baghdad), Khurasan (Balkh, Samarqand, Bukhara), and other cities in Transoxiana, Persia, India, etc., forming a vast network of scholarship. This passage serves as a historical overview of the Hanafi school's early proponents and geographical expansion, emphasizing the school's preeminence.

Key Terms
أصحابنا الحنفية (ashābunā al-ḥanafiyya): Our Hanafi companions, referring to the followers and scholars of the Hanafi school.
الفقه التقديري (al-fiqh al-taqdīrī): Speculative fiqh, referring to hypothetical legal reasoning used to establish principles.
الجامع (al-jāmiʿ): One who collects or compiles, epithet of Nuh ibn Abi Maryam for compiling Abu Hanifa's fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which student of Abu Hanifa was noted for his mastery of qiyas (analogical reasoning)?
A) Abu Yusuf
B) Muhammad al-Shaybani
C) Zufar
D) Hasan ibn Ziyad

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's early authority was built on a diverse group of specialized students and its rapid geographical expansion, as recorded in this biographical account.

The Ijtihad Status of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani
Defending the ijtihad status of the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for the independent ijtihad of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani and explain the concept of mujtahid muntasib.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad were independent mujtahids, not mere followers—Abu Hanifa ordered them to follow their own ijtihad.

This passage addresses a crucial methodological question: were the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani—independent mujtahids or merely transmitters of his school? The author marshals evidence from Ghazali and al-Kardari to defend their high rank, showing that Abu Hanifa himself commanded them to exercise their own ijtihad. Understanding this helps us appreciate the internal diversity and dynamic nature of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
The author begins by refuting the idea that the Sahibayn only oppose Abu Hanifa in minor branches (furu') but not in fundamentals (usul). Recognize this as the opposing position.
The opposing claim is that they could not differ from Abu Hanifa in usul.
2
Examine the evidence from Ghazali and al-Kardari
Read Ghazali's statement that they opposed Abu Hanifa in two-thirds of his madhhab. Then note al-Kardari's report that Abu Hanifa knew they reached ijtihad and ordered them to follow their own reasoning when his proof was unclear, forbidding taqlid of himself.
These two quotes are the core of the argument.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's instruction on ijtihad
Al-Kardari's report shows that Abu Hanifa considered ihktilaf permissible and even required for those qualified. This refutes the notion that dissent is disloyalty.
Key phrase: 'لا يحل لأحد أن يأخذ بقولي ما لم يعلم من أين قلته'
4
Draw the conclusion about their status and implications
The author concludes they were absolute mujtahids (mujtahid mutlaq) who affiliated out of respect (mujtahid muntasib). This applies also to later Hanafi imams like al-Khasaf and al-Tahawi.
The practical impact: muftis today can prefer the Sahibayn's view over Abu Hanifa's if evidence supports it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يخالفون إمامه في الأصول، وليس كذلك، فإنّ مخالفتهما لإمامهما في الأصول غير قليلة، حتى قال الإمام الغزالي في كتابه «المنخول»: «إنّهما خالفا أبا حنيفة في ثلثي مذهبه». انتهى وقال شمس الأئمة محمّد بن عبد الستار الكَرْدَرِي في «ردّ المنخول»: «إنّ الإمام أبا حنيفة الله قد عَلِمَ أنهما بلغا رتبة الاجتهاد، وإنَّ وظيفة المجتهد العمل باجتهاده دون اجتهاد غيره، فأمر بترك العمل بقوله؛ إذ لم يظهر دليله، وقال: لا يحل لأحد أن يأخذ بقولي ما لم يعلم من أين قلته ونهى عن التقليد، وندب إلى معرفة الدليل، فلم يظهر لهما دليل قول أبي حنيفة له في بعض المسائل، وظهرت لهما الإمارة على خلاف قوله، فتركوا قوله بأمره عملاً برأيهما بأمره». انتهى. فالحق أنهما مجتهدان مستقلان نالا مرتبة الاجتهاد المطلق، إلا أنهما لحسن تعظيمهما لأستاذهما، وفرط إجلالهما لإمامهما أصلاً أصله، وسلكا نحوه، وتوجها إلى نقل مذهبه، وتأييده وانتصاره، وانتسبوا إليه. فمن ثم عدّهما المحدّث الدهلوي في «الإنصاف»، وغيره، وعبد الوهاب الشَّعْرَانِي في «الميزان» من المجتهدين المنتسبين. الدراسة الثانية طبقات الحنفية. ومنها: إنّ قولَهم في الخصاف والطَّحَاوي والكَرْخي أنهم لا يقدرون على مخالفة إمامهم، لا في الأصول ولا في الفروع، يردُّه النظر في أحوالهم المذكورة في طبقات الحنفية، وأقوالهم وآرائهم المأثورة في الكتب الفرعية والأصلية.
They claim that the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) oppose their imam in fundamental principles, but it is not so. Indeed, their opposition to their imam in fundamentals is not few, until Imam al-Ghazali said in his book al-Mankhul: 'Indeed, they opposed Abu Hanifa in two-thirds of his madhhab.' End. And Shams al-A'immah Muhammad ibn Abd al-Sattar al-Kardari said in Radd al-Mankhul: 'Indeed, Imam Abu Hanifa knew that they had reached the rank of ijtihad, and the function of a mujtahid is to act according to his own ijtihad, not the ijtihad of others. So he ordered them to abandon acting on his statement when his proof did not become apparent, and he said: It is not permissible for anyone to take my statement unless he knows from where I said it. He forbade taqlid and encouraged knowledge of the proof. So the proof of Abu Hanifa's statement did not become apparent to them in some issues, and the evidence became clear to them contrary to his statement. So they abandoned his statement by his order, acting according to their own opinion by his order.' End. The truth is that they are independent mujtahids who attained the rank of absolute ijtihad. However, due to their excellent respect for their teacher and their extreme reverence for their imam, they followed his path, directed themselves to transmit his madhhab, support it, defend it, and they attributed themselves to him. Hence, the Muhaddith al-Dihlawi in al-Insaf and others, and Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani in al-Mizan counted them among the affiliated mujtahids. The second study: طبقات الحنفية. And among them: Their statement regarding al-Khasaf, al-Tahawi, and al-Karkhi that they are unable to oppose their imam, neither in fundamentals nor in branches, is refuted by examining their conditions mentioned in the طبقات الحنفية, and their statements and views transmitted in the subsidiary and fundamental books.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological argument defending the independent ijtihad status of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) within the Hanafi school. The author begins by refuting the claim that the Sahibayn only differ from Abu Hanifa in minor branches but not in fundamentals (usul). He counters with evidence from Imam al-Ghazali's al-Mankhul, who famously stated that they opposed Abu Hanifa in two-thirds of his madhhab, indicating extensive disagreement. The author then quotes al-Kardari's Radd al-Mankhul, which narrates that Abu Hanifa himself recognized their ijtihad capability and instructed them to follow their own ijtihad when his proof was not clear, even forbidding taqlid of himself. This establishes that their occasional departures from Abu Hanifa were by his command. The author concludes that the Sahibayn were absolute mujtahids (mujtahid mutlaq) but chose to affiliate with Abu Hanifa out of respect and to propagate his school. He notes that later scholars like Shah Wali Allah al-Dihlawi and Abd al-Wahhab al-Sha'rani classified them as 'affiliated mujtahids' (mujtahid muntasib). Finally, the author extends this argument to later Hanafi imams like al-Khasaf, al-Tahawi, and al-Karkhi, asserting that they too were capable of opposing Abu Hanifa, as evidenced by their recorded opinions in both furu' and usul works. This passage is crucial for understanding the internal dynamic of the Hanafi school: the Sahibayn were not mere transmitters but active mujtahids whose rulings carry weight and sometimes differ from Abu Hanifa, and later Hanafi scholars continued this tradition of qualified ijtihad.

Key Terms
مجتهد منتسب (mujtahid muntasib): A mujtahid who is affiliated with a particular imam's school but is capable of independent ijtihad and may differ from that imam in some rulings.
اجتهاد مطلق (ijtihad mutlaq): The highest level of ijtihad, where a scholar is able to derive rulings directly from the primary sources (Quran and Sunnah) without being bound to a specific madhhab.
تقليد (taqlid): Following the legal opinion of a qualified scholar without knowing the evidence or reasoning. In this passage, Abu Hanifa is reported to have forbidden taqlid of himself for those capable of ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the rank of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani in relation to Abu Hanifa?
A) They were mere followers (muqallids) who could not differ from Abu Hanifa.
B) They were independent mujtahids (mujtahid mutlaq) who sometimes disagreed with Abu Hanifa by his own command.
C) They were only narrators of hadith with no expertise in fiqh.
D) They were students who never reached the level of ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani were absolute mujtahids whose occasional dissent from Abu Hanifa was authorized and expected; their affiliation was one of respect, not legal subordination.

Defending the High Ranks of Abu Bakr al-Razi, al-Quduri, and Sahib al-Hidayah
Defense of the high rank of Abu Bakr al-Razi, al-Quduri, and al-Marghinani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi tradition holds Abu Bakr al-Razi, al-Quduri, and al-Marghinani (Sahib al-Hidayah) as mujtahids of high rank, and evaluate the arguments for and against their classification.

Core Idea
Earlier Hanafi imams laid the foundations; later scholars are dependents, not superiors.

The following passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya defends two major figures in Hanafi history—Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas and al-Quduri—as well as the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) against being unjustly ranked below later scholars like Qadi Khan. It argues that these earlier authorities were not mere muqallids but were mujtahids whose works formed the basis for later generations. Understanding this defense is crucial for appreciating the hierarchy of Hanafi scholarship and the transmission of legal authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two errors being refuted
Read the opening and closing arguments to see what incorrect rankings are being corrected. The first error is counting Abu Bakr al-Razi among those absolutely incapable of ijtihad. The second is placing Qadi Khan above al-Quduri and Sahib al-Hidayah.
The entire passage is structured as a rebuttal of these two claims.
2
Analyze the arguments for al-Razi's ijtihad
Look at the evidence presented: his precedence in time, higher rank, greater knowledge, and the fact that later mujtahids (al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi, al-Bazdawi) rely on his works. Note the quote from al-Marjani and the chain of teachers leading back to al-Razi.
The argument uses both chronology and intellectual dependence to establish al-Razi's status.
3
Understand the meaning of takhrij in context
The critic claimed al-Razi only did takhrij (deriving subsidiary rulings from principles). The author shows that takhrij itself is a form of ijtihad, and that many senior mujtahids also engaged in it. The examples of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani doing takhrij demonstrate this.
Takhrij does not lower one's rank; it is a method used by even the highest mujtahids.
4
Compare the ranks of al-Quduri and Sahib al-Hidayah vs Qadi Khan
Note that al-Quduri is older than Shams al-A'imma, who is considered a mujtahid, so he must be at least at that level. Sahib al-Hidayah was acknowledged by his peers (including Qadi Khan himself) as superior. Therefore, placing Qadi Khan above them is unjust.
The argument relies on scholarly consensus (ijma') of the contemporaries.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi ranking criteria
From the passage, extract the criteria used: chronological precedence, breadth of knowledge, influence on later scholars, and recognition by peers. These are the markers of a mujtahid in the Hanafi tradition.
The passage implicitly argues for a 'foundationalist' view: earlier scholars are generally higher.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : إن عدهم أبا بكر الرازي الجصاص من الذين لا يقدرون على الاجتهاد مطلقاً. بعيد جداً، مع عدّهم شمس الأئمة الحَلْوَانِي وَالسَّرَخْسِيُّ والبَزْدَوِيَّ وقاضي خان في المجتهدين في المذهبين مع أنّ الرازي أقدم منهم زماناً ، وأعلى منهم شأناً، وأوسع منهم علماً ، وأدق منهم سراً).
هذا من مسائل الأصول». ينظر : حسن التقاضي (ص۸۹). (۱) قال المرجاني في ناظورة (الحق ص ٦١ - ٦٣) : «عُدَّ أبو بكر الرازي الجصاص من المقلدين الذي لا يقدرون على الاجتهاد أصلاً، وهو ظلم عظيم في حقه، وتنزيل له عن رفيع محله وغض منه وجهل بين بجلالة شأنه في العلم وباعه الممتد في الفقه، وكعبه العالي في الأصول، ورسوخ قدمه، وشدة وطأته وقوة بطشه في معارك النظر والاستدلال، ومن تتبع تصانيفه والأقوال المنقولة عنه عَلِم أن الذين عدَّهم من المجتهدين من شمس الأئمة ومن بعدهم كلهم عيال لأبي بكر الرازي، ومصداق ذلك دلائله التي نصبها لاختياراته، وبراهينه التي كشف استدلالاته. فيها عن وجوها نشأ ببغداد التي هي دار الخلافة، ومدار العلم والرشاد، ومدينة السلام ومعقل الإسلام، ورحل في الأقطار، ودخل الأمصار ولقي العلماء أولي الأيدي والأبصار، وأخذ الفقه والحديث عن المشايخ الكبار.
وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني فيه : هو رجل كبير معروف في العلم، وإنـا نقـلـده ونأخذ بقوله. انتهى. فكيف يصح تقليد المجتهد للمقلد؟ وذكر في «الكشف الكبير» ما يدلُّ على أنه أفقه من أبي منصور الماتريدي، وقال قاضي خان: في «التوكيل بالخصومة»: يجوز للمرأة المخدرة أن توكل، وهي التي لم تخالط الرجال بكراً كانت أو ثيباً. كذا ذكره أبو بكر الرازي. وفي «الهداية»(۳: (۱۳۷) ولو كانت المرأة مخدرة قال الرازي: يلزم التوكيل منها، ثم قال : وهذا شيء استحبه المتأخرون ، وقال ابن الهمام في فتح القدير (٧ : ٥٠٩): هو الإمام الكبير أبو بكر الجصاص أحمد بن علي الرازي، يعني أنه على ظاهر إطلاق الأصل وغيره عن أبي حنيفة لا فرق بين البكر والثيب المخدرة والمبرزة، والفتوى على ما اختاروه من ذلك ، وحينئذ فتخصيص الرازي ثمّ تعميم المتأخرين ليس إلا لفائدة أنه المبتدئ بتفريع ذلك وتبعوه. انتهى كلامه.
وقد أكثر شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي في كتبه النقل عن أبي بكر الرازي والاستشهاد به والمتابعة لآرائه ، ثمّ الحَلْوانيُّ ومَن ذكره بعدهم وعدهم من المجتهدين في المسائل كلهم تنتهي سلسلة علومهم إلى أبي بكر الرازي، فقد تفقه عليه أبو جعفر الاستروشني وهو أستاذ القاضي أبي زيد الدبوسي ، وأبو علي حسين بن خضر النسفي ، وهو أستاذ شمس الأئمة الحلواني، ومعلوم أن السَّرَخْسِي من تلاميذه وقاضي خان من أصحاب أصحابه. فلعله نظر إلى قوله : إنه كذلك في تخريج الرازي ، فظن أن وظيفته في الصناعة هي التخريج فحسب، وأن غاية شأوه هذا القدر، وقد خرّج أبو حنيفة وأصحابه قول ابن عباس في
الدراسة الثانية طبقات الحنفية
۳۷
٤. ومنها : إن شأن القُدُوري أجلّ من قاضي خان وصاحب «الهداية»، إن لم يكن أجل منه فليس بأدنى منه ، فجعل قاضي خان في مرتبة ثالثة، وحط القُدُوري وصاحب «الهداية» عنها ليس مما ينبغي وذكر أحمد بن حجر المكي الهيتمي الشافعي (٢) في رسالته «شـن الغـارة على من أبدى معرّة تقوله في الحناء وعواره ۳ نقلا عن «شرح المهذب» تكبيرات العيدين أنها ثلاث عشرة تكبيرة بحمل أنها على هذا العدد بإضافة التكبيرات الأصلية، والشافعي وأتباعه بحملها على الزوائد.
وخرج أبو يوسف قول الشعبي : إن للخنثى المشكل من الميراث نصف النصيبين بأن ذلك ثلاث من سبعة، ومحمد بأنه خمس من اثني عشر ، وخرَّجَ أبو الحسن الكرخي قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد في تعديل الركوع والسجود وجعله واجباً ، وأبو عبد الله جاني خرجه وحمله على السنة. ونظائر ذلك كثيرة وقعت من كبار المجتهدين فما ضرَّهم ذلك في اجتهادهم، ولا نزلهم من شأنهم فكيف ينزل أبا بكر الرازي إلى الرتبة النازلة عن منزلته». ينظر : «حسن التقاضي» (ص۸۹ - (۹۱) ، وطبقات الحنفية» لابن الجنائي (ص٤٠). (۱) قال المرجاني في «ناظورة الحق» (ص ٦٣) : جعل القُدُوري وصاحب «الهداية» من أصحاب الترجيح وقاضي خان من المجتهدين مع تقدم القُدُوري على شمس الأئمة زماناً وكونه أعلى منه كعباً وأطول باعاً، فكيف لا يكون أعلى من قاضي خان، وأما صاحب «الهداية» فهو المشار إليه في عصره، والمعقود عليه الخناصر في دهره وفريد وقته، ونسيج وحده. وقد ذكر في «الجواهر»(٢ : ٦٢٧ ، وغيره : إنه أقر له أهل عصره بالفضل والتقدم كالإمام فخر الدين قاضي خان والإمام زين الدين العتابي وغيرهما ، وقالوا : إنه فاق على أقرانه حتى على شيوخه في الفقه وأذعنوا له به فكيف يُنْزَلُ شأنه عن قاضي خان بمراتب، بل هو أحق منه بالاجتهاد وأثبت في أسبابه وألزمه لأبوابه». ينظر : حسن التقاضي»(ص۹۱ - ۹۲). (۲) المتوفى بمكة سنة (٩٧٥). منه رحمه الله. (۳) قال ابن حجر الهيتمي في سبب تأليف هذا الكتاب في «الكبائر» (۱) : ٤٠٥ - ٤٠٦): «علم من خبر المخنث المخضوب الذي نفاه لعب لأجل تشبهه بالنساء بخضبه يديه ورجليه أن خضب الرجل يديه أو رجليه بالحناء حرام، بل كبيرة على ما ذكر فيه من التشبه بالنساء ، وأن الحديث المذكور صريح في ذلك، وقد وقعت هذه المسألة قريباً من اليمن فاختلف فيها علماؤها وصنفوا في الحل والحرمة ، ثم أرسلوا إلي بمكة سنة اثنتين وخمسين وتسعمائة ثلاث مصنفات ، اثنين في حله مطلقاً، وواحداً في حرمته، وطلبوا مني إبانة الحق في المسألة، فألفت فيها كتاباً حافلاً سميته : شن الغارة على من أظهر معرة تقوله في الحناء وعواره ، وإنما سميته بذلك ليطابق اسمه مسماه ، فإن بعض القائلين بالحل تعدى طوره إلى أن ادعى فيه الاجتهاد ، وزعم أن القائلين بالحرمة : أي وهم الأصحاب قاطبة بل والشافعي كما بينته ثم استروحوا ولم يتأملوه
And among them: that they counted Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas among those who are absolutely incapable of ijtihad. This is very far-fetched, while they count Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi, al-Bazdawi, and Qadi Khan among the mujtahids in the two schools, even though al-Razi is older in time, higher in rank, more extensive in knowledge, and more precise in understanding. This is from the issues of usul. See: Husn al-Taqadi (p. 89). (1) al-Marjani said in Nazurat al-Haqq (pp. 61-63): 'Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas was counted among the muqallids who are absolutely incapable of ijtihad, which is a great injustice to him, a demotion from his high station, a belittling of him, and a clear ignorance of the grandeur of his stature in knowledge, his extensive experience in fiqh, his high standing in usul, his firm footing, his strong impact, and his powerful might in arenas of investigation and inference. Whoever traces his works and the transmitted opinions from him knows that those whom they counted as mujtahids, from Shams al-A'imma and after, are all dependents of Abu Bakr al-Razi. The proof is the evidences he established for his choices and the proofs he revealed in his inferences, showing the aspects. He grew up in Baghdad, the seat of the caliphate, the center of knowledge and guidance, the city of peace and stronghold of Islam. He traveled across regions, entered cities, met scholars of insight and vision, and took fiqh and hadith from the great shaykhs.' Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said about him: 'He is a great man known in knowledge, and we indeed imitate him and take his statement.' End quote. How can a mujtahid imitate a muqallid? It is mentioned in al-Kashf al-Kabir what indicates that he was more jurisprudent than Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. Qadi Khan said in al-Tawkil bi al-Khusuma: It is permissible for a secluded woman to appoint an agent, meaning one who has not mixed with men, whether virgin or non-virgin. Thus Abu Bakr al-Razi mentioned it. And in al-Hidayah (3:137): 'If the woman is secluded, al-Razi said: appointment of an agent is necessary from her.' Then he said: 'This is something preferred by later scholars.' Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir (7:509): 'He is the great Imam Abu Bakr al-Jassas Ahmad ibn Ali al-Razi, meaning that according to the apparent absolute statement of the original and others from Abu Hanifa, there is no difference between the virgin and non-virgin, secluded or unveiled, and the fatwa is based on what they chose. Therefore, the specification by al-Razi and then the generalization by later scholars is only for the benefit that he was the first to deduce that and they followed him.' End of his words. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi in his books frequently transmitted from Abu Bakr al-Razi, sought his testimony, and followed his views. Then al-Halwani and those mentioned after them, counting them as mujtahids in issues, all their chains of knowledge end with Abu Bakr al-Razi. For Abu Ja'far al-Usrushni studied under him, and he is the teacher of Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi; and Abu Ali Husayn ibn Khidr al-Nasafi, who is the teacher of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. It is known that al-Sarakhsi is among his students and Qadi Khan among the companions of his companions. Perhaps he looked at his statement: that it is so in the takhrij of al-Razi, so he thought that his function in the field was only takhrij, and that his utmost limit was this, even though Abu Hanifa and his companions derived the statement of Ibn Abbas in... al-Dirasa al-Thaniya: Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya 37 4. And among them: that the status of al-Quduri is greater than Qadi Khan and the author of al-Hidayah; if not greater, then not less than him. So he placed Qadi Khan in a third rank and lowered al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah from it, which is not appropriate. And Ahmad ibn Hajar al-Makki al-Haytami al-Shafi'i (2) mentioned in his treatise 'Shann al-Ghara 'ala man Abda Ma'arrata Taqawwulihi fi al-Hinna' a quote from Sharh al-Muhadhdhab that the takbirs of the two Eids are thirteen takbirs, carrying it as this number by adding the original takbirs, while al-Shafi'i and his followers carry them as additional. Abu Yusuf derived the statement of al-Sha'bi: that the khuntha mushkil takes half of the two shares, that being three out of seven; and Muhammad (derived) that it is five out of twelve. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi derived the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on equalizing bowing and prostration and making it wajib; and Abu Abd Allah Jani derived it and carried it as sunna. Many such examples occurred from senior mujtahids, yet that did not harm them in their ijtihad nor lower their status. So how can Abu Bakr al-Razi be lowered to a rank lower than his station?' See: Husn al-Taqadi (pp. 89-91) and Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya by Ibn al-Jana'i (p. 40). (1) al-Marjani said in Nazurat al-Haqq (p. 63): 'He made al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah among the people of tarjih (preference) and Qadi Khan among the mujtahids, despite al-Quduri being older than Shams al-A'imma in time and higher in stature and more extensive in experience. So how can he not be higher than Qadi Khan? As for the author of al-Hidayah, he is the one referred to in his time, the one on whom fingers are counted in his age, the unique of his time, the peerless. It is mentioned in al-Jawahir (2:627) and elsewhere that the people of his time acknowledged his virtue and precedence, such as Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan and Imam Zayn al-Din al-‘Attabi and others. They said: He surpassed his peers, even his teachers, in fiqh and they submitted to him. So how can his status be reduced below Qadi Khan by degrees? Rather, he is more deserving of ijtihad and more established in its means and more committed to its doors.' See: Husn al-Taqadi (pp. 91-92). (2) He died in Mecca in 975 AH. May Allah have mercy on him. (3) Ibn Hajar al-Haytami said in the reason for writing this book in al-Kaba'ir (1:405-406): 'It is known from the report of the effeminate man who dyed his hands and feet, whom the Prophet banished because of his imitation of women with his dye, that dyeing a man's hands or feet with henna is forbidden, indeed a major sin due to the imitation of women mentioned, and that the mentioned hadith is explicit in that. This issue recently occurred in Yemen, and its scholars differed on it and wrote works on permissibility and prohibition. Then they sent to me in Mecca in the year 952 AH three treatises: two on its absolute permissibility, and one on its prohibition. They asked me to clarify the truth in the matter, so I wrote a comprehensive book on it, titled: Shann al-Ghara 'ala man Abda Ma'arrata Taqawwulihi fi al-Hinna wa 'Awarruh. I named it thus to match its name to its meaning, for some of the pro-permissibility exceeded their bounds to claim ijtihad in it, claiming that those who forbid (i.e., all the companions, indeed al-Shafi'i as I clarified) then relaxed and did not ponder it.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological defense of the ranking of Hanafi jurists. The author refutes two errors: (1) downgrading Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas to a mere muqallid, and (2) placing Qadi Khan above al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani). 

First, the author argues that Abu Bakr al-Razi is a mujtahid, not a muqallid, citing his precedence in time, depth of knowledge, and the fact that later major Hanafi scholars (like Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, al-Sarakhsi, and al-Bazdawi, all considered mujtahids) rely heavily on his works. Al-Marjani's quote adds that those who degrade al-Razi are ignorant of his true stature; in fact, later scholars are dependent on him. Al-Halwani himself is quoted as saying they 'imitate him' (nuqalliduhu), implying al-Razi is a source of taqlid for others. The author further notes that al-Razi's fatwa on the secluded woman's agency (tawkil) was later generalized by later scholars, showing his pioneering role. The chain of Hanafi knowledge traces back to him through his students.

Second, the author defends al-Quduri and Sahib al-Hidayah against being ranked below Qadi Khan. Al-Marjani's quote argues that al-Quduri is older and more learned than Shams al-A'imma, so he cannot be lower than Qadi Khan. Sahib al-Hidayah was acknowledged as the foremost scholar of his time, with Qadi Khan himself testifying to his virtue. Therefore, placing Qadi Khan above them is unjustified. The passage concludes by criticizing the arbitrary ranking that lowers Abu Bakr al-Razi, al-Quduri, and Sahib al-Hidayah while elevating later figures.

The passage also includes a digression from Ibn Hajar al-Haytami on the ruling of men dyeing hands/feet with henna, which he deems forbidden (haram) due to imitation of women, citing a hadith. This is presented as an example of a fiqh dispute where he wrote a treatise against those who permit it.

Key Terms
مُجْتَهِد (mujtahid): A jurist qualified to derive legal rulings directly from the sources (Quran, Sunnah, etc.) through ijtihad.
مُقَلِّد (muqallid): A person who follows a mujtahid without independent derivation of rulings.
تَخْرِيج (takhrij): The process of deriving subsidiary rulings from the principles of the school's founders (like Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it wrong to count Abu Bakr al-Razi as a muqallid?
A) Because he was a companion of Abu Hanifa.
B) Because later mujtahids like al-Sarakhsi relied on his works, showing he was a source of ijtihad.
C) Because he only transmitted hadith, not fiqh.
D) Because he was a Shafi'i scholar.

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr al-Razi, al-Quduri, and Sahib al-Hidayah are foundational Hanafi authorities whose rank should not be lowered; later scholars are indebted to them.

Life of the Author
intermediate
8 min
The Proper Ranking of Hanafi Scholars: Defending al-Quduri and al-Marghinani
Critique of devaluing Quduri and Sahib al-Hidayah relative to Qadi Khan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the relative ranks of al-Quduri, al-Marghinani, and Qadi Khan in the Hanafi tabaqat and explain why ikhtilaf does not diminish a scholar's ijtihad status.

Core Idea
A scholar's rank depends on overall juristic mastery, not on isolated differences.

This lesson addresses a common misconception: that later scholars like Qadi Khan can be ranked above earlier foundational figures like al-Quduri and al-Marghinani. The passage defends the high rank of these early authorities, emphasizing that ikhtilaf (disagreement) among mujtahids is natural and does not lower their stature. By understanding the careful reasoning behind tabaqat, you will appreciate how Hanafi scholars evaluate authority and why the great texts remain central.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed claim
Who is being compared? What ranking is being contested? The author objects to lowering al-Quduri and al-Marghinani below Qadi Khan.
The claim is that Qadi Khan is in a third rank (higher) while al-Quduri and al-Marghinani are placed below.
2
Examine the evidence for higher rank
What arguments support the author's defense? Quoting al-Marjani: al-Quduri preceded Shams al-A'imma and is greater; al-Marghinani was acknowledged as peerless even by Qadi Khan and others.
Note that al-Marjani uses chronological precedence and contemporary accolades as evidence.
3
Understand the role of ikhtilaf
The passage lists three examples of differences between great mujtahids (takbirs, khuntha inheritance, ta'dil al-arkan). How do these examples support the defense? They show that ikhtilaf is common and does not harm rank.
The author stresses that such differences 'did not harm them in their ijtihad, nor did it lower their status.'
4
Apply the principle
How does this affect your use of Hanafi sources? Knowing the rank helps prioritize texts: when al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadi Khan conflict, the earlier authoritative text is preferred.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that the mufta bihi is often from the higher-ranked mujtahid.

The second study: Tabaqat al-Hanafiyyah (Layers of Hanafis). 4. Among them: Indeed the status of al-Quduri is greater than Qadi Khan and the author of al-Hidayah; if not greater, then not less. So placing Qadi Khan in a third rank and lowering al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah from it is not appropriate. And Ahmad ibn Hajar al-Makki al-Haytami al-Shafi'i mentioned in his treatise 'Shann al-Ghara...' quoting from 'Sharh al-Muhadhdhab' (about) the takbirs of the two 'Eids that they are thirteen takbirs, carrying that on this number by adding the original takbirs, while al-Shafi'i and his followers carry it on the extras. And Abu Yusuf derived the saying of al-Sha'bi that for the ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) from inheritance is half of the two shares, that being three out of seven, and Muhammad that it is five out of twelve. And Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi derived the saying of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad regarding the straightening of bowing and prostration and making it obligatory, while Abu 'Abdallah Jani derived it and carried it on the Sunnah. And many such examples occurred from great mujtahids, and that did not harm them in their ijtihad, nor did it lower their status; so how can Abu Bakr al-Razi be lowered to a rank below his station? Refer to 'Husn al-Taqadi' (pp. 89-91) and 'Tabaqat al-Hanafiyyah' by Ibn al-Junaydi (p. 40). (1) al-Marjani said in 'Nadhurat al-Haqq' (p. 63): 'He made al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah from among the people of tarjih (preference) and Qadi Khan from the mujtahids, while al-Quduri preceded Shams al-A'imma in time and is higher than him in stature and longer in reach – so how can he not be higher than Qadi Khan? As for the author of al-Hidayah, he is the one pointed to in his era, the one on whom fingers are counted in his time, the unique of his time and the peerless one. And it is mentioned in al-Jawahir (2:627) etc. that the scholars of his time acknowledged his virtue and precedence, like Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan and Imam Zayn al-Din al-'Attabi and others, and they said that he surpassed his peers, even his teachers, in fiqh and they acknowledged that to him. So how can his rank be lowered below Qadi Khan by degrees? Rather, he is more deserving of ijtihad and more established in its means and more attached to its doors.' Refer to 'Husn al-Taqadi' (pp. 91-92). (2) He died in Mecca in the year 975; from him (the author), may Allah have mercy on him. (3) Ibn Hajar al-Haytami said regarding the reason for composing this book in 'al-Kaba'ir' (1:405-406): 'It is known from the report of the effeminate man dyed with henna whom the Prophet exiled because of his imitation of women by dyeing his hands and feet, that dyeing a man's hands or feet with henna is haram, indeed a major sin due to what is mentioned of imitating women, and that the mentioned hadith is explicit in that. And this issue occurred recently near Yemen, and its scholars differed regarding it and authored works on permissibility and prohibition. Then they sent to me in Mecca in the year 952 AH three works, two on its absolute permissibility and one on its prohibition, and they asked me to clarify the truth in the matter. So I authored a comprehensive book on it, naming it 'Shann al-Ghara 'ala man azhara ma'irrata taqawwulihi fi al-hinna' wa 'iwaruhu'. I named it so that its name matches its subject, for some of those who said it is permissible overstepped their bounds to the point of claiming ijtihad in it, and they claimed that those who said it is prohibited—meaning all the companions, indeed even al-Shafi'i as I clarified—were mistaken and did not reflect.'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is from a supercommentary (hashiya) on Sharh al-Wiqaya, discussing the classification of Hanafi scholars and defending the high rank of al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) and the author of al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), against an unnamed opinion that placed Qadi Khan (d. 592 AH) above them. The author argues that al-Quduri is at least equal to or greater than Qadi Khan, and al-Marghinani is peerless. He supports this by quoting al-Marjani and citing recognition from contemporaries. The passage then gives examples of ikhtilaf (disagreement) among great mujtahids: (1) The number of takbirs in 'Eid prayer: Hanafis count 13 including the original takbirs of the prayer, while Shafi'is count only the extra ones. (2) The inheritance of a khuntha mushkil (ambiguous hermaphrodite): Abu Yusuf derived from al-Sha'bi that they get half of the two shares (i.e., 3/7 of the estate), while Muhammad said 5/12. (3) The ruling on ta'dil al-arkan (straightening in bowing and prostration): Abu Hanifa and Muhammad considered it wajib, while others considered it sunnah. These examples show that ikhtilaf does not diminish the status of mujtahids. The author then criticizes those who lower the rank of earlier scholars, stating that their ijtihad is valid and their differences do not harm their standing. The footnote (3) provides background on Ibn Hajar al-Haytami's work on the prohibition of men dyeing with henna, which he wrote to refute those who claimed permissibility based on faulty ijtihad.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, a leading Hanafi faqih (d. 428 AH), author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
قاضي خان (Qadi Khan): Fakhr al-Din al-Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi, a Hanafi jurist (d. 592 AH), author of the influential fatwa collection Fatawa Qadi Khan.
صاحب الهداية (Sahib al-Hidayah): Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), author of al-Hidayah, a central commentary of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and a major reference for Hanafi fatwa.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): The total exertion by a jurist to derive rulings from the primary sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas) using valid methods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the number of takbirs in 'Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Twelve takbirs total
B) Thirteen takbirs including the original takbirs of the prayer
C) Thirteen extra takbirs besides the original
D) Nine takbirs

Key Takeaway
A scholar's rank in Hanafi tabaqat is determined by juristic mastery and recognition from peers, not by the absence of ikhtilaf.

The Importance of Author Biography in Hanafi Textual Criticism
Discussion of authorship attribution of Khulasat al-Kaydani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four opinions on the authorship of Khulasat al-Kaydani and explain why the work's authority is limited unless it aligns with authoritative Hanafi books.

Core Idea
A book's fame does not guarantee its author's scholarly credibility.

The Khulasat al-Kaydani is a popular fiqh text in Central Asia, but its authorship is uncertain. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah lists four opinions and warns that the author's obscurity limits the text's independent authority. Understanding this teaches us how Hanafi scholars evaluate texts based on author biographies and cross-checking with reliable sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its fame
Recognize that Khulasat al-Kaydani is widely used in Transoxiana for memorization and study, but its author is unknown.
2
List the four opinions on authorship
From the passage, note the four attributions: (1) Shams al-Din al-Fanari, (2) Ibn Kamal Pasha, (3) Lutf Allah al-Nasafi (al-Fadil al-Kaydani), (4) Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi.
The fourth is considered the weakest.
3
Evaluate the strength of each opinion
Assess why the fourth is weak (shows ignorance of Hanafi biographers) and why the third is most widespread but still problematic (author is obscure).
The first two have known authors with other works.
4
Understand the conclusion
The commentator states that if the third opinion is true, the author is unknown, and such a work is not relied upon unless it agrees with reliable books (al-kutub al-mu'tabara).
5
Apply the principle
In your study, when encountering a Hanafi text of uncertain authorship, compare its rulings with authoritative works like al-Quduri or al-Hidayah before relying on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا: «خُلاصَةُ الْكَيْدَانِي» الْمَنْسُوبَةِ إِلَى لُطْفِ اللهِ النَّسَفِي، فَإِنَّهَا وَإِنِ اشْتَهَرَتْ فِي بِلَادِ مَا وَرَاءَ النَّهْرِ اشْتِهَاراً، وَتَدَاوَلُوهَا فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمْ حِفْظاً وَاسْتِذْكَاراً إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُعْرَفْ إِلَى الْآنَ حَالُ مُؤَلِّفِهَا أَنَّهُ مَنْ هُوَ ؟ وَكَيْفَ هُوَ ؟ وَهَلْ هُوَ مِمَّنْ يَسْتَنَدُ بِتَصْنِيفِهِ مِمَّنْ يُضْرَبُ بِهِ الْمَثَلُ الْمَشْهُورُ : إِنَّ مَنْ لَا يَعْرِفُ الْفِقْهَ صَنَّفَ فِيهِ كِتَاباً ؟ وَقَدِ اخْتَلَفَ فِي تَعْيِينِ مُؤَلِّفِهَا عَلَى أَقْوَالٍ ثَلَاثَةٍ أَوْرَدَهَا صَاحِبُ «كَشْفِ الظُّنُونِ» : الْأَوَّلُ : إِنَّهَا لِشَمْسِ الدِّينِ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ حَمْزَةَ الْفَنَارِي، الْمُتَوَفَّى سَنَةَ أَرْبَعٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ وَثَمَانِمِئَةٍ، وَهُوَ جَدُّ حَسَنٍ جَلَبِي، مُحَشِّي «الْمُطَوَّلِ»، وَ«التَّلْوِيحِ»، وَغَيْرِهِ. الثَّانِي : إِنَّهَا لِابْنِ كَمَالْ بَاشَا الرُّومِي، مُؤَلِّفِ «الْإِيضَاحِ وَالْإِصْلَاحِ». الثَّالِثُ : إِنَّهَا لِلْفَاضِلِ لُطْفِ اللهِ النَّسَفِي الْمَشْهُورِ بِالْفَاضِلِ الْكَيْدَانِي. وَهَا هُنَا قَوْلٌ رَابِعٌ ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُ مُعَاصِرِي عَلِيِّ الْقَارِي الْمَكِّي، وَهُوَ أَنَّهَا لِأَبِي الْبَرَكَاتِ النَّسَفِي، حَافِظِ الدِّينِ عُمَرَ مُؤَلِّفِ «الْوَافِي»، وَهَذَا الْقَوْلُ أَضْعَفُ الْأَقْوَالِ، يَشْهَدُ بِعَدَمِ مَعْرِفَةِ قَائِلِهِ أَحْوَالَ الْفُقَهَاءِ. وَأَمَّا الْأَقْوَالُ الثَّلَاثَةُ فَعَلَى الْقَوْلِ الثَّالِثِ مِنْهَا الَّذِي هُوَ الْمَشْهُورُ بَيْنَ الْجُمْهُورِ، يَكُونُ مُؤَلِّفُهَا رَجُلاً مَجْهُولاً، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ نَقِفْ فِي كَلَامِ أَحَدٍ مِمَّنْ أَلَّفَ فِي تَرَاجِمِ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ لِلُطْفِ اللهِ النَّسَفِي خَبَراً وَلَا أَثَراً، وَالْمَجْهُولُ يَكُونُ تَأْلِيفُهُ مِمَّا لَا يُعْتَمَدُ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُوَافِقَ الْكُتُبَ الْمُعْتَبَرَةَ.
Among them: 'Khulasat al-Kaydani', attributed to Lutf Allah al-Nasafi. Although it is widely famous in Transoxiana, and they exchanged it among themselves for memorization and recall, yet the condition of its author is not known to this day: who he is? And what is he like? And is he among those whose authorship is relied upon, or among those of whom the famous proverb is said: 'He who does not know fiqh authored a book in it'? There are three opinions regarding the identification of its author, which the author of 'Kashf al-Zunun' listed: First: that it is by Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Fanari, who died in 834 AH, and he is the grandfather of Hasan Jalabi, the commentator on 'al-Mutawwal' and 'al-Talwih' and others. Second: that it is by Ibn Kamal Pasha al-Rumi, author of 'al-Idah wa al-Islah'. Third: that it is by the virtuous Lutf Allah al-Nasafi, known as al-Fadil al-Kaydani. There is also a fourth opinion mentioned by some contemporaries of 'Ali al-Qari al-Makki, which is that it is by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, Hafiz al-Din 'Umar, author of 'al-Wafi'. And this opinion is the weakest of the opinions, as it shows the speaker's lack of knowledge of the conditions of the jurists. As for the three opinions, according to the third of them, which is well-known among the majority, its author is an unknown man, for we have not found in the speech of anyone who wrote about the biographies of Hanafis any news or trace of Lutf Allah al-Nasafi, and an unknown person's composition is not to be relied upon unless it agrees with reliable books.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a biographical discussion about the authorship of a famous fiqh text, 'Khulasat al-Kaydani'. The author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah (the commentator) is addressing a common work used in many madrasas and noting that its author is uncertain. He lists four opinions collected from various sources. The first opinion attributes it to Shams al-Din al-Fanari, the second to Ibn Kamal Pasha, the third to Lutf Allah al-Nasafi (al-Fadil al-Kaydani), and a fourth (very weak) to Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi. The commentator deems the third opinion the most widespread but notes that Lutf Allah al-Nasafi is an obscure figure; no biographer of Hanafi scholars mentions him. Consequently, the work's authority is limited unless it aligns with widely accepted reliable books (al-kutub al-mu'tabara). This serves as a caution: a work's widespread use does not guarantee its author's credibility. It also illustrates the importance of author biography (tarajim) in the Hanafi tradition for evaluating fiqh texts.

Key Terms
خُلاصَةُ الْكَيْدَانِي (Khulasat al-Kaydani): A well-known Hanafi fiqh text, the authorship of which is disputed among several scholars.
الْكُتُبَ الْمُعْتَبَرَةَ (al-kutub al-mu'tabara): Reliable and authoritative books in the Hanafi school, such as the works of the Mutun (e.g., al-Quduri, al-Kanz) and the Zahir al-Riwaya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the most widespread opinion about the author of 'Khulasat al-Kaydani'?
A) It is by Shams al-Din al-Fanari.
B) It is by Ibn Kamal Pasha.
C) It is by Lutf Allah al-Nasafi (al-Fadil al-Kaydani).
D) It is by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi.

Key Takeaway
The authority of a fiqh text depends on the reliability of its author; an unknown author requires comparison with authoritative works.

Classification of Hanafi Scholars: Mutaqaddimun and Muta'akhkhirun
Classification of Hanafi scholars with definitions and critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three different definitions for the boundary between early and later Hanafi scholars and identify an example of terminological inconsistency.

Core Idea
The Hanafi scholarly timeline is not fixed; multiple boundaries exist and usage varies.

Understanding who is considered an early (mutaqaddim) versus later (muta'akhkhir) Hanafi scholar is essential for weighing opinions in fiqh. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents several competing definitions and points out a real inconsistency in how the term 'muta'akhkhirun' is applied. We will explore these classifications and their significance for Hanafi methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions given
The passage gives at least three definitions: one from 'al-Khayalat al-Latifa', one from al-Dhahabi, and an implicit critique from the commentator. List each definition's criteria.
Focus on the chronological cutoffs: Abu Hanifa to Muhammad, Muhammad to al-Halwani, and the year 300 AH.
2
Pinpoint the inconsistency
The commentator notes that in al-Hidayah, the term 'muta'akhkhirun' is applied to scholars like al-Jurjani who lived before al-Halwani. Why is this problematic?
Al-Jurjani died c. 398 AH, while al-Halwani died c. 452 AH. If the boundary is al-Halwani, then al-Jurjani should be counted among the mutaqaddimun or khalaf, not muta'akhkhirun.
3
Understand the practical implication
Explain why this classification matters: the authority of a ruling depends on whether the scholar is from the early period (more authoritative) or later period.
Later scholars' opinions are generally considered less binding if they contradict the early imams.
4
Analyze the commentary style
Notice how the commentator uses a cross-reference (al-Hidayah and al-'Inayah) to challenge a previous claim. This is a typical expansion-probe technique.
The commentator is not just reporting but critically evaluating the earlier classification.
5
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Suppose you read in a later Hanafi fatwa collection a ruling attributed to 'some muta'akhkhirun'. How would you determine which scholars are included?
You would need to check the author's own definition or look at the scholars cited in the work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر عبد النبي الأحمد نكري في جامع العلوم نقلاً عن صاحب «الخيالات اللطيفة»: «إنَّ الخلف عند الفقهاء من محمد بن الحسن إلى شمس الأئمة الحَلْوَانِي، والسلف من أبي حنيفة إلى محمد، والمتأخرون من الحلواني إلى حافظ الدين البخاري). انتهى. وذكر الذهبي في مفتح كتابه ميزان الاعتدال في نقد أسماء الرجال»: «إنّ الحد الفاصل بين المتقدمين والمتأخرين هو رأس ثلاثمئة»(4). ويخدش ما ذكره عبد النبي أنهم كثيراً ما يطلقون المتأخرين على من قبل الحَلْوَاني؛ فقد قال في «الهداية» في «كتاب الصوم» في «بحث قضاء المجنون الصوم» : «هذا مختار بعض المتأخرين». انتهى (٥) . قال في «العناية»: «منهم أبو عبد الله الجُرْجَاني، والإمام الرستغْفنِي، والزاهد الصفار (۱) ). انتهى مع أن الجرجاني متقدم على الحَلْوانِي، فإنّ الحَلْوانِي من رجال المئة الخامسة، مات سنة اثنتين وخمسين أو تسع وأربعين أو ثمان وأربعين بعد أربعمئة على ما يأتي ذكره. وأبو عبد الله محمد بن يحيى الجُرْجَاني مات سنة ثمان أو سبع وتسعين وثلاثمئة. كما ذكره الكفوي ، وغيره
And 'Abd al-Nabi al-Ahmadi al-Nakri mentioned in 'Jami' al-'Ulum' quoting from the author of 'al-Khayalat al-Latifa': 'Verily, the successors (khalaf) among the jurists are from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and the predecessors (salaf) are from Abu Hanifa to Muhammad, and the later ones (muta'akhkhirun) are from al-Halwani to Hafiz al-Din al-Bukhari.' End. And al-Dhahabi mentioned in the introduction to his book 'Mizan al-I'tidal': 'The boundary between the early and later scholars is the year 300.' End. And what 'Abd al-Nabi mentioned is problematic because they often apply 'muta'akhkhirun' to those before al-Halwani; for it was said in 'al-Hidayah' in the book of Fasting, in the section on making up fasts for the insane: 'This is the choice of some later scholars.' End. And in 'al-'Inayah': 'Among them are Abu 'Abd Allah al-Jurjani, Imam al-Rustughfani, and al-Zahid al-Saffar.' End, despite the fact that al-Jurjani is earlier than al-Halwani, for al-Halwani is from the fifth century, dying in the year 452 or 449 or 448 after four hundred as will come. And Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Jurjani died in the year 398 or 397, as mentioned by al-Kafawi and others.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage discusses the classification of Hanafi scholars into early (mutaqaddimun) and later (muta'akhkhirun) categories. Multiple definitions are presented. According to one view, the early scholars (salaf) run from Abu Hanifa to Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani), the successors (khalaf) from Imam Muhammad to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) from al-Halwani to Hafiz al-Din al-Bukhari. Al-Dhahabi places the dividing line at the year 300 AH. However, the author notes an inconsistency: in al-Hidayah, the term 'muta'akhkhirun' is applied to scholars like al-Jurjani, who died before al-Halwani. This shows that the terminology is not uniformly applied. The student must be aware of these classifications to properly evaluate the authority of rulings in different Hanafi books.

Key Terms
المتقدمون (al-mutaqaddimūn): Early Hanafi scholars; various definitions exist, but commonly those up to Imam Muhammad or up to al-Halwani.
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirūn): Later Hanafi scholars; the cutoff point is debated, but they are generally those after the early period.
السلف (al-salaf): In this context, the earliest Hanafi scholars from Abu Hanifa to Imam Muhammad.
الخلف (al-khalaf): The successors after Imam Muhammad up to al-Halwani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Dhahabi, what is the boundary between early and later scholars?
A) The death of Abu Hanifa
B) The year 300 AH
C) The time of al-Halwani
D) The death of Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
The classification of Hanafi scholars into early and later is not uniform; different authorities use different cutoffs, and the same text may use 'muta'akhkhirun' inconsistently.

A Cross-Madhhab Authority: Ibn Hajar al-Haytami
Biographical note on a revered Shafi'i scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key works of Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and explain why a Shafi'i scholar's writings are studied in Hanafi circles.

Core Idea
A Shafi'i giant whose works irrigate all madhahib — including the Hanafi.

This lesson introduces you to a celebrated Shafi'i jurist whose works transcend his own school. Although the passage is brief, it reveals why later scholars across madhahib, especially Hanafis, still rely on his writings. Understanding his stature helps you appreciate the shared scholarly heritage and the importance of cross-referencing authoritative sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Read the first phrase: 'He is Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Ali bin Hajar al-Haytami…' Note the attributions: al-Sa'di, al-Makki, and the nisbah to the locality of Abi al-Haytam. What do these tell you about his origin and travels?
His lineage indicates connections to Egypt and Makkah.
2
Extract the praise and its significance
The quote from al-Aidarusi calls him 'khatimat ahl al-fatya' (the last of the people of fatwa). Why is such a lofty title given? Consider that he lived in the 10th century AH, a period of mature scholarship. This title implies he was the final great jurisconsult of his era.
This rank is not taken lightly in Hanafi tradition; fatwa requires immense knowledge.
3
List his major works mentioned
Three works are cited: 'Tuhfat al-Muhtaj', 'al-Jawhar al-Munazzam', and 'al-Khayrat al-Hisan'. In one sentence each, note the topic of each work. Which one is a commentary? Which deals with visiting the Prophet's grave? Which is about Abu Hanifa?
His writing on Abu Hanifa (al-Nu'man) directly connects to Hanafis.
4
Connect to Hanafi fiqh
Although Ibn Hajar was Shafi'i, his 'Tuhfat al-Muhtaj' is a major reference for fiqh rulings, and his fatwas are cited in later Hanafi works. Why would Hanafi scholars use a Shafi'i commentary? Because in later centuries, jurists from all schools consult comprehensive works for their rigor and detail.
Hanafi scholars such as Ibn Abidin occasionally reference Ibn Hajar's fatwas.
5
Evaluate his legacy
The passage ends with references to other biographical sources ('al-Nur al-Safir', 'al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyyah'). This suggests his biography is well-documented. As a student, you should know that Hanafi scholarship does not exist in isolation; it engages with the broader Sunni tradition.
Respecting scholars of other madhahib is part of the Hanafi adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) وهو أحمد بن محمد بن علي بن حَجَر الهَيْتَمِي السَّعْدِي المَكي، أبو العباس، شهاب الدين ، نسبة إلى محلة أبي الهيتم من إقليم مصر الغربية، قال العيدروسي : الشيخ الإمام خاتمة أهل الفتيا والتدريس، كان بحرا في علم الفقه وتحقيقه لا تكدره الدلاء من مؤلفاته : «تحفة المحتاج شرح المنهاج»، و«الجوهر المنظم في زيارة قبر النبي المكرم»، و«الخيرات الحسان في مناقب النعمان»، (۹۰۹ - ٩٧٤هـ ) . ينظر : «النور السافر» (ص ٢٥٨ - ٢٦٣). التعليقات السنية» (ص٤١١ - ٤١٢).
(2) He is Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Ali bin Hajar al-Haytami al-Sa'di al-Makki, Abu al-Abbas, Shihab al-Din, attributed to the locality of Abi al-Haytam in the western region of Egypt. Al-Aidarusi said: 'The leading Imam, the last of the people of fatwa and teaching, he was a sea in the science of fiqh and its verification, its buckets cannot muddy him.' Among his works: 'Tuhfat al-Muhtaj bi-Sharh al-Minhaj', 'al-Jawhar al-Munazzam fi Ziyarat Qabr al-Nabi al-Mukarram', 'al-Khayrat al-Hisan fi Manaqib al-Nu'man' (909-974 AH). Look at: 'al-Nur al-Safir' (pp. 258-263), 'al-Ta'liqat al-Saniyyah' (pp. 411-412).
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for the renowned Shafi'i scholar Ibn Hajar al-Haytami (909-974 AH). Although he was a Shafi'i, his works are widely used in Hanafi circles, especially his commentaries and fatwas. He studied in Cairo and Makkah and became a leading authority in fiqh. His most famous work is 'Tuhfat al-Muhtaj', a commentary on al-Nawawi's 'Minhaj al-Talibin', which is a standard Shafi'i reference. He also wrote 'al-Jawhar al-Munazzam' on visiting the Prophet's grave, and 'al-Khayrat al-Hisan' on the virtues of Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage highlights his position as a 'sea of fiqh' and his prolific output. Despite being from the later period (mutakhkhirin), his works remain authoritative.

Key Terms
الفتيا (al-fatya): Giving legal verdicts; Ibn Hajar is called the 'khatimat ahl al-fatya' (last of the great jurisconsults).
الخيرات الحسان في مناقب النعمان (al-Khayrat al-Hisan fi Manaqib al-Nu'man): A work by Ibn Hajar on the virtues of Imam Abu Hanifa (al-Nu'man).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following statements best summarizes Ibn Hajar al-Haytami's relationship with Hanafi fiqh?
A) He was a Hanafi scholar who wrote on Shafi'i fiqh.
B) He was a Shafi'i scholar whose works are occasionally cited by Hanafi authorities due to their thoroughness.
C) He rejected all non-Shafi'i positions and did not interact with Hanafi thought.
D) He converted to the Hanafi school later in life.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, though a Shafi'i, is a universally respected authority whose works, especially his biography of Abu Hanifa, make him relevant to Hanafi students.

Biography of Sadr al-Shari'ah and His Lineage
Biographical account of Sadr al-Shari'ah's lineage and scholarly credentials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the lineage and scholarly chain of Sadr al-Shari'ah and explain their significance in establishing his authority within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Sadr al-Shari'ah's authority rests on a noble lineage tracing to a Companion and an unbroken chain of great Hanafi masters.

This passage recounts the lineage and scholarly credentials of Sadr al-Shari'ah, the esteemed commentator of al-Wiqaya. Understanding a scholar's chain (sanad) is crucial in the Hanafi tradition for establishing the authority of his transmission. This lesson will help you navigate such biographical accounts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main figures and their titles
Note the titles 'Sadr al-Shari'ah', 'Taj al-Shari'ah', 'Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar', and 'Jamal al-Din'. These distinguish multiple generations of scholars in the same family.
Titles often repeat across generations; pay attention to modifiers like 'al-Akbar' (the Elder).
2
Trace the lineage back to the Companion
Follow the chain of names from Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud back to Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari. Note the key names that appear in both citations.
The lineage is given twice, once from al-Dimyati and once from al-Kafawi, with slight differences.
3
Identify the scholarly chain (sanad)
From al-Kafawi's account, extract the sequence of teachers from Sadr al-Shari'ah up to al-Halwani: his grandfather → Imamzadah → al-Zaranjari → his father → al-Sarakhsi → al-Halwani.
This chain shows direct transmission from earlier Hanafi authorities.
4
Understand the significance of each link
Recognize that each person in the chain is a recognized Hanafi master. For example, al-Sarakhsi is the author of al-Mabsut, a foundational text.
The chain establishes the reliability and continuity of the transmitted knowledge.
5
Appreciate the breadth of Sadr al-Shari'ah's learning
Al-Kafawi lists his expertise in many disciplines (fiqh, usul, kalam, tafsir, hadith, Arabic, logic). This shows he was not only a jurist but a polymath, which enhances his authority as a commentator.
This breadth is typical of top-tier Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدراسة السادسة
في ذكر تراجم: مصنف «الوقاية) وصدر الشريعة شارح «الوقاية» وآبائهما وأجدادهما مع ذكر نسبهما ونسبتهما
قال عبد المولى الدمياطي في «تعاليق الأنوار على الدر المختار»: «رأيتُ في مسلسلات شيخنا السيد مرتضى الحسيني ذكر نسب صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة الأكبر أحمد بن جمال الدين أبي المكارم عبيد الله بن إبراهيم بن أحمد بن عبد الملك بن عمير بن عبد العزيز بن محمد بن جعفر بن خلف بن هارون بن محمد بن محمد بن محبوب بن الوليد بن عبادة بن الصامت الصحابي الأنصاري المحبوبي. قال شيخنا: كذا رأيتُ نسبه في تاريخ بخارا»، وهو أخذ عن جده محمود عن والده أحمد عن والده جمال الدين عبيد الله بن إبراهيم المحبوبي، وأحمد هذا هو صاحب «الفروق» المسمّى بـ «التلقيح». انتهى كلام الدمياطي.
وقال الكفوي الرومي في كتاب «أعلام الأخيار في طبقات فقهاء مذهب النعمان المختار»: «الإمامُ العلامة صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة الأكبر أحمد بن جمال الدين المحبوبي، صاحب «شرح الوقاية»، المعروف بين الطلبة بصدر الشريعة. وهو الإمام المتفق عليه، والعلامة المختلف إليه، حافظ قوانين الشريعة، ملخص مشكلات الفرع والأصل، شيخ الفروع والأصول، عالم المعقول والمنقول، فقيه أصولي خلافي جدلي، محدث مفسر، نحوي لغوي أديب، نظار متكلم منطقي، عظيم القدر جليل المحل، كثير العلم يضرب به المثل، غذي بالعلم والأدب، وارث المجد عن أب فأب، نشأ في حجر الفضل، ونال العلى وحمل على أكتاف الفقهاء، كفل به ورباه جده في صباه، فسَعِدَ جده وأنجح جده، حتى صار محرزاً قصب السبق في الفروع والأصول. أخذ العلم عن جده تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة أحمد بن عبيد الله المحبوبي عن أبيه جمال الدين المحبوبي عن الشيخ الإمام المفتي إمام زَادَه عن عماد الدين بن شمس الأئمة الزَّرَنْجَري عن أبيه شمس الأئمة بكر بن محمد بن علي عن السرخسي عن الحلواني».
The Sixth Study
On Mentioning the Biographies of: The Author of 'al-Wiqaya' and Sadr al-Shari'ah, the Commentator of 'al-Wiqaya', and their Fathers and Grandfathers, with Mention of Their Lineage and Attribution.
Abd al-Mawla al-Dimyati said in his 'Ta'aliq al-Anwar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar': 'I saw in the Musalsalat of our shaykh al-Sayyid Murtada al-Husayni the mention of the lineage of Sadr al-Shari'ah: Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din Abi al-Makarim Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Malik ibn Umayr ibn Abd al-Aziz ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far ibn Khalaf ibn Harun ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahbub ibn al-Walid ibn Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari al-Mahbubi. He said: Our shaykh said: Thus I saw his lineage in the History of Bukhara', and he took (knowledge) from his grandfather Mahmud from his father Ahmad from his father Jamal al-Din Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim al-Mahbubi, and this Ahmad is the author of 'al-Furuq' named 'al-Talqih'.' End of the words of al-Dimyati.
And al-Kafawi al-Rumi said in his book 'A'lam al-Akhyar fi Tabaqat Fuqaha' Madhhab al-Nu'man al-Mukhtar': 'The Imam, the all-knowing Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi, the author of 'Sharh al-Wiqaya', known among the students as Sadr al-Shari'ah. And he is the universally agreed-upon Imam, the all-sign to whom people turn, the preserver of the laws of the Shari'ah, the summarizer of the difficult issues of the branches and the fundamentals, the shaykh of branches and fundamentals, the knower of the rational and transmitted, a jurist, a legal theorist, disputationist, dialectician, hadith scholar, exegete, grammarian, linguist, man of letters, a speculator, theologian, logician, great in stature, lofty in station, abundant in knowledge such that proverbs are made about him, nurtured on knowledge and literature, inheritor of glory from father to father, raised in the lap of virtue, attained eminence and was carried on the shoulders of the jurists, his grandfather took charge of him and raised him in his childhood, so his grandfather succeeded and he made his grandfather successful, until he became the one who obtained the prize in branches and the fundamentals. He took knowledge from his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi from his father Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi from al-Shaykh al-Imam al-Mufti Imamzadah from Imad al-Din ibn Shams al-A'immah al-Zaranjari from his father Shams al-A'immah Bakr ibn Muhammad ibn Ali from al-Sarakhsi from al-Halwani.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This is a biographical passage providing the lineage and scholarly credentials of Sadr al-Shari'ah, the commentator of al-Wiqaya. The author of 'Umda al-Ri'aya' begins by citing two authorities: first, Abd al-Mawla al-Dimyati, who reports from his teacher Murtada al-Husayni the complete lineage tracing back to the Companion Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari. This lineage passes through several notable Hanafi scholars, including Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi and Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar. The second citation from al-Kafawi al-Rumi praises Sadr al-Shari'ah's mastery across numerous disciplines—fiqh, usul, kalam, tafsir, hadith, Arabic, and logic—and enumerates his scholarly chain from his grandfather down through the great Hanafi transmitters: Imamzadah, al-Zaranjari, his father, al-Sarakhsi, and al-Halwani. This establishes both the nobility of his bloodline and the authority of his transmission, a key concern in traditional Hanafi scholarship.

Key Terms
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): Title meaning 'Chief of the Shari'ah', referring to the author of Sharh al-Wiqaya, Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud al-Mahbubi.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): Title meaning 'Crown of the Shari'ah', referring to Sadr al-Shari'ah's grandfather, Mahmud ibn Ahmad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Ali ibn Abi Talib
D) Abd Allah ibn Umar

Key Takeaway
Sadr al-Shari'ah's lineage and scholarly chain are central to his authority as a Hanafi commentator.

Scholarly Lineage of Sadr al-Shari'ah
Biographical account with scholarly chain and works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the chain of teachers from Sadr al-Shari'ah back to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and identify the major works of Sadr al-Shari'ah.

Core Idea
Sadr al-Shari'ah's scholarly chain traces directly to Abu Hanifa through Imam Muhammad — a key link in Hanafi transmission.

This passage introduces the towering Hanafi scholar Sadr al-Shari'ah (Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi), author of the famous commentary on Al-Wiqayah. It details his unparalleled expertise across Islamic sciences and, crucially, his scholarly lineage (silsila) that connects him to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and through him to Abu Hanifa. Understanding this chain is essential for appreciating the authority of his works in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and the person
The passage begins with 'Sadr al-Shari'ah' – identify this as the commentator, Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi (d. 747 AH). Note the praise that follows.
Sadr al-Shari'ah means 'the foremost in Shari'ah'.
2
Trace the teacher-student chain
Read the lineage from Taj al-Shari'ah (grandfather) back through several scholars to Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and then to Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf? Actually the chain ends with 'from Muhammad, from Abu…' but we can note it goes to Muhammad al-Shaybani.
The chain: Sadr al-Shari'ah → Taj al-Shari'ah → Jamal al-Din → Imam Zadah → Imad al-Din → Shams al-A'imma al-Zaranjari → Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi → Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani → Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi → Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl → al-Sabdamuni → Abu Abd Allah ibn Abi Hafs al-Kabir → his father → Muhammad → Abu (Hanifa?). The final link is abbreviated.
3
List the major works of Sadr al-Shari'ah
The passage mentions his commentary on Al-Wiqayah (this volume), an abridgment Al-Niqayah, a usul text Al-Tanqih and its commentary Al-Tawdih, plus other treatises.
Al-Wiqayah is by his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah.
4
Note the death and burial
He died after 740 AH (specifically 747 AH according to other sources) and is buried in Bukhara. His grandfathers died and were buried in Kirman.
The death year is given as 'seven hundred and forty-something' in the text.
5
Identify a prominent student
The passage mentions Hafiz al-Haqq wa al-Din Abu Tahir al-Tahiri, who received an ijaza from Sadr al-Shari'ah in 745 AH. Also the author of 'Fasl al-Khitab' studied under him.
This shows the continued transmission of Hanafi fiqh.

بين الطلبة بصدر الشريعة). وهو الإمام المتفق عليه، والعلامة المختلف إليه، حافظ قوانين الشريعة، ملخص مشكلات الفرع والأصل، شيخ الفروع والأصول، عالم المعقول والمنقول، فقيه أصولي خلافي جدلي، محدث مفسر ، نحوي لغوي أديب، نظار متكلم منطقي، عظيم القدر جليل المحل، كثير العلم يضرب به المثل، غذي بالعلم والأدب، وارث المجد عن أب فأب، نشأ في حجر الفضل، ونال العلى وحمل على أكتاف الفقهاء، كفل به ورباه جده في صباه ، فسَعِدَ جده وأنجح جده ، حتى صار محرزاً قصب السبق في الفروع والأصول. أخذ العلم عن جده تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة أحمد بن عبيد الله المحبوبي عن أبيه جمال الدين المحبوبي عن الشيخ الإمام المفتي إمام زَادَه عن عماد الدين عن أبيه شمس الأئمة الزَّرَنْجَري عن شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي، عن شمس الأئمة الحَلْوَانِي، عن القاضي أبي علي النَّسَفِي، عن أبي بكر محمـد بـن الفـضـل ، عـن السلموني، عن أبي عبد الله بن أبي حفص الكبير ، عن أبيه عن محمد عن أبي وكان ذا عناية بتقييد نفائس جده وجمع فوائده ، شرح كتاب «الوقاية» مــن تصانيف جده تاج الشريعة وهو أحسن شروحه ، واختصر «الوقاية» وسماه «النقاية»، وألف في الأصول متناً لطيفاً سماه «التنقيح»، ثمّ صنف شرحاً نفيساً سمّاه «التوضيح»، وله «المقدمات الأربعة» و«تعديل العلوم»، و«الشروط»، و«المحاضر»، مات سنة وأربعين وسبعمئة ومرقده ومرقدُ والديه وأولاده وأجداد والديه كلهم في شرع آبار بخارا. وأما جده أبو أبيه تاج الشريعة، وأبو والدته برهان الدين، فإنهما ماتا في كرمان ودفنا فيه. كذا ذكره عبد الباقي - الخطيب بالمدينة المنورة - الذي يرفع نسبه إلى قاضي خان. وتفقه عليه حافظ الحق والدين أبو طاهر محمّد بن محمّد بـن الحـسـن بـن علـي الطاهري، ووقع للشيخ أبي طاهر الإجازة من صدر الشريعة في بخارا سنة خمس وأربعين وسبعمئة. وأخذ الفقه عنه صاحب فصل الخطاب» محمد بن محمد البخاري الشهير
(Popular among students as Sadr al-Shari'ah). He is the unanimously accepted Imam, the distinguished scholar referred to, the preserver of the laws of Shari'ah, the summarizer of the problematic issues of subsidiary and foundational matters, the teacher of subsidiary and foundational matters, the learned in rational and transmitted sciences, a jurist, legal theorist, disputations scholar, dialectician, hadith scholar, exegete, grammarian, linguist, literary man, thinker, theologian, logician, of great stature, lofty station, abundant knowledge, an exemplar, nurtured by knowledge and literature, inheritor of glory from father to father, raised in the lap of virtue, attained eminence, and carried on the shoulders of jurists. His grandfather took care of him and raised him in his childhood, so his grandfather was fortunate and his fortune succeeded, until he became the foremost in subsidiary and foundational matters. He acquired knowledge from his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi, from his father Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi, from the Shaykh, the Imam, the Mufti Imam Zadah, from Imad al-Din, from his father Shams al-A'imma al-Zaranjari, from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, from al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi, from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, from al-Sabdamuni, from Abu Abd Allah ibn Abi Hafs al-Kabir, from his father, from Muhammad, from Abu... He was diligent in recording the gems of his grandfather and collecting his benefits. He explained the book 'Al-Wiqayah' from the works of his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah, and it is the best of its commentaries. He abridged 'Al-Wiqayah' and named it 'Al-Niqayah'. He authored a text in Usul named 'Al-Tanqih', then wrote a precious commentary called 'Al-Tawdih'. He also wrote 'Al-Muqaddimat al-Arba'', 'Ta'dil al-Ulum', 'Al-Shurut', and 'Al-Muhadir'. He died in the year seven hundred and forty-something, and his grave, the graves of his parents, his children, and his grandparents are all in the street of the wells of Bukhara. As for his paternal grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah and his maternal grandfather Burhan al-Din, they both died in Kirman and were buried there. This was mentioned by Abd al-Baqi, the khatib in Medina, who traces his lineage to Qadi Khan. He (Sadr al-Shari'ah) taught fiqh to Hafiz al-Haqq wa al-Din Abu Tahir Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Tahiri, and Abu Tahir received an ijaza from Sadr al-Shari'ah in Bukhara in the year 745. The author of 'Fasl al-Khitab', Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bukhari, known as... also studied fiqh under him.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry (tarjama) for the author of Al-Wiqayah and its commentator, Sadr al-Shari'ah. It begins by praising him in superlative terms, highlighting his expertise in all branches of Islamic learning. It then details his scholarly lineage, tracing his chain of teachers back to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the direct student of Abu Hanifa. The passage mentions his key works: he wrote a commentary on his grandfather's book Al-Wiqayah (which is being commented upon in this volume), an abridgment called Al-Niqayah, a text on usul called Al-Tanqih, and its commentary Al-Tawdih, among other treatises. His death date is given as after 740 AH, and his burial place is in Bukhara. The passage also notes that he granted an ijaza to Abu Tahir al-Tahiri in 745 AH, and that his grandfathers died in Kirman.

Key Terms
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): Title of the commentator (the subject of this biography), meaning 'the foremost in Shari'ah'.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): Title of the grandfather of the commentator, meaning 'the crown of Shari'ah'.
الوقاية (Al-Wiqayah): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text composed by Taj al-Shari'ah, on which the commentator wrote a commentary.
النقاية (Al-Niqayah): An abridgment of Al-Wiqayah by Sadr al-Shari'ah.
التنقيح (Al-Tanqih): A text in usul al-fiqh authored by Sadr al-Shari'ah.

Scholarly Lineage and Works of the Authors of al-Wiqayah
Biographical overview of the scholarly chain and works of al-Wiqayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the scholarly chain of transmission from the author of al-Wiqayah back to Imam Abu Hanifa and identify the major works authored by Taj al-Shari'ah and his grandfather.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fiqh manual al-Wiqayah is rooted in a direct chain of scholarship from Abu Hanifa.

This passage introduces the scholars behind al-Wiqayah and its commentary. Understanding their scholarly lineage (isnad) reinforces the authority of these works. We meet Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, author of al-Wiqayah, and his grandfather Sadr al-Shari'ah, and see how their writings shaped the Hanafi curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the chain of transmission
The passage begins with a chain from the author's father al-Zaranjari back to Abu Hanifa. List the names and note how this establishes authority.
2
Recognize the author of al-Wiqayah
The passage clarifies that Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud wrote al-Wiqayah for his grandson. Do not confuse him with Sadr al-Shari'ah.
3
List the works of Taj al-Shari'ah
Besides al-Wiqayah, he wrote a commentary on it, an abridgment (al-Niqayah), usul works (al-Tanqih, al-Tawdih), and others.
4
Note the biographical details of Sadr al-Shari'ah
He is described as a great scholar, father of Taj al-Shari'ah, and author of Sharh al-Hidayah and other works.
5
Understand the geographical and lineage references
Burial places, teachers, and students mentioned provide context for the scholarly network.

الدراسة السادسة ترجمة مؤلف الوقاية وشارحها
أبيه شمس الأئمة الزَّرَنْجَري عن شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي، عن شمس الأئمة الحَلْوَانِي، عن القاضي أبي علي النَّسَفِي، عن أبي بكر محمـد بـن الفـضـل ، عـن السلموني، عن أبي عبد الله بن أبي حفص الكبير ، عن أبيه عن محمد عن أبي حنيفة.
