The sixth study: biography of the author of al-Wiqayah and its commentator. His father Shams al-A'imma al-Zaranjari from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, from al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi, from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, from al-Sabzmuni, from Abu Abd Allah ibn Abi Hafs al-Kabir, from his father, from Muhammad, from Abu Hanifa. And he was careful to record the precious works of his grandfather and collect his benefits. He wrote a commentary on the book 'al-Wiqayah' from the works of his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah, and it is the best of its commentaries. He abridged 'al-Wiqayah' and called it 'al-Niqayah'. He authored a concise text in usul called 'al-Tanqih', then wrote a precious commentary called 'al-Tawdih'. He also wrote 'al-Muqaddimat al-Arba', 'Ta'dil al-'Ulum', 'al-Shurut', and 'al-Mahadir'. He died in the year forty and seven hundred [i.e., 740s?], and his grave, his parents', his children's, and his paternal and maternal grandparents' all are in the town of Abar of Bukhara. Seven. As for his paternal grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah and his maternal grandfather Burhan al-Din, they both died in Kirman and were buried there. Thus mentioned 'Abd al-Baqi, the khatib in Medina, who traces his lineage to Qadi Khan. And studied with him Hifz al-Haqq wa al-Din Abu Tahir Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Tahiri. And Shaykh Abu Tahir received an ijazah from Sadr al-Shari'ah in Bukhara in the year five and forty and seven hundred [745?]. And studied jurisprudence with him the author of 'Fasl al-Khitab' Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Bukhari, known as Khwajah Parsa, and he received an ijazah from him in the year six and seventy and seven hundred [776?] in Bukhara. The author of 'al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyyah' mentioned it in his discussion of Ilyas ibn Yahya al-Rumi. End of al-Kafawi's words. And al-Kafawi also said in the thirteenth booklet: 'The Imam Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad ibn 'Ubayd Allah Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi. He studied jurisprudence with his father Sadr al-Shari'ah Shams al-Din Ahmad, a learned virtuous scholar, a perfect writer, an overflowing sea, an excellent ink, outstanding, pious, scrupulous, a verifier and exact scholar, possessor of magnificent works, among them: the book 'al-Wiqayah' which he selected from 'al-Hidayah', 'al-Fatawa', and 'al-Waqi'at', and he wrote it for his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Mahmud. He also wrote 'Sharh al-Hidayah', an accepted commentary among the virtuous, handled by the hands of scholars. End. And he also said in the twelfth booklet: 'The Imam Sadr al-Shari'ah Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din 'Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad al-Mahbubi, he acquired knowledge from his father Jamal al-Din from Shaykh Imam Zadah Rukn al-Islam Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Wa'iz, author of 'Shir'at al-Islam'. He was among the great scholars, and reached in his father's lifetime a complete level of juristic ability, and had ability in usul. His son Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud studied with him. He authored the book 'Talqih al-'Uqul fi al-Furuq'. Mentioned by Ibn Qutlubugha. End.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the scholarly lineage behind the Hanafi fiqh manual 'al-Wiqayah' and its commentary. It begins by presenting the chain of transmission (isnad) of fiqh knowledge from the author's father up to Imam Abu Hanifa, establishing the authority of the work. The chain includes prominent Hanafi scholars like Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, al-Halwani, and al-Nasafi. The subject of the biography is described as meticulous in preserving his grandfather's works, writing a commentary on 'al-Wiqayah' (which his grandfather authored), and producing several other important texts: an abridgment ('al-Niqayah'), a usul text with its commentary ('al-Tanqih' and 'al-Tawdih'), and other treatises on Islamic sciences. His death is placed in the 740s AH, and his burial site is noted in Bukhara. The passage then provides additional biographical details from the works of al-Kafawi, clarifying that the author of 'al-Wiqayah' is Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad. Taj al-Shari'ah wrote 'al-Wiqayah' by extracting from 'al-Hidayah' and other fatwa collections, and he composed it for his grandson. The biography also covers Taj al-Shari'ah's own teachers, including his father, and mentions his commentary on 'al-Hidayah'. Furthermore, it gives a sketch of Sadr al-Shari'ah Shams al-Din Ahmad, the father of Taj al-Shari'ah, noting his education and his own scholarly lineage. This passage is found in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a super-commentary on the Sharh al-Wiqayah, and it provides the necessary scholarly context for understanding the authority of the texts being studied.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A famous Hanafi fiqh manual compiled by Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, extracted from al-Hidayah and other sources.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A major Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, on which al-Wiqayah is based.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): A title meaning 'Crown of the Sharia', used for the Hanafi scholar Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah, author of al-Wiqayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud

Key Takeaway
The scholarly chain and biographical details confirm that al-Wiqayah is a reliable Hanafi text rooted in a direct transmission from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Life of the Author

Biography of the Author of Al-Wiqayah and Its Commentator
Biographical account of two Hanafi scholars and their lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the names and lineages of Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud and Sadr al-Shari'a 'Ubayd Allah, and explain the nisbas al-Mahbubi and al-'Ubadi.

Core Idea
The authority of Al-Wiqayah is rooted in a scholarly lineage tracing back to the Companion 'Ubada ibn al-Samit.

This passage compiles biographical accounts of two pivotal Hanafi scholars: Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud, who authored the foundational text Al-Wiqayah, and his father/relative Sadr al-Shari'a 'Ubayd Allah, who wrote a commentary on Al-Hidayah. Understanding their lineage and nisbas is essential for appreciating the authority and transmission of these works within the Hanafi madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures
Locate the names and roles of the two primary scholars: Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud (author of Al-Wiqayah) and Sadr al-Shari'a 'Ubayd Allah (commentator). Note their full names and familial relationship.
The text refers to both as part of the al-Mahbubi family.
2
Trace the lineage to the Companion
The text asserts descent from the Companion 'Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari. This is indicated by the nisba al-'Ubadi. Use the genealogy provided by Ibn al-Athir to understand the full lineage.
This connection establishes scholarly prestige and chain of knowledge.
3
Understand the nisba al-Mahbubi
Al-Mahbubi is a nisba referring to an ancestor named Mahbub. It is used for Taj al-Shari'a and his forefathers in Hanafi works like 'Furuq al-Mahbubi' and 'Sharh al-Hidayah'.
Distinguish it from al-'Ubadi: the latter is broader, while al-Mahbubi is a family nisba.
4
Recognize the importance of Al-Wiqayah
Al-Wiqayah is an abridgment selected from Al-Hidayah, Al-Fatawa, and Al-Waqi'at. Its authorship by a member of this scholarly family adds to its authority as a foundational Hanafi matn.
The commentary on Al-Wiqayah is also by a descendant, reinforcing the chain.

عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية
بخواجه بارسا، ووقع له الإجازة منه سنة ست وسبعين في بخارا. ذكره صاحب «الشقائق النعمانية» في ذكر إلياس بن يحيى الرومي. انتهى كلام الكفوي. وقال الكفوي أيضاً في «الكتيبة الثالثة عشر»: «الشيخ الإمام تاج الشريعة محمود ابن صدر الشريعة أحمد بن عبيد الله جمال الدين المحبوبي. أخذ الفقه عن أبيه صدر الشريعة شمس الدين أحمد، عالم فاضل، تحرير كامل، بحر زاخر، وحبر فاخر بارع ورع متورع، محقق مدقق، صاحب التصانيف الجليلة، منها: كتاب «الوقاية» التي انتخبها من «الهداية»، و«الفتاوى»، و«الواقعات»، وصنفها لابن ابنه صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود بن محمود، وله: «شرح الهداية»، وهو شرح مقبول بين الفضلاء تداولته أيدي العلماء. انتهى.
وقال أيضاً في «الكتيبة الثانية عشر»: «الشيخ الإمام صدر الشريعة شمس الدين أحمد بن جمال الدين عبيد الله بن إبراهيم بن أحمد المحبوبي، أخذ العلم عن أبيه جمال الدين عن الشيخ إمام زاده ركن الإسلام محمد بن أبي بكر الواعظ، صاحب شرعة الإسلام، وكان من كبار العلماء، وبلغ في حياة أبيه في الفقاهة مبلغاً كاملاً، وله قدرة في الأصول، وتفقه عليه ابنه تاج الشريعة محمود، وله كتاب «تلقيح العقول في الفروق». ذكره ابن قُطلُوبُغا. انتهى.

الدراسة السادسة: ترجمة مؤلف الوقاية وشارحها
وفي كتاب «العبر بأخبار من غبر» لشيخ الإسلام أبي عبد الله شمس الدين محمد بن أحمد الذهبي في وقائع سنة ثلاثين وستمئة: «توفي عبيد الله بن إبراهيم جمال الدين المحبوبي البخاري، شيخ الحنفية بما وراء النهر، وأحد من انتهت إليه معرفة المذهب، أخذ عن أبي العلاء عمر بن بكر بن محمد الزرنجري عن أبيه شمس الأئمة، وتفقه أيضاً على قاضي خان الأوزجندي، توفي ببخارا في جمادى الأولى عن أربع وثمانين سنة». انتهى.
قلت: استفيدت من هذه العبارات أمور:
الأول: إن الشارح والمصنف من أولاد سيدنا عبادة بن الصامت الأنصاري؛ ولذا يقال له العبادي، وهو على ما ذكره ابن الأثير الجزري في «جامع الأصول»: «عبادة - بضم العين - ابن الصامت - بكسر الميم - ابن أصرم – بفتح الهمزة وسكون الصاد المهملة - ابن فهر بن ثعلبة بن غنم - بالفتح - ابن سالم بن عوف بن عمير بن عوف بن الخزرج الأنصاري الخزرجي، كان نقيباً شهد العقبة الأولى، وشهد بدراً والمشاهد كلها ثم وجهه عمر إلى الشام قاضياً ومعلماً، فأقام بحمص، ثم انتقل إلى فلسطين، ومات بها في الرملة في بيت المقدس سنة أربع وثلاثين، وقيل: إنه أقام إلى زمان معاوية.
الثاني: إن المحبوبي الذي يطلق على تاج الشريعة وآبائه - كما ترى الحنفية يقولون: في «فروق» المحبوبي كذا، وقال تاج الشريعة المحبوبي في «شرح الهداية» كذا، ونحو ذلك نسبة إلى محبوب، أحد أجدادهم.
الثالث: إن لقب شارح «الوقاية» عبيد الله، ولقب والد جده من قبل الأب، وهو
The commentary on Al-Wiqayah. By Khwaja Parsa, and he received authorization from him in the year 876 in Bukhara. Mentioned by the author of 'Al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya' in the entry of Ilyas ibn Yahya al-Rumi. End of al-Kafawi's words. And al-Kafawi also said in 'Al-Kutayba al-Thalitha 'Ashar': 'The Imam, Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'a Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi. He studied fiqh from his father Sadr al-Shari'a Shams al-Din Ahmad, a learned virtuous man, complete in writing, a vast ocean, an excellent ink, skillful, pious, cautious, a verifier, a scrutinizer, author of noble works, including: the book 'Al-Wiqayah' which he selected from 'Al-Hidayah', 'Al-Fatawa', 'Al-Waqi'at', and authored it for his grandson Sadr al-Shari'a Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Mahmud, and he also wrote 'Sharh al-Hidayah', which is a commentary accepted among the learned and circulated by scholars. End.' And he also said in 'Al-Kutayba al-Thaniya 'Ashar': 'The Imam Sadr al-Shari'a Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim ibn Ahmad al-Mahbubi, he acquired knowledge from his father Jamal al-Din from the Shaykh Imam Zada Rukn al-Islam Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr al-Wa'iz, author of 'Shar'at al-Islam', and he was among the great scholars, and he reached a complete level of jurisprudence during his father's lifetime, and he had ability in principles, and his son Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud studied under him, and he wrote the book 'Talqih al-Uqul fi al-Furuq'. Mentioned by Ibn Qutlubugha. End.' Footnotes: ... (full translation of footnotes omitted for brevity). Sixth Study: Biography of the author of Al-Wiqayah and its commentator. And in the book 'Al-'Ibar bi Akhbar man Ghabar' by Shaykh al-Islam Abu Abdullah Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Dhahabi, under the events of the year 630: 'Ubayd Allah ibn Ibrahim Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi al-Bukhari, the leading Hanafi scholar of Transoxiana, and one of those who had ultimate knowledge of the madhhab, studied under Abu al-'Ala' Umar ibn Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zarnajari from his father Shams al-A'imma, and also studied fiqh under Qadi Khan al-Uzjandi, died in Bukhara in Jumada al-Ula at the age of eighty-four.' End. I say: I derive from these statements several matters: First: That the commentator and the author are descendants of our master 'Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari; hence they are called al-'Ubadi, and as per what Ibn al-Athir al-Jazari mentioned in 'Jami' al-Usul': 'Ubada - with damm on 'ayn - ibn al-Samit - with kasr on mim - ibn Asram - with fatha on hamza and sukun on sad - ibn Fahr ibn Tha'laba ibn Ghanm - with fatha - ibn Salim ibn 'Awf ibn 'Umayr ibn 'Awf ibn al-Khazraj al-Ansari al-Khazraji, he was a naqib, attended the First 'Aqaba, and witnessed Badr and all the battles, then 'Umar sent him to Syria as a judge and teacher, he stayed in Hims, then moved to Palestine, and died in al-Ramla in Bayt al-Maqdis in the year 34, and it is said he lived until the time of Mu'awiya. Second: That the term al-Mahbubi, which is applied to Taj al-Shari'a and his forefathers, as you see the Hanafis say: 'In the Furuq of al-Mahbubi such and such', and 'Taj al-Shari'a al-Mahbubi said in Sharh al-Hidayah such and such', and so on, is a nisba to Mahbub, one of their ancestors. Third: That the title of the commentator of 'Al-Wiqayah' is 'Ubayd Allah, and the title of his paternal grandfather is... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction (tarjama) about the author of the Hanafi text Al-Wiqayah and its commentator, taken from the larger commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya. The text compiles quotes from several biographical works to establish the lineage and scholarly credentials of two key figures: Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud, the author of Al-Wiqayah (an abridgment of Al-Hidayah), and his father or grandfather figure Sadr al-Shari'a 'Ubayd Allah, who wrote a commentary on Al-Hidayah. The author follows the order of the sources: first quoting al-Kafawi's biographical dictionary, then al-Dhahabi's historical work, and finally summarizing three key insights. First, both the author and commentator are descendants of the Companion 'Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari, hence they are called al-'Ubadi. Second, the nisba 'al-Mahbubi' refers to an ancestor named Mahbub. Third, the commentator's name is 'Ubayd Allah. The passage emphasizes the scholarly lineage and the transmission of Hanafi knowledge within this family, tying them directly to a prominent Companion of the Prophet. This kind of biographical preface is standard in classical Hanafi works to establish the authority and reliability of the author.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A Hanafi fiqh work by Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud, selected from Al-Hidayah, Al-Fatawa, and Al-Waqi'at.
المحبوبي (al-Mahbubi): A nisba referring to the ancestor Mahbub, used for Taj al-Shari'a and his family.
العبادي (al-'Ubadi): A nisba indicating descent from the Companion 'Ubada ibn al-Samit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The author and commentator of Al-Wiqayah are both descendants of the Companion 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, with the nisba al-'Ubadi, and the family nisba al-Mahbubi refers to an ancestor named Mahbub.

Biographies of Al-Wiqayah's Author and Commentator
Biographical study resolving identities and correcting errors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi scholars behind Al-Wiqayah and its commentary, distinguish between the two Sadr al-Shari'a and Taj al-Shari'a, and correct common historical errors in their lineage.

Core Idea
Knowing the authors of Hanafi texts clarifies authority; Al-Wiqayah's author and commentator are from one family.

This lesson introduces the key figures behind two essential Hanafi texts: Al-Wiqayah and its commentary. The passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya clarifies the names, titles, and lineage of the author (Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud) and the commentator (Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar 'Ubaydullah). It also corrects misunderstandings from later historians. Understanding these distinctions is important for navigating Hanafi textual references.

Guided Path
1
Examine the primary source
Read al-Dhahabi's entry on 'Ubaydullah al-Mahbubi to get the foundation of the biographical discussion.
Al-Dhahabi identifies him as a chief Hanafi scholar.
2
Extract the five key points
Identify the five conclusions the author draws: lineage from 'Ubada, nisba to Mahbub, the two Sadr al-Shari'a, shared name 'Ubaydullah, and Taj al-Shari'a as the grandfather and author.
These points resolve the identities.
3
Analyze conflicting reports
Review al-Azniqi's and 'Ali al-Qari's errors. Note how they confused names and omitted generations.
Recognizing errors prevents misattribution.
4
Reconstruct the correct lineage
Based on the passage, trace the family: Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud (author) → Mas'ud → 'Ubaydullah (commentator)? Actually, passage states commentator's paternal grandfather is Ahmad. But Taj al-Shari'a is the grandfather on father's side. The correct lineage needs careful parsing; for now, understand that the commentator's grandfather is Ahmad (Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar) and his other grandfather is Mahmud (Taj al-Shari'a) — likely through different lines.
The passage emphasizes that Taj al-Shari'a is the grandfather of the commentator on his father's side.

(٤) الثاني : إن المحبوبي الذي يطلق على تاج الشريعة وآبائه - كما ترى الحنفية يقولون: في «فروق» المحبوبي كذا ، وقال تاجُ الشريعة المحبوبي في «شرح الهداية» كذا ، ونحو ذلك نسبة إلى محبوب، أحد أجدادهم. الثالث : إن لقب شارح «الوقاية» عبيد الله ، ولقب والد جده من قبل الأب، وهو (۱) وهـو محمد بن أحمـد بـن عثمان بن قايماز بن عبد الله التركماني الأصل الفاروقي الدِّمَشْقِي - الذهبي الشَّافِعِي، من مؤلفاته: «سير أعلام النبلاء»، و«العبر»، «تاريخ الإسلام»، (٦٧٣ - ٧٤٨هـ). ينظر : «الدرر الكامنة (٣: ٣٣٦ - ٣٣٨) ، وفوات الوفيات (٣: ٣١٥ - ٣١٦)، و«طبقات الأسنوي»(۱ : ۲۸۲ – ۲۷۳). (۲) من العبر بأخبار من غبر (٥ : ١٢٠). (۳) هو أبو السعادات، مبارك بن أبي الكرم محمد بن محمد الجزري، نسبة إلى جزيرة ابن عمر ، مؤلف جامع الأصول»، و«النهاية في غريب الحديث»، وغيرهما، المتوفى سنة (٦٠٦). منه رحمه الله سبقت ترجمته. (٤) ينظر: تاريخ دمشق»(٢٦ : ١٩١).  ۱۰۲ عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية أحمد بن جمال الدين المحبوبي واحد وهو صدر الشريعة، والفرق أن شارح الوقاية يعرفُ بصدر الشريعة الأصغر، وصدر الشريعة الثاني، وأبو جده يعرف بصدر الشريعة الأكبر، وصدر الشريعة الأول. والرابع : إن علم شارح «الوقاية»، وعَلَم والد صدر الشريعة الأكبر واحد، وهو عبيد الله مصغراً. والخامس : إن تاج الشريعة لقب لجد شارح «الوقاية من قبل أبيه، واسمه محمود، وهو المؤلف للوقاية»، و«شرح الهداية»، وهو الأستاذ لشارح «الوقاية»، وقد وقعت في بيان نسب شارح «الوقاية» وجده تاج الشريعة من المؤرخين والمحسين كلمات مختلفة كما بسطناها مع ما لها وما عليها في «مقدمة السعاية»، وفي «الفوائد البهية في تراجم الحنفية (٢) : (۲) ١. منها : إنّ الأزنيقي ذكر في مدينة العـلـوم عند ذكر «التنقيح» و«التوضيح» وشروح «الهداية»: «إنّ تاج الشريعة هو محمود بن عبيد الله بن محمود المحبوبي، وإنّه المؤلف للـ«وقاية» ولـ«شرح الهداية» المسمّى بـ«نهاية الكفاية» ». فهذا كما ترى يخالف ما مر بوجهين : أحدهما : إنه جعل عبيد الله المحبوبي والد تاج الشريعة، وحذف صدر الشريعة الأكبر أحمد من البين. إبراهيم. وثانيهما : إنه سمّى والد عبيد الله بمحمود، مع أن ما سبق دلّ على أن اسمه ٢. ومنها : إنّ علياً القاري المكي ذكر في حرف الميم مـن كتابة «الأثمار الجنية في طبقات الحنفية»: «مسعود بن أحمد العلامة صدر الشريعة الجامع للفضائل الجميلة والشمائل الجليلة»(۳). فهذا كما ترى مشتمل على ما لا يخفى ؛ فإنَّ صدر الشريعة ليس لقباً لمسعود بن أحمد، بل لعبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة، ولوالد تاج الشريعة أحمد.
The sixth study: Biography of the author of Al-Wiqayah and its commentator. (1) 101. And in the book 'Al-Ibar bi Akhbar man Ghabar' by Shaykh al-Islam Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Dhahabi, under the events of the year 630 AH: 'Died Ubaydullah ibn Ibrahim Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi al-Bukhari, the chief of the Hanafis in Transoxiana, one of those who reached the utmost knowledge of the madhhab. He studied under Abu al-'Ala' Umar ibn Bakr ibn Muhammad al-Zarnajari from his father Shams al-A'imma, and also studied fiqh under Qadi Khan al-Uzjandi. He died in Bukhara in Jumada al-Ula at the age of eighty-four.' End. (2) I say: I have derived from these expressions several matters: First: That the commentator and the author are descendants of our master 'Ubada ibn al-Samit al-Ansari; hence they are called al-'Ubadi. And as Ibn al-Athir al-Jazari mentioned in 'Jami' al-Usul': ''Ubada - with damm on 'ayn - ibn al-Samit - with kasr on mim - ibn Asram - with fatha on hamza and sukun on the important sad - ibn Fihr ibn Tha'laba ibn Ghanm - with fatha - ibn Salim ibn 'Awf ibn 'Umayr ibn 'Awf ibn al-Khazraj al-Ansari al-Khazraji. He was a naqib, witnessed the first 'Aqaba, Badr, and all the battles. Then 'Umar sent him to Syria as a judge and teacher. He resided in Hims, then moved to Palestine, and died there in al-Ramla in Bayt al-Maqdis in the year 34 AH. It is said that he remained until the time of Mu'awiya.' (4) Second: That 'al-Mahbubi', which is applied to Taj al-Shari'a and his ancestors - as you see the Hanafis say: 'In 'Furuq' al-Mahbubi such and such', and 'Taj al-Shari'a al-Mahbubi said in 'Sharh al-Hidaya' such and such', and so on - is a nisba to Mahbub, one of their ancestors. Third: That the personal name of the commentator of 'Al-Wiqaya' is 'Ubaydullah, and the personal name of his paternal grandfather (1) is Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din al-Mahbubi, and he is Sadr al-Shari'a. The difference is that the commentator of 'Al-Wiqaya' is known as Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar and Sadr al-Shari'a al-Thani, while his paternal grandfather is known as Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar and Sadr al-Shari'a al-Awwal. Fourth: That the personal name of the commentator of 'Al-Wiqaya' and the personal name of the father of Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar are the same: 'Ubaydullah in the diminutive form. Fifth: That 'Taj al-Shari'a' is the title of the grandfather of the commentator of 'Al-Wiqaya' on his father's side, and his name is Mahmud. He is the author of 'Al-Wiqaya' and 'Sharh al-Hidaya', and he was the teacher of the commentator of 'Al-Wiqaya'. There have occurred in the statements of historians and genealogists various conflicting words regarding the lineage of the commentator of 'Al-Wiqaya' and his grandfather Taj al-Shari'a, as we have detailed with their pros and cons in 'Muqaddimat al-Si'aya' and in 'Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya'. (2) From them: 1. That al-Azniqi mentioned in 'Madinat al-'Ulum' when mentioning 'Al-Tanqih' and 'Al-Tawdih' and commentaries on 'Al-Hidaya': 'Taj al-Shari'a is Mahmud ibn 'Ubaydullah ibn Mahmud al-Mahbubi, and he is the author of 'Al-Wiqaya' and 'Sharh al-Hidaya' called 'Nihayat al-Kifaya'.' This, as you see, contradicts what was mentioned before in two ways: One: He made 'Ubaydullah al-Mahbubi the father of Taj al-Shari'a, and omitted Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar Ahmad from the lineage. The other: He named the father of 'Ubaydullah as Mahmud, whereas what preceded indicates that his name was Ibrahim. 2. And among them: 'Ali al-Qari al-Makki mentioned in the letter 'mim' of his book 'Al-Athmar al-Janiyya fi Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya': 'Mas'ud ibn Ahmad, the scholar Sadr al-Shari'a, the collector of beautiful virtues and excellent qualities.' This, as you see, contains what is not hidden; for Sadr al-Shari'a is not a title for Mas'ud ibn Ahmad, but rather for 'Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'a, and for the father of Taj al-Shari'a, Ahmad.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This is a biographical study by the author of 'Umda al-Ri'aya, clarifying the identities of the author of Al-Wiqayah (Taj al-Shari'a) and its commentator (Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar). The author begins by quoting al-Dhahabi's account of the death of 'Ubaydullah ibn Ibrahim al-Mahbubi, noting that he was a leading Hanafi scholar. From this, the author extracts five key points: (1) Both the commentator and the author descend from 'Ubada ibn al-Samit, hence the nisba 'al-'Ubadi'. (2) 'Al-Mahbubi' is a nisba to their ancestor Mahbub. (3) The commentator's personal name is 'Ubaydullah, and his grandfather's personal name is Ahmad; the grandfather is known as Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar, the commentator as Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar. (4) Both the commentator and the father of Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar share the name 'Ubaydullah (diminutive). (5) Taj al-Shari'a is the grandfather of the commentator, named Mahmud, who authored Al-Wiqayah and Sharh al-Hidaya. The author then notes conflicting reports from historians: al-Azniqi mistakenly claimed Taj al-Shari'a was Mahmud ibn 'Ubaydullah ibn Mahmud, omitting Ahmad, and named 'Ubaydullah's father as Mahmud instead of Ibrahim. 'Ali al-Qari mistakenly called Mas'ud ibn Ahmad 'Sadr al-Shari'a', whereas that title belongs to 'Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud and to Ahmad.

Key Terms
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'a): A title meaning 'Foremost of the Sacred Law,' applied to two Hanafi scholars: the grandfather (Ahmad) as al-Akbar and the grandson ('Ubaydullah) as al-Asghar.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'a): A title meaning 'Crown of the Sacred Law,' applied to Mahmud, the grandfather of the commentator and author of Al-Wiqayah.
المحبوبي (al-Mahbubi): A nisba (relational surname) referring to the descendants of Mahbub, an ancestor of the family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is the author of Al-Wiqayah?
A) 'Ubaydullah ibn Ibrahim
B) Mahmud (Taj al-Shari'a)
C) Ahmad (Sadr al-Shari'a al-Akbar)
D) 'Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud

Key Takeaway
Al-Wiqayah was authored by Taj al-Shari'a Mahmud, and its commentary by his grandson Sadr al-Shari'a al-Asghar 'Ubaydullah; subsequent historians have introduced errors that must be corrected.

Identifying the Author of al-Wiqāyah: A Scholarly Dispute
Biographical dispute over the identity of Tāj al-Sharī'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main opinions on the identity of Tāj al-Sharī'ah and trace the lineage of the Maḥbūbī family as described in the passage.

Core Idea
Two Hanafi scholars, Mahmūd and 'Umar, are both called Tāj al-Sharī'ah — which one authored al-Wiqāyah is disputed.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'āya tackles a puzzle in Hanafi literary history: Who is Tāj al-Sharī'ah? The answer determines whether the author of al-Wiqāyah is the same person who wrote a famous commentary on al-Hidāyah. By parsing the conflicting reports, you will learn how medieval scholars weighed evidence to settle authorship disputes.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three points of disagreement
The passage opens by listing three issues that scholars differed on. Identify each one explicitly.
These are numbered in the Arabic text (1. 2. 3.).
2
Identify the two main opinions
One opinion comes from al-Kafawī in his Ṭabaqāt, the other from al-Quhustānī in Jāmi' al-Rumūz. Note which scholar holds which view.
Al-Kafawī and al-Quhustānī are the key sources.
3
Examine the evidence for each
Al-Kafawī cites the preface of Mukhtaṣar al-Wiqāyah; al-Quhustānī cites the colophon of Sharḥ al-Hidāyah. Compare the strength of these proofs.
The colophon explicitly names 'Umar, while the preface uses a title without a personal name.
4
Trace the genealogical relationships
Determine who is the 'proper grandfather' (jadd ṣaḥīḥ) and who is the 'improper grandfather' (jadd fāsid) in each version.
These terms are defined in the key terms.

محمود كيف لا وقد صرّح به تلميذه وشارح كلامه في ديباجة «مختصر الوقاية» حيث قال: «وبعد فإنّ العبد المتوسل إلى الله بأقوى الذريعة عبيد الله صدر الشريعة بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة سعد جده يقول قد ألف جدي المحبوبي مؤلّف «تلقيح العقول في الفروق». وفي ترجمة تاج الشريعة. وفي ترجمة إلياس بن يحيى الرومي. وفي ترجمة حافظ الدين الطاهري محمد بن محمد. وفي ترجمة خواجه بارسا مؤلّف فصل الخطاب محمد بن محمد. يدل على أن تاج الشريعة جد شارح «الوقاية» من قبل الأب اسمه محمود بن صدر الشريعة الأكبر أحمد وأنه المؤلف لـ «شرح الهداية» و«الواقعات» و«الفتاوى» وأنه هو المؤلّف للوقاية ألفها لأجل ابن ابنه وتلميذه عبيد الله صدر الصحيح لشارح «الوقاية» يعني تاج الشريعة اسمه عمر بن صدر الشريعة أحمد ومؤلّف «الوقاية» جد فاسد للشارح وهو محمود بن صدر الشريعة أحمد ولقبه برهان الشريعة وهو الأستاذ لشارح «الوقاية» صدر الشريعة الأصغر وهذه العبارة التي نقلها من آخر كتاب الإيمان من شرح الهداية يؤيده ما ذكره القهستاني تأييداً عظيماً فإنها صريحة في أن اسم شارح «الهداية» عمر بن صدر الشريعة الأكبر.
Ahmad. Secondly: The father of Tāj al-Sharī'ah is not 'Ubayd Allāh, rather there is Ahmad between them. Thirdly: The father of 'Ubayd Allāh is not Mahmūd ibn Muhammad, rather it is Ibrāhīm ibn... And know that there is another difference here: they agreed that the knowledge of the author of al-Wiqāyah is Mahmūd, how could it not be, since his student and the commentator of his words stated clearly in the preface of Mukhtaṣar al-Wiqāyah: 'After [praise], this servant who seeks nearness to Allāh through the strongest means, 'Ubayd Allāh Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah ibn Mas'ūd ibn Tāj al-Sharī'ah Sa'd his grandfather, says: My grandfather and master, the rabbānī scholar, the sāmandānī worker, Burhān al-Sharī'ah wa al-Ḥaqq wa al-Dīn: Mahmūd ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah, may Allāh reward him on my behalf and on behalf of all Muslims with the best reward, for my memorization of the book 'Wiqāyat al-Riwāyah fī Masā'il al-Hidāyah'...' Etcetera. And they differed: 1. Whether he (the author of Wiqāyah) is a proper grandfather (jadd ṣaḥīḥ) of the commentator or an improper grandfather (jadd fāsid). 2. Whether the commentator of al-Hidāyah, Tāj al-Sharī'ah, is the author of al-Wiqāyah or someone else. 3. Whether the name of Tāj al-Sharī'ah is Mahmūd or someone else, while they agreed that the Maḥbūbī commentator of al-Hidāyah is Tāj al-Sharī'ah and no other, and that Tāj al-Sharī'ah is a title for the paternal grandfather of the commentator, not from the mother's side. So the statement of al-Kafawī in his Ṭabaqāt: In the biography of Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Aṣghar 'Ubayd Allāh ibn Mas'ūd. And in the biography of the grandfather Tāj al-Sharī'ah: 'Ubayd Allāh ibn Ibrāhīm Jamāl al-Dīn al-Maḥbūbī, died in 630 AH according to what was transmitted from 'Ibar al-Dhahabī, or 680 AH according to what is in Ṭabaqāt al-Ḥanafiyyah of 'Alī al-Qārī. And in the biography of Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Akbar: Shams al-Dīn Aḥmad ibn 'Ubayd Allāh al-Maḥbūbī, author of Talqīḥ al-'Uqūl fī al-Furūq. And in the biography of Tāj al-Sharī'ah. And in the biography of Ilyās ibn Yaḥyā al-Rūmī. And in the biography of Ḥāfiẓ al-Dīn al-Ṭāhirī Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad. And in the biography of Khwājah Pārsā, author of Faṣl al-Khiṭāb, Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad. It indicates that Tāj al-Sharī'ah, the paternal grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqāyah, his name is Mahmūd ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Akbar Aḥmad, and he is the author of Sharḥ al-Hidāyah, al-Wāqi'āt, and al-Fatāwā, and he is the author of al-Wiqāyah, which he wrote for his grandson and student 'Ubayd Allāh Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Aṣghar. And the statement of the author of Madīnat al-'Ulūm agrees with this: that the author of al-Wiqāyah is Tāj al-Sharī'ah Mahmūd, the proper grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqāyah and his teacher, and he is the commentator of al-Hidāyah. As for the statement of al-Quhustānī in Jāmi' al-Rumūz, it indicates that the proper grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqāyah, i.e., Tāj al-Sharī'ah, his name is 'Umar ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah Aḥmad, and the author of al-Wiqāyah is an improper grandfather of the commentator, and he is Mahmūd ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah Aḥmad, his title is Burhān al-Sharī'ah, and he is the teacher of the commentator of al-Wiqāyah, Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Aṣghar, the son of his daughter, and he authored it for him. This is supported by the statement of the author of Kashf al-Ẓunūn regarding the names of books and arts when mentioning the commentaries of al-Hidāyah: 'Among the commentaries is the commentary of Shaykh al-Imām Tāj al-Sharī'ah 'Umar ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Awwal al-Maḥbūbī al-Ḥanafī, and he named it Nihāyat al-Kifāyah fī Dirāyat al-Hidāyah; its opening: Naṣrun mina Llāhi wa fatḥun qarīb, He is the Praised... etc.' And at the end of the Book of Īmān: 'The perfection of the benefits of the Book of Īmān was completed by Abū 'Abd Allāh 'Umar ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah at the end of Sha'bān 673 AH.' This statement that he quoted from the end of the Book of Īmān from Sharḥ al-Hidāyah strongly supports what al-Quhustānī mentioned, for it is explicit that the name of the commentator of al-Hidāyah is 'Umar ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Akbar.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a biographical investigation into the identity of Tāj al-Sharī'ah, the author of al-Wiqāyah, and his relationship to the commentator of al-Wiqāyah, namely Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Aṣghar. The text begins by listing three points of disagreement among scholars: (1) whether the author of al-Wiqāyah is a proper or improper grandfather of the commentator; (2) whether Tāj al-Sharī'ah, the commentator of al-Hidāyah, is the same as the author of al-Wiqāyah; and (3) whether Tāj al-Sharī'ah's personal name is Mahmūd or another. It then presents two conflicting opinions. The first, supported by al-Kafawī in his Ṭabaqāt and the author of Madīnat al-'Ulūm, holds that Tāj al-Sharī'ah is Mahmūd ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Akbar Aḥmad, who is the author of al-Wiqāyah, Sharḥ al-Hidāyah, and other works, and that he is the proper paternal grandfather of the commentator. The second opinion, advocated by al-Quhustānī in Jāmi' al-Rumūz and supported by a quotation from Kashf al-Ẓunūn, identifies Tāj al-Sharī'ah as 'Umar ibn Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah al-Akbar Aḥmad, making him the proper grandfather, while the author of al-Wiqāyah is Mahmūd, titled Burhān al-Sharī'ah, who is an improper grandfather (maternal or through marriage) and the teacher of the commentator. The passage does not definitively resolve the dispute but carefully documents the evidence for each view, demonstrating the scholarly rigor in determining authorial lineages within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
تاج الشريعة (Tāj al-Sharī'ah): Title meaning 'Crown of the Law', used for a Hanafi scholar, either Mahmūd or 'Umar, depending on the opinion. In this passage, it is the title of the commentator of al-Hidāyah and the grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqāyah.
صدر الشريعة (Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah): Title meaning 'Chest (or Chief) of the Law', used for multiple scholars: al-Akbar (the elder) and al-Aṣghar (the younger). Here it refers to Shams al-Dīn Aḥmad (al-Akbar) and 'Ubayd Allāh (al-Aṣghar).
جد صحيح (jadd ṣaḥīḥ): Proper or true grandfather, i.e., the father's father, or a direct paternal ancestor.
جد فاسد (jadd fāsid): Improper grandfather, meaning a grandfather through the mother's line or by marriage, not a direct paternal ancestor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main point of disagreement regarding Tāj al-Sharī'ah?
A) Whether he is the author of al-Hidāyah or not
B) Whether his personal name is Mahmūd or 'Umar
C) Whether he lived in the 6th or 7th century AH
D) Whether he was a Hanafi or Shafi'i scholar

Key Takeaway
The identity of Tāj al-Sharī'ah is disputed: some say Mahmūd, others say 'Umar; the choice affects the authorship chain of al-Wiqāyah.

Life of the Author
intermediate
10 min
Resolving the Authorship of al-Wiqayah and Sharh al-Hidayah
Biographical investigation into the authorship of al-Wiqayah and its commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the authors of al-Wiqayah and Sharh al-Hidayah and identify the correct scholarly lineage using textual evidence.

Core Idea
Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar wrote Sharh al-Hidayah; his brother Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud wrote al-Wiqayah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah resolves a common confusion: who authored the two foundational Hanafi works, al-Wiqayah and Sharh al-Hidayah? By examining conflicting reports and manuscript evidence, the author establishes clear identities. Understanding this distinction is essential for properly citing these texts in fiqh study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting views
The text presents two views: one from Madinat al-'Ulum claiming Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud authored both works, and another from al-Quhistani distinguishing Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar as the sharh author and Mahmud (Burhan al-Shari'ah) as the Wiqayah author.
Note the different titles: Taj al-Shari'ah vs. Burhan al-Shari'ah.
2
Examine the evidence from Kashf al-Zunun
Kashf al-Zunun quotes a colophon from Sharh al-Hidayah that names the commentator as 'Umar ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, supporting al-Quhistani's view.
A colophon is a scribal note at the end of a manuscript; it is a strong primary source.
3
Confirm the consensus among historians
The passage notes that historians and later Hanafi commentators agree that Sharh al-Hidayah is by Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar and that al-Wiqayah is by Mahmud (Burhan al-Shari'ah).
The list includes well-known Hanafi authorities like al-'Ayni, Ibn al-Humam, and Ibn 'Abidin.
4
Conclude the genealogical relationship
Both scholars are sons of Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar. Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar is the true (biological) grandfather of the commentator (Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar), while Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud is a false grandfather (maternal grandfather or teacher).
Understanding this lineage clarifies textual transmission chains.

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah, which clarifies the identities of the authors of two major Hanafi works: al-Wiqayah and its commentary, as well as Sharh al-Hidayah. The passage addresses a confusion in scholarly circles about who exactly authored al-Wiqayah and who wrote Sharh al-Hidayah. The text begins by citing several biographies from 'Kata'ib A'lam al-Akhyar' and then presents two conflicting views. One view, from the author of 'Madinat al-'Ulum', holds that Taj al-Shari'ah (named Mahmud) is the author of both al-Wiqayah and Sharh al-Hidayah, and that he is the true grandfather of the commentator (Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar). The other view, from al-Quhistani in 'Jami' al-Rumuz', states that the true grandfather (Taj al-Shari'ah) is named 'Umar, and that Mahmud (known as Burhan al-Shari'ah) is a false grandfather and the actual author of al-Wiqayah. The passage then provides strong evidence from Kashf al-Zunun, which quotes the colophon of a manuscript of Sharh al-Hidayah showing that the commentator's name is 'Umar ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar. Additionally, it notes that historians and commentators unanimously agree that Sharh al-Hidayah is by Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar, and that the author of al-Wiqayah is Mahmud (Burhan al-Shari'ah). The passage concludes that Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar and Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud are two brothers, both sons of Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar. This resolution is critical for correctly attributing these foundational Hanafi texts and understanding the scholarly lineage.

Key Terms
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): A title meaning 'Crown of the Law'. In this passage, it refers to 'Umar ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, the commentator of al-Hidayah and the true grandfather of Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar.
برهان الشريعة (Burhan al-Shari'ah): A title meaning 'Proof of the Law'. In this passage, it refers to Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, the author of al-Wiqayah and the false grandfather of the commentator.
صدر الشريعة الأكبر (Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar): A title meaning 'Foremost of the Law, the Greater'. Refers to Ahmad ibn 'Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi, the father of both 'Umar and Mahmud.
صدر الشريعة الأصغر (Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar): A title meaning 'Foremost of the Law, the Lesser'. Refers to 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud al-Mahbubi, the commentator of al-Wiqayah and grandson of Taj al-Shari'ah.
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A famous Hanafi fiqh text authored by Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud al-Mahbubi, serving as a mukhtasar (summary) of al-Hidayah.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A seminal Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, which has many commentaries. Here, it refers to the work commented upon by Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar in his Sharh al-Hidayah.
شرح الهداية (Sharh al-Hidayah): The commentary on al-Hidayah written by Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar, also known as Nihayat al-Kifayah fi Dirayat al-Hidayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of al-Wiqayah according to the passage?
A) Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar
B) Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud
C) Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar
D) Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar

Key Takeaway
The author of al-Wiqayah is Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud, while Sharh al-Hidayah was written by his brother Taj al-Shari'ah 'Umar.

Identifying the Commentators of al-Wiqayah and Their Lineages
Biographical study on key commentators of al-Wiqaya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key commentators of al-Wiqayah mentioned in the source and explain the genealogical relationships between Taj al-Shari‘ah, Sadr al-Shari‘ah, and the author of al-Wiqayah.

Core Idea
Know the teacher and his lineage to trust the text.

This lesson delves into the biographical study (الدراسة السابعة) from 'Umdat al-Ri‘ayah, which introduces us to the prominent commentators of al-Wiqayah. Understanding who these scholars are and how they relate to one another is crucial for appreciating the chain of transmission and the authority of their works. We will first clarify the family tree of key figures and then meet two early commentators whose efforts helped solidify al-Wiqayah's place in Hanafi studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars and their titles
First, list the scholars mentioned: Taj al-Shari‘ah (‘Umar), Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Akbar, Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Asghar, Burhan al-Shari‘ah, and the author of al-Wiqayah (Mahmud). Note each one's title and role.
Titles like Taj al-Shari‘ah and Sadr al-Shari‘ah are used to distinguish multiple scholars in the same family.
2
Understand the genealogical corrections
The passage resolves a confusion: Taj al-Shari‘ah (‘Umar) is the true grandfather of Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Asghar, while Burhan al-Shari‘ah is a false grandfather. Both are brothers, sons of Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Akbar. Trace this tree.
This corrects earlier mistaken attributions about the lineage of al-Wiqayah's author.
3
Recognize the two commentators
The passage lists two commentators: ‘Ala’ al-Din al-Rumi (Qara Khwajah) and ‘Abd al-Latif ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz (Ibn Malik). For each, note their full name, the commentary they wrote, and any special circumstances (e.g., Ibn Malik's commentary was completed by his son).
These are early commentators; their works are part of the rich scholarly tradition around al-Wiqayah.
4
Appreciate the scholarly tradition
Reflect on why the author includes these biographies: to establish the reliability and authority of the commentaries, showing the continuous engagement of scholars with this foundational text.
This biographical detail strengthens the user's trust in the matn and its explanations.

وقد اتفق المؤرخون وشراح «الهداية» وغيرهم على أن «شرح الهداية» لتاج الشريعة، فثبت أن اسم تاج الشريعة عمر. وقد اتفقوا أيضاً على أنّ تاج الشريعة جد صحيح لصدر الشريعة الأصغر، وعلى أن صاحب «الوقاية» اسمه محمود، فثبت أنه غير شارح «الهداية» جد فاسد له، وكلاهما: يعني جد شارح «الوقاية الصحيح تاج الشريعة، والفاسد برهان الشريعة أخوان ابنان لصدر الشريعة الأكبر.

الدراسة السابعة
في تراجم طائفة من شراح «الوقاية»

قد مرّ أنّ «الوقاية» من المتون المعتبرة، وأن مؤلفه من الفقهاء الكملة؛ فلذلك عكف عليه العلماء تعليقاً وتدريساً، وكتبوا عليه حواشي وشروحاً، وقد بسطت في تراجمهم في «مقدمة السعاية» ونذكر هاهنا قدراً مختصراً منه مع زيادات:
١. فمنهم: علاء الدين الأسود الرومي، المشتهر بقره خواجه، واسمه علي بن عمر، وله شرح على «المغني»، فرغ منه سنة سبع وثمانين وسبعمئة، وله شرح حافل للوقاية في مجلدين، صنفه حين كان مدرساً بمدرسة أزنيق في عهد السلطان أورخان بن عثمان خان، المتوفى سنة ستين وسبعمئة، وكانت وفاته سنة ثمانمئة. كذا في «كشف الظنون»، و«أعلام الأخيار»، و«الشقائق النعمانية في علماء الدولة العثمانية».
٢. ومنهم: المولى عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز بن فرشتا، الشهير بابن ملك، عالماً فاضلاً، ماهراً في جميع العلوم، له شرح مجمع البحرين»، و«شرح مشارق سماه بـ«مبارق الأزهار»، و «شرح المنار»، و«رسالة في التصوف»، وألف شرحاً للوقاية لكن لم يتفق له تبييضه، فبيضه ابنه محمد وزاد عليه. كذا في «الضوء اللامع في أعيان القرن التاسع لشمس الدين السخاوي».
Historians and commentators of al-Hidayah and others have agreed that the commentary on al-Hidayah belongs to Taj al-Shari‘ah, thus it is established that the name of Taj al-Shari‘ah is ‘Umar. They also agreed that Taj al-Shari‘ah is the true grandfather of Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Asghar, and that the author of al-Wiqayah is named Mahmud, so it is established that he is not the commentator of al-Hidayah who is a false grandfather to him, and both — meaning the true grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqayah is Taj al-Shari‘ah, and the false one is Burhan al-Shari‘ah — are two brothers, sons of Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Akbar.

The Seventh Study
On the Biographies of a Group of Commentators of al-Wiqayah

It has previously been mentioned that al-Wiqayah is among the esteemed texts and that its author is among the perfect jurists; therefore, scholars devoted themselves to it in annotation and teaching, and wrote commentaries and glosses upon it. I have expanded on their biographies in the 'Introduction to al-Si‘ayah,' and here we mention a concise amount of it with additions:
1. Among them: ‘Ala’ al-Din al-Aswad al-Rumi, known as Qara Khwajah, whose name is ‘Ali ibn ‘Umar. He has a commentary on al-Mughni, which he completed in the year 787 AH, and he has a comprehensive commentary on al-Wiqayah in two volumes, which he authored while he was a teacher at the school of Iznik during the reign of Sultan Orhan ibn ‘Uthman Khan, who died in 760 AH. He himself died in 800 AH. Thus in 'Kashf al-Zunun,' 'A‘lam al-Akhyar,' and 'al-Shaqa’iq al-Nu‘maniyyah fi ‘Ulama’ al-Dawlah al-‘Uthmaniyyah.'
2. Among them: al-Mawla ‘Abd al-Latif ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz ibn Farishta, famous as Ibn Malik, a virtuous scholar, proficient in all sciences. He has a commentary on 'Majma‘ al-Bahrayn,' and a commentary on 'Mashariq' named 'Mabariq al-Azhar,' and a commentary on 'al-Manar,' and a treatise on Sufism. He composed a commentary on al-Wiqayah but did not manage to finalize it, so his son Muhammad finalized it and added to it. Thus in 'al-Daw’ al-Lami‘ fi A‘yan al-Qarn al-Tasi‘' by Shams al-Din al-Sakhawi.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a biographical study (الدراسة السابعة) from 'Umdat al-Ri‘ayah focusing on the commentators of al-Wiqayah. It begins on page 106 with a clarification of the scholarly consensus regarding the identity of Taj al-Shari‘ah and the author of al-Wiqayah. It establishes that Taj al-Shari‘ah is ‘Umar and that he is the true grandfather of Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Asghar, while the author of al-Wiqayah is Mahmud. It also notes that both the true grandfather (Taj al-Shari‘ah) and the false one (Burhan al-Shari‘ah) are brothers, sons of Sadr al-Shari‘ah al-Akbar. On page 107, the author lists two commentators: first, ‘Ala’ al-Din al-Aswad al-Rumi (Qara Khwajah), who wrote a comprehensive commentary on al-Wiqayah in two volumes; second, ‘Abd al-Latif ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz (Ibn Malik), whose commentary was completed by his son Muhammad. The passage cites several sources for these biographies, indicating the author's scholarly method.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A renowned Hanafi fiqh text (matn) authored by Mahmud, used as a standard reference.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari‘ah): A title of ‘Umar, the scholar who wrote a commentary on al-Hidayah.
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari‘ah): A title for a family of Hanafi scholars; al-Akbar is the elder, al-Asghar the younger.
برهان الشريعة (Burhan al-Shari‘ah): The false grandfather figure in the lineage discussion, brother of Taj al-Shari‘ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who completed the commentary on al-Wiqayah that was left unfinished by his father?
A) ‘Ala’ al-Din al-Rumi
B) Muhammad ibn ‘Abd al-Latif
C) Shams al-Din al-Sakhawi
D) Burhan al-Shari‘ah

Key Takeaway
Knowing the identities and relationships of scholars like Taj al-Shari‘ah, Sadr al-Shari‘ah, and the commentators of al-Wiqayah is essential for proper attribution and understanding of the Hanafi textual tradition.

The Commentators of Al-Wiqayah: Preserving Hanafi Fiqh
Biographical introduction to four Hanafi scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify four major commentators of Al-Wiqayah and describe their contributions to Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Commentaries on Al-Wiqayah are living chains of Hanafi teaching — each scholar added his own legacy to the matn.

Al-Wiqayah is a core Hanafi text, and its commentators are not just authors but transmitters of a living tradition. This lesson introduces four key figures who shaped the study of Hanafi fiqh through their commentaries, showing how a single matn can generate a rich scholarly heritage.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the status of Al-Wiqayah
Understand why Al-Wiqayah is a foundational text in the Hanafi school — a summary of Al-Hidayah that became a standard reference for teaching and commentary.
The passage describes it as 'among the esteemed texts' and its author as 'among the perfect jurists'.
2
Identify each commentator and his key work
For each of the four scholars, note their name, the title of their commentary on Al-Wiqayah, and any unique details about its composition (e.g., completed by a son, named 'Al-'Inayah').
Use the Arabic names and dates to anchor the historical context.
3
Trace the scholarly chains and geographical spread
Observe the locations (Iznik, Togat, Herat, Rum) and connections to other scholars (e.g., Musannifak studied under students of al-Taftazani). This shows the wide network of Hanafi learning.
Focus on how each commentary reflects the author's environment and education.
4
Understand the concept of tahqiq and completion
Note that Ibn Malik's commentary was 'whitewritten' (fair copied) and completed by his son Muhammad. This illustrates the collaborative nature of scholarship and the importance of editing (tahqiq).
This practice ensures the work reaches future generations.

الدراسة السابعة
في تراجم طائفة من شراح «الوقاية»
(۲)
قد مرّ أنّ «الوقاية» من المتون المعتبرة، وأن مؤلفه من الفقهاء الكملة؛ فلذلك عكف عليه العلماء تعليقاً وتدريساً، وكتبوا عليه حواشي وشروحاً، وقد بسطت في تراجمهم في «مقدمة السعاية» ونذكر هاهنا قدراً مختصراً منه مع زيادات: ١. فمنهم: علاء الدين الأسود الرومي، المشتهر بقره خواجه، واسمه علي بن عمر، وله شرح على «المغني»، فرغ منه سنة سبع وثمانين وسبعمئة، وله شرح حافل للوقاية (۳) في مجلدين، صنّفه حين كان مدرساً بمدرسه أزنيق في عهد السلطان أورخان بن عثمان خان، المتوفى سنة ستين وسبعمئة، وكانت وفاته سنة ثمانمئة. كذا في «كشف الظنون» (٤) و«أعلام الأخيار» و«الشقائق النعمانية في علماء الدولة العثمانية» (٥). ومنهم: المولى عبد اللطيف بن عبد العزيز بن فرشتا، الشهير بابن ملك، عالماً فاضلاً، ماهراً في جميع العلوم، له شرح مجمع البحرين، و«شرح مشارق» سماه بـ«مبارق الأزهار»، و«شرح المنار»، و«رسالة في التصوّف»، وألف شرحاً للوقاية لكن لم يتفق له تبييضه، فبيضه ابنه محمد وزاد عليه. كذا في «الضوء اللامع في أعيان القرن التاسع» لشمس الدين السخاوي، و«الشقائق»، و«أعلام الأخيار»، و«كشف الظنون».
ومنهم: السيد علي التومناتي الرومي، كان في موضع توقات من بلاد الروم، صاحب فضيلة في العلوم كلّها، ألف «شرح الوقاية» وسماه «العناية»، وشرحاً للـ«زيج»، مات في أواخر المئة الثامنة. كذا في «الشقائق».
ومنهم: علي الشهير بمصنفك بن مجد الدين محمد بن محمد بن مسعود بن محمود بن محمد بن الإمام فخر الدين البسطامي الهروي الرازي، ولد سنة ثلاث وثمانمئة، وسافر مع أخيه لتحصيل العلم سنة ثلاث وعشرين، وأخذ العلم عن جلال الدين يوسف، تلميذ السعد التفتازاني، وعبد العزيز بن أحمد الأبهري الشافعي، وفصيح الدين محمد بن محمد، وغيرهم، وبلغ رتبة الفضل والكمال، وألف من صغر سنه تأليفاً؛ ولذا اشتهر بمصنفك، والكاف في لغة العجم للتصغير. فألف «شرح مصباح النحو» و«شرح آداب البحث» و«شرح اللباب» و«شرح المطوّل» و«شرح شرح التفتازاني للمفتاح» و«حاشية التلويح» و«شرح القصيدة البردة» و«شرح قصيدة ابن سينا» و«شرح الوقاية» و«شرح الهداية» ألفهما بعد سنة تسع وثلاثين وثمانمئة، وهي سنة سفره إلى هراة. وارتحل سنة ثمان وأربعين إلى بلاد الروم، وألف هناك «شرح مصابيح السنة» و«شرح شرح السيد الجرجاني للمفتاح» و«حاشية شرح المطالع» وشرح قدر من «أصول فخر الإسلام» و«شرح الكشاف» و«أنوار الحدائق» و«حدائق الإيمان» و«تحفة السلاطين» هذه الثلاثة بالفارسية، و«التحفة المحمودية» بالفارسية في نصيحة السلاطين.
The Seventh Study: On the biographies of a group of commentators of Al-Wiqayah. It has already passed that Al-Wiqayah is among the esteemed texts, and its author is among the perfect jurists; therefore scholars devoted themselves to it in commentary and teaching, and wrote glosses and commentaries upon it. I have expanded on their biographies in 'Muqaddimah al-Si'ayah', and here I mention a brief portion from it with additions. 1. Among them: 'Ala' al-Din al-Aswad al-Rumi, known as Qarah Khwajah, his name is 'Ali ibn 'Umar. He has a commentary on 'Al-Mughni' which he completed in 787 AH, and he has a comprehensive commentary on Al-Wiqayah in two volumes, which he wrote when he was a teacher at his madrasah in Iznik during the reign of Sultan Orkhan ibn 'Uthman Khan (d. 760 AH). His death was in 800 AH. Thus in 'Kashf al-Zunun', 'A'lam al-Akhyar', and 'Al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyyah fi 'Ulama' al-Dawlah al-'Uthmaniyyah'. 2. Among them: al-Mawla 'Abd al-Latif ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Farishta, known as Ibn Malik, a virtuous scholar, skilled in all sciences. He has a commentary on 'Majma' al-Bahrayn', and 'Sharh al-Mashariq' which he named 'Mabariq al-Azhar', and 'Sharh al-Manar', and a treatise on tasawwuf. He authored a commentary on Al-Wiqayah but did not manage to whitewrite it (write a fair copy); so his son Muhammad whitewrote it and added to it. Thus in 'Al-Daw' al-Lami' li-A'yan al-Qarn al-Tasi'' by Shams al-Din al-Sakhawi, 'Al-Shaqa'iq', 'A'lam al-Akhyar', and 'Kashf al-Zunun'. 3. Among them: al-Sayyid 'Ali al-Tummanati al-Rumi, who was in the region of Togat in the land of Rum, a man of virtue in all sciences. He authored 'Sharh al-Wiqayah' and named it 'Al-'Inayah', and a commentary on 'Al-Zij'. He died at the end of the eighth century. Thus in 'Al-Shaqa'iq'. 4. Among them: 'Ali known as Musannifak, son of Majd al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mas'ud ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad ibn al-Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Bistami al-Harawi al-Razi. He was born in 803 AH, and traveled with his brother for the pursuit of knowledge in 823 AH. He studied with Jalal al-Din Yusuf (student of Sa'd al-Taftazani), 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Abhari al-Shafi'i, Fasih al-Din Muhammad ibn Muhammad, and others. He reached the rank of virtue and perfection, and authored works from a young age; therefore he became famous as Musannifak, the kaf in the Persian language being a diminutive. So he authored: 'Sharh Misbah al-Nahw', 'Sharh Adab al-Bahth', 'Sharh al-Lubab', 'Sharh al-Mutawwal', 'Sharh Sharh al-Taftazani li al-Miftah', 'Hashiyat al-Talwih', 'Sharh al-Qasidah al-Burdah', 'Sharh Qasidah Ibn Sina', 'Sharh al-Wiqayah', and 'Sharh al-Hidayah', the last two he authored after 839 AH, which was the year of his journey to Herat. He migrated in 848 AH to the land of Rum, and authored there 'Sharh Masabih al-Sunnah', 'Sharh Sharh al-Sayyid al-Jurjani li al-Miftah', 'Hashiyat Sharh al-Matali'', a commentary on part of 'Usul Fakhr al-Islam', 'Sharh al-Kashshaf', 'Anwar al-Hada'iq', 'Hada'iq al-Iman', 'Tuhfat al-Salatin' (the last three in Persian), and 'Al-Tuhfah al-Mahmudiyyah' in Persian on advice to sultans.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarajim) from the work 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah'. It presents the lives and scholarly contributions of four Hanafi commentators of the legal text Al-Wiqayah by Imam Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani. The author begins by reaffirming the status of Al-Wiqayah as a reliable matn and the dedication of scholars to its study. He then lists four commentators: first, 'Ala' al-Din al-Aswad al-Rumi (Qarah Khwajah), who wrote a two-volume commentary during his tenure as a teacher in Iznik. Second, al-Mawla 'Abd al-Latif ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Farishta (Ibn Malik), a versatile scholar whose unfinished commentary was completed by his son Muhammad. Third, al-Sayyid 'Ali al-Tummanati al-Rumi, who wrote a commentary called Al-'Inayah. Fourth, 'Ali al-Shahir bi-Musannifak, a prolific author who produced commentaries on multiple fields including Al-Wiqayah and Al-Hidayah. The passage provides valuable historical data about the transmission and development of Hanafi legal scholarship.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Imam Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, known as 'Wiqayat al-Riwayah fi Masa'il al-Hidayah', which serves as a summary of his larger work Al-Hidayah.
شرح (sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
تبييض (tabyid): The process of producing a fair copy (whitewriting) of a manuscript, often after the author's draft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The commentators on Al-Wiqayah each contributed uniquely to the Hanafi tradition, and their biographies reveal the collaborative, intergenerational nature of Islamic scholarship.

Life and Teachers of al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani
Biographical entry with personal details and teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, birth and death dates of al-Jurjani, and identify his primary teachers and their contributions.

Core Idea
Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani was a towering Hanafi scholar whose teachers included the author of the famed hashiah on al-Hidayah.

Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani (d. 816 AH) is one of the most influential figures in the Islamic intellectual tradition. His biography, as recorded by his student or later biographers, provides a window into the scholarly networks of the 8th–9th centuries AH. In this lesson, we focus on his lineage, the teachers who shaped him, and the scholarly environment that produced his remarkable corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and lineage
Note the complete name: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ali, Abu al-Hasan, Zayn al-Din al-Husayni. Recognize the honorifics that indicate his noble Sayyid lineage and his scholarly reputation.
The title 'al-Sayyid' denotes descent from the Prophet (ﷺ).
2
Record birth and death dates
He was born in Sha'ban 740 AH and died on Wednesday, 6 Rabi' al-Awwal 816 AH. Commit these dates as anchors for the 8th–9th century scholarly timeline.
His lifespan covers about 76 years.
3
List the teachers mentioned
The text names al-Nur al-Ta'usi (commentator of al-Miftah), Mukhlis al-Din Abu al-Khayr Ali ibn Qutb al-Din al-Razi, and in Egypt: Akmal al-Din al-Babarti (author of al-Inayah: Hashiyat al-Hidayah) and Mubarak Shah al-Mantiqi.
Al-Babarti's hashiah on al-Hidayah is a key Hanafi reference.
4
Note the scholarly reputation
The text states he 'attained a high rank of verification' and 'gained the utmost degree of precision'. This reflects his mastery of both rational and transmitted sciences.
His debates with al-Taftazani are legendary.
5
Contextualize within Hanafi tradition
Al-Jurjani's study under al-Babarti links him directly to the school's authoritative commentary tradition. This lineage strengthens the reliability of his own hashiah works.
His hashiah on al-Hidayah is considered a major Hanafi reference.

السيد السند العلامة المستند المشهور بالسيد الشريف الجرجاني: علي بن محمد بن علي، أبو الحسن، زين الدين الحسيني، ولد في شعبان سنة أربعين بعد سبعمئة، وأخذ العلم عن النور الطاؤسي شارح «المفتاح»، ومخلص الدين أبي الخير علي بن قطب الدين الرازي، وغيرهما من علماء بلاده. ودخل بلاد مصر فأخذ بها عن أكمل الدين البابرتي، مؤلّف «العناية حاشية الهداية»، وعن مبارك شاه المنطقي. وبلغ رتبة عليا من التحقيق، وفاز بالمرتبة القصوى من التدقيق، وكانت وفاته الأربعاء السادس من الربيع الأوّل من سنة ست عشرة بعد ثمانمئة. وله تصانيف كثيرة ذكرها السخاوي في «الضوء اللامع في أعيان القرن التاسع»، والكفوي في أعلام الأخيار، والسيوطي في «بغية الوعاة في طبقات النحاة»، وغيرهم منها: رسالة في تقسيم الموجود»، و«رسالة في الحرف»، و«رسالة في الصوت»، ورسالة «صغرى» وأخرى «كبرى» في المنطق، و«رسالة في مناقب خواجه نقشبند»، و«رسالة في الوجود والعدم»، و«رسالة في الآفاق والأنفس»، و«رسالة في علم الأدوار». و«رسالة في الصرف»، و «رسالة في النحو»، و «شرح مختصر الأبهري» الشهير بايسا غوجي، وحاشية شرح الشمسية القطبي»، و«حاشية شرح المطالع»، و«حاشية شرح التجريد» للأصفهاني، وشرح ملخص الجغميني»، و«حاشية شرح مختصر ابن الحاجب» للعضد، وحاشية تفسير البيضاوي»، و«حاشية شرح حكمة العين، و «شرح التذكرة في الهيأة»، و «شرح الفرائض السراجية»، و«شرح الوقاية». و «شرح المواقف» و«شرح «المفتاح» و «شرح الكافية»، و«حاشية تفسير البيضاوي»، و«حاشية مشكاة المصابيح»، و«حاشية خلاصة الطيبي في أصول الحديث»، و«حاشية العوارف»، و«حاشية الهداية»، و«حاشية حكمة الإشراق» و«حاشية التحفة الشاهية»، و«حاشية شرح الكافية» للرضي. و«حاشية المتوسط شرح الكفاية»، و«حاشية العوامل الجرجانية»، و«حاشية رسالة الوضع»، و«حاشية التلويح» أو «التوضيح»، و«حاشية إشكال التأسيس»، وحاشية تحرير إقليدس»، و«رسالة في المناظرة»، و«رسالة في تعريفات الأشياء». و«حاشية شرح الطوالع»، و «حاشية شرح هداية الحكمة»، و«حاشية شرح الكافية لنقره كار، وحاشية شرح شك الإشارات» للطوسي، وغير ذلك، وكل تصانيفه جيدة مفيدة شاهد بجودة طبعه، وقوّة ذكاوته، وله مع معاصره السعد التفتازاني مشاجرات ومناظرات، وقد بسطت في ترجمتهما في «الفوائد البهية».
The masterly leader, the illustrious scholar, the support, famous as al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn Ali, Abu al-Hasan, Zayn al-Din al-Husayni, born in Sha'ban in the year forty after seven hundred (740 AH). He studied under al-Nur al-Ta'usi, commentator of 'al-Miftah', and Mukhlis al-Din Abi al-Khayr Ali ibn Qutb al-Din al-Razi and other scholars of his land. He entered Egypt and studied under Akmal al-Din al-Babarti, author of 'al-Inayah: Hashiyat al-Hidayah', and under Mubarak Shah al-Mantiqi. He attained a high rank of verification and gained the utmost degree of precision. His death was on Wednesday, the sixth of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year sixteen after eight hundred (816 AH). He has many works mentioned by al-Sakhawi in 'al-Daw' al-Lami' fi A'yan al-Qarn al-Tasi', al-Kafawi in 'A'lam al-Akhyar', al-Suyuti in 'Bughyat al-Wu'ah fi Tabaqat al-Nuhah', and others. Among them: a treatise on the division of existence, a treatise on the letter, a treatise on sound, a small and a large treatise on logic, a treatise on the merits of Khwaja Naqshband, a treatise on being and non-being, a treatise on the horizons and souls, a treatise on the science of cycles, a treatise on morphology, a treatise on grammar, a commentary on 'Mukhtasar al-Abhari' famous as 'Iysa Ghawji', a gloss on 'Sharh al-Shamsiyyah al-Qutbi', a gloss on 'Sharh al-Matali'', a gloss on 'Sharh al-Tajrid' by al-Isfahani, a commentary on 'Talkhis al-Jaghmini', a gloss on 'Sharh Mukhtasar Ibn al-Hajib' by al-'Adud, a gloss on 'Tafsir al-Baydawi', a gloss on 'Sharh Hikmat al-'Ayn', a commentary on 'al-Tadhkirah fi al-Hay'ah', a commentary on 'al-Fara'id al-Sirajiyyah', a commentary on 'al-Wiqayah', a commentary on 'al-Mawaqif', a commentary on 'al-Miftah', a commentary on 'al-Kafiyah', a gloss on 'Tafsir al-Baydawi', a gloss on 'Mishkat al-Masabih', a gloss on 'Khulasat al-Tibi fi Usul al-Hadith', a gloss on 'al-'Awarif', a gloss on 'al-Hidayah', a gloss on 'Hikmat al-Ishraq', a gloss on 'al-Tuhfah al-Shahiyyah', a gloss on 'Sharh al-Kafiyah' by al-Radi, a gloss on 'al-Mutawassit Sharh al-Kifayah', a gloss on 'al-'Awamil al-Jurjaniyyah', a gloss on 'Risalah al-Wad'', a gloss on 'al-Talwih' or 'al-Tawdih', a gloss on 'Ishkal al-Ta'sis', a gloss on 'Tahrir Uqlidis', a treatise on disputation, a treatise on definitions of things, a gloss on 'Sharh al-Tawali'', a gloss on 'Sharh Hidayat al-Hikmah', a gloss on 'Sharh al-Kafiyah' by Naqrah Kar, a gloss on 'Sharh Shakk al-Isharat' by al-Tusi, and other works. All his works are good and beneficial, testifying to the excellence of his nature and the strength of his intelligence. He had debates and discussions with his contemporary Sa'd al-Taftazani. I have expanded on their biographies in 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah'.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This is an extensive biography of al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani (d. 816 AH), one of the most influential scholars in the Islamic intellectual tradition. He was a master of both rational and transmitted sciences. The text details his birth, teachers (including Akmal al-Din al-Babarti, author of the famous hashiah on al-Hidayah called al-Inayah), and death date. It then lists a large number of his works, covering logic, philosophy, grammar, morphology, astronomy, fiqh, usul, hadith, and more. Notably, he wrote commentaries on al-Wiqayah, al-Mawaqif, and al-Miftah, and glosses on many standard texts. The author notes that al-Jurjani engaged in academic debates with his contemporary Sa'd al-Taftazani, and that he has treated both scholars more fully in his al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah.

Key Terms
السيد الشريف الجرجاني (al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani): A famed scholar of the 8th–9th centuries AH, known for his works in logic, philosophy, and commentary on Hanafi fiqh
حاشية (hashiyah): A gloss or super-commentary, often written on the margins of a base text or sharh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Major Works of al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani
List of scholarly works of al-Jurjani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize al-Jurjani's works by discipline (fiqh, usul, logic, etc.) and identify his most famous commentaries and glosses, especially those related to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Jurjani authored over thirty works covering almost every Islamic science, but his Hanafi fiqh commentaries are among the most influential.

The biographical passage on al-Jurjani includes an extensive list of his writings, demonstrating his prolific output across multiple disciplines. In this lesson, we will survey his works, focusing on those most relevant to Hanafi fiqh and usul, and understand their place in the scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main disciplines covered
Scan the list for keywords indicating subject: logic (al-mantiq), grammar (al-nahw), morphology (al-sarf), fiqh (al-fiqh, al-Hidayah), usul, hadith, philosophy, etc.
The list includes treatises (risalah), commentaries (sharh), and glosses (hashiyah).
2
Select works directly related to Hanafi fiqh
Highlight 'Sharh al-Wiqayah' (commentary on a Hanafi fiqh text), 'Hashiyat al-Hidayah', and 'Sharh al-Fara'id al-Sirajiyyah' (Hanafi inheritance).
These are the core Hanafi contributions.
3
Note the commentary chain
Al-Jurjani's hashiah on al-Hidayah is a super-commentary on al-Babarti's 'al-Inayah'. Understand that this is typical: a hashiah refines an earlier sharh.
The chain: al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) -> al-Inayah (al-Babarti) -> Hashiyat al-Jurjani.
4
Recognize works in logic and philosophy
Many works like 'Sharh al-Mawaqif', glosses on 'Sharh al-Tajrid', and treatises on existence show his expertise in rational sciences.
His 'Sharh al-Mawaqif' is a classic text in kalam.
5
Assess the breadth and significance
The sheer number and variety indicate his mastery. The author remarks that 'all his works are good and beneficial', testifying to their quality.
This breadth is typical of scholars of his era.

This is an extensive biography of al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani (d. 816 AH), one of the most influential scholars in the Islamic intellectual tradition. Biography of Muhammad al-Kawakibi: Scholar and Versifier
Short biography of a Hanafi scholar and his works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Muhammad al-Kawakibi's major works and explain his contribution to the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar who versified key Hanafi texts to aid memorization and wrote beneficial commentaries.

This lesson introduces a later Hanafi scholar who made important contributions by putting foundational texts into verse. Understanding his work helps you see how Hanafi knowledge was transmitted and preserved through the centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Note his full name: Muhammad ibn Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Yahya al-Kawakibi al-Halabi, and his death date: 1096 AH in Dhu al-Qa'dah.
2
List his versifications
He versified two major texts: al-Wiqayah (Hanafi fiqh) and al-Manar (usul al-fiqh). Versification (nazm) made the content easier to memorize.
These are not original works but poetic renditions of existing prose.
3
Note his commentaries
He wrote a commentary (sharh) on his own versification of al-Wiqayah, described as 'beneficial'. He also commented on his versification of al-Manar.
This shows he was not only a poet but also a thorough commentator.
4
Recognize his other works
He authored glosses (hawashi) on Tafsir al-Baydawi and Sharh al-Mawaqif, indicating his breadth in tafsir and kalam.
These works are outside fiqh but show his scholarly range.
5
Identify the source
The biography is taken from 'Khulasat al-Athar fi A'yan al-Qarn al-Hadi 'Ashar' by Muhammad al-Muhibbi al-Dimashqi.
This is a biographical dictionary of the 11th century AH.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦. ومنهم : محمد بن حسن بن أحمد بن أبي يحيى الكواكبي الحلبي، المتوفى سنة ست وتسعين وألف في ذي القعدة، نظم «الوقاية»، وشرحه شرحا مفيدا، ونظم «المنار» وشرحه، وعلق على تفسير البيضاوي»، و«حاشية على شرح المواقف) . كذا في خلاصة الأثر في أعيان القرن الحادي عشر لمحمد بن فضل الله المحبي الدِّمَشْقِي.
6. Among them: Muhammad ibn Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Yahya al-Kawakibi al-Halabi, died in the year one thousand ninety-six in Dhu al-Qa'dah. He versified 'al-Wiqayah', and commented on it with a beneficial commentary, and versified 'al-Manar' and commented on it, and wrote glosses on 'Tafsir al-Baydawi', and a gloss on 'Sharh al-Mawaqif'. Thus in 'Khulasat al-Athar fi A'yan al-Qarn al-Hadi 'Ashar' by Muhammad ibn Fadlallah al-Muhibbi al-Dimashqi.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This is a brief biography of Muhammad al-Kawakibi al-Halabi (d. 1096 AH). He is known for putting two key Hanafi texts into verse: al-Wiqayah (a famous manual of Hanafi fiqh) and al-Manar (a work of usul al-fiqh). He also wrote commentaries on his own versifications. Additionally, he composed glosses on Tafsir al-Baydawi and Sharh al-Mawaqif. The source for this biography is al-Muhibbi's biographical dictionary Khulasat al-Athar.

Key Terms
نظم (nazama): To put a prose work into verse form, making it easier to memorize
شرح (sharh): A commentary, explaining and expanding on a text
حاشية (hashiyah): A gloss or marginal note on a larger work

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Hidayah and al-Manar
B) Al-Wiqayah and al-Manar
C) Al-Wiqayah and al-Miftah
D) Al-Manar and al-Mustasfa

Key Takeaway
Muhammad al-Kawakibi is a notable Hanafi scholar who versified and commented on key texts to facilitate memorization and understanding.

The Life and Works of Ahmad Ibn Kamal
Biography of Ahmad Ibn Kamal, who composed a concise text from al-Wiqayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ahmad Ibn Kamal's key works and explain his contribution to the Hanafi tradition by pointing out oversights in al-Wiqayah and its commentary.

Core Idea
Ibn Kamal revised al-Wiqayah and critiqued its author and commentator.

This lesson introduces you to Ahmad Ibn Kamal, a prolific Hanafi scholar who composed a revised abridgment of al-Wiqayah and a commentary. Understanding his work helps you appreciate the scholarly tradition of commentary and critique within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Locate the full name and nickname of the scholar: Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal al-Rumi, known as Ibn Kamal.
Notice the nisbah 'al-Rumi' indicates his origin.
2
Name His Main Works
Identify the two works directly mentioned: 'al-Islah' (the abridgment) and 'al-Idah' (the commentary on it).
These titles reflect his critical approach ('Islah' means reform/improvement).
3
Recognize His Critical Approach
Note that in both works he pointed out objections and oversights against the author of al-Wiqayah and its commentator. This shows he did not merely summarize but engaged critically.
The terms used are 'iradat' (objections) and 'musamahat' (oversights).
4
Acknowledge His Broader Oeuvre
He authored over one hundred works, including a text in usul al-fiqh called 'Taghyir al-Tanqih' and its commentary.
This demonstrates his wide-ranging scholarship beyond fiqh.

ومنهم: أحمد بن سليمان بن كمال الرومي الشهير بابن كمال، ألف متناً مختصرا من «الوقاية مع تغيرات، سماه بـ«الإصلاح»، ثم شرحه وسماه بـ«الإيضاح»، وأشار فيهما إلى إيرادات ومسامحات على مؤلّف «الوقاية» وشارحه، وله تصانیف آخر تزيد على مئة منها: متن في الأصول سماه «تغيير التنقيح» وشرحه.
And among them: Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Kamal al-Rumi, famous as Ibn Kamal. He authored a concise text from 'al-Wiqayah' with changes, calling it 'al-Islah'. Then he commented on it, calling it 'al-Idah'. In both, he pointed out objections and oversights against the author of 'al-Wiqayah' and its commentator. He has other works exceeding one hundred, including a text in usul called 'Taghyir al-Tanqih' and its commentary.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This is a biography of Ahmad Ibn Kamal (d. after 1000 AH?), known as Ibn Kamal. He produced a revised abridgment of al-Wiqayah, titled al-Islah, and then wrote a commentary on it called al-Idah. In these works, he raised objections (iradat) and pointed out oversights (musamahat) in the original al-Wiqayah and its standard commentary. He was a prolific author with over one hundred works, including a text on usul al-fiqh called Taghyir al-Tanqih, which he also commented on.

Key Terms
إيضاح (al-Idah): The title of Ibn Kamal's commentary on his own abridgment of al-Wiqayah
الإصلاح (al-Islah): Ibn Kamal's revised abridgment of al-Wiqayah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ahmad Ibn Kamal is remembered for his critical abridgment and commentary on al-Wiqayah, contributing to the Hanafi tradition of scholarly revision.

Hanafi Commentators on Al-Wiqayah (Continued)
Continuation of a biographical list of Hanafi commentators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi scholars who wrote commentaries on Al-Wiqayah and describe their contributions to the tradition.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab was transmitted and refined through generations of commentators on core texts like Al-Wiqayah.

This lesson continues our survey of commentators on the foundational Hanafi fiqh text Al-Wiqayah. The passage lists several scholars, including Al-Tamartashi, Fasih al-Din al-Harawi, and others, along with their works and significant relationships. Understanding these commentaries is essential for tracing the transmission of Hanafi rulings and appreciating the depth of the school's scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of each biographical entry
For each scholar, note the name, any honorific titles, and the title of their commentary on Al-Wiqayah. Pay attention to attributions like 'al-Tamartashi' or 'al-Harawi'.
The commentary titles often reveal the author's approach (e.g., 'Kashf al-Wiqayah' suggests an uncovering of meanings).
2
Trace the scholarly relationships
Look for mentions of other scholars in connection with each commentator. For example, Fasih al-Din al-Harawi had discussions with Sadr al-Shari'ah, and the passage mentions the author's maternal grandfather.
These relationships help map the chains of transmission (isnad) of the Hanafi school.
3
Note the geographical and temporal context
Identify where each scholar is from (e.g., Khwarazm, Harat) and, if given, their death dates. This situates them in the history of the madhhab.
Al-Tamartashi died in 1004 AH; Qasim al-Nikandi died in 970 AH.
4
Recognize the variety of commentary styles
Some commentaries are in verse (e.g., 'Tuhfat al-Aqran'), others are critical responses. Note the purpose: to explain, defend, or expand on the base text.
The range of works shows the vitality of the Hanafi tradition.
5
Connect to later sources
The passage references later Hanafi works like 'Radd al-Muhtar' and 'Kashf al-Zunun'. Understand that these biographical notes come from a meta-commentary (a commentary on a commentary).
This layered referencing is typical of later Hanafi scholarship.

Among them: 'Allamah Fasih al-Din al-Harawi, I did not find a biography for him, and I read his commentary in two volumes, and it is a commentary sufficient for solving difficulties, and he has with the commentator Sadr al-Shari'ah discussions, and among his works as he mentioned in places from his commentary: 'Hawashi Sharh Talkhis al-Ma'ani wa al-Bayan', and 'Sharh Shamsiyyat al-Hisab'. And he mentioned in 'Kitab al-Zakat' after quoting the words of Sadr al-Shari'ah: 'Look at this one who inserted another pillar in faith... etc.' He indicated by this to my maternal grandfather, the greatest Shaykh al-Islam, the Imam of the Ummah in the world, the reviver of the rites of the religion among the nations, the eradicator of the strength of lions of innovation and traces of injustice, the happy martyr, the system of the nation, the Shari'ah, piety, and religion, famous among the people of Islam as Shaykh al-Taslim (the Elder of Submission), for he verified in his treatise called 'Tahqiq al-Iman' that there must be in Islam submission... etc. 12. Thus in Kashf al-Zunun 'an Asami al-Kutub wa al-Funun. 19. And among the commentaries is a commentary called 'Kashf al-Wiqayah' which, as its name suggests, is an uncovering of the demands of 'al-Wiqayah'.

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the biographical section listing commentators on the Hanafi fiqh text 'Al-Wiqayah'. The author, likely 'Ali al-Qari, provides brief notes on several scholars who wrote commentaries on Al-Wiqayah. The first part completes the biography of the author Al-Tamartashi, mentioning his works and death date. Then entries 11–19 list other commentators, including Fasih al-Din al-Harawi, who had debates with Sadr al-Shari'ah, and a reference to the author's maternal grandfather ('Shaykh al-Taslim'). The list includes names such as Junayd ibn Sandal, 'Ali al-Tarabullusi, Qasim al-Nikandi, Husam al-Din al-Kusaj, 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Naysaburi, and 'Izz al-Din Tahir al-Shafi'i. The final entry mentions an unnamed commentary titled 'Kashf al-Wiqayah'. The footnotes (not fully preserved) provide additional references from later Hanafi works like Radd al-Muhtar and Kashf al-Zunun. This section serves to document the scholarly chain and variety of commentaries on the foundational text. It underscores the importance of Al-Wiqayah in the Hanafi curriculum and the efforts of later scholars to explain and expand upon it.

Key Terms
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): A commentary on the Hanafi fiqh text 'Al-Wiqayah' by Taju al-Shari'ah; here it refers to the base text being commented upon.
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): Honorific title for the renowned Hanafi scholar 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud al-Mahbubi (d. 747 AH), author of a famous commentary on Al-Wiqayah.
مناقشات (munaqashat): Scholarly discussions or critical debates, often involving disagreement on points of interpretation.
