Biographical Survey of Commentators and Glossators of Sharh al-Wiqayah
Biographical listing of scholars and their works on Sharh al-Wiqayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key commentators and glossators of Sharh al-Wiqayah and explain the significance of their works within the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
The scholarly tradition of Sharh al-Wiqayah produced a rich corpus of commentaries and glosses, each contributing to the transmission and refinement of Hanafi fiqh.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah provides a biographical survey of the scholars who wrote commentaries (shurrah) and glosses (muhashshin) on Sharh al-Wiqayah. While not a fiqh ruling, this chain of transmission is essential for understanding the development of Hanafi fiqh scholarship and the authoritative weight of later works. The passage lists names, works, and sometimes additional details such as teachers or unique features of each commentary.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish commentators from glossators
The seventh study lists commentators (shurrah) who wrote independent commentaries on al-Wiqayah, while the eighth study lists glossators (muhashshin) who wrote supercommentaries (hashiyah) on Sharh al-Wiqayah by Sadr al-Shari'ah. Identify which category each scholar belongs to.
Commentators wrote on the original al-Wiqayah, glossators wrote on Sharh al-Wiqayah.
2
Extract each scholar's name, work title, and any distinctive features
For each entry, note the scholar's full name, the title of their commentary or gloss, and any special notes (e.g., al-Nikandi's al-Tatbiq explicitly answers Ibn Kamal's objections, or Yusuf Jalbī's gloss includes the sultan's name and dates).
Some entries are brief; others provide more biographical detail.
3
Identify the time period and geographical context
The passage mentions dates like 970 AH for al-Nikandi and 891-901 AH for Yusuf Jalbī's composition. Many scholars are from the 'land of Rum' (Ottoman Anatolia). Note the 9th–10th/15th–16th century context.
This period is significant in Hanafi scholarship with many glosses and commentaries produced in the Ottoman realm.
4
Recognize the significance of this chain for later Hanafi works
Works like Dhakhirat al-'Uqba became widely studied. Understanding who wrote what helps in evaluating the authority of later references (e.g., Ibn 'Abidin quotes these works).
This biographical awareness is a key skill for navigating the Hanafi madrasa curriculum.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical survey from the work 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. It lists commentators (shurrah) and glossators (muhashshin) of the Hanafi fiqh text Sharh al-Wiqayah. The seventh study presents several commentators: al-Mawla Muhammad (grandfather of the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar), Zayn al-Din Junayd ibn Sandal (author of Tawfiq al-'Inayah), 'Ala' al-Din al-Tarabulsi (author of al-Istighna'), Qasim ibn Sulayman al-Nikandi (author of al-Tatbiq), Husam al-Din al-Kusaj (author of al-Istighna' fi al-Istifa'), 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Naysaburi, and 'Izz al-Din Tahir al-Shafi'i. A commentary named Kashf al-Wiqayah is also mentioned. The eighth study lists glossators: al-Mawla known as Musannifak (already mentioned) and Yusuf Jalbī, whose gloss Dhakhirat al-'Uqba is famous. Details about Yusuf Jalbī include his lineage, teachers, and the period of composition. The passage reflects the scholarly tradition surrounding Sharh al-Wiqayah, a key Hanafi fiqh text.

Key Terms
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A famous Hanafi fiqh text by Sadr al-Shari'ah, the base text for many commentaries.
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): The commentary on al-Wiqayah by the same author, Sadr al-Shari'ah, which itself became the subject of further commentaries and glosses.
حاشية (hashiyah): A gloss or supercommentary, typically written in the margins of a main text, providing explanation and critique.
ذخيرة العقبى (Dhakhirat al-'Uqba): The name of Yusuf Jalbī's gloss on Sharh al-Wiqayah, meaning 'Provision for the Hereafter'.
التطبيق (al-Tatbiq): Commentary by Qasim al-Nikandi on al-Wiqayah, notable for answering Ibn Kamal's objections.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Ala' al-Din al-Tarabulsi
B) Zayn al-Din Junayd ibn Sandal
C) Yusuf Jalbī
D) Qasim ibn Sulayman al-Nikandi

Key Takeaway

Biography of Yusuf Jalabi (Ahi Jalabi) and His Hashiyah Dhakheerah al-Uqba
Biographical entry on the Hanafi jurist Yusuf Jalabi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Yusuf Jalabi and explain the significance of his hashiah in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Yusuf Jalabi's hashiah Dhakheerah al-Uqba is a vital Hanafi commentary that bridged the Ottoman scholarly tradition with classical texts.

This lesson introduces you to Yusuf Jalabi, a prominent Hanafi jurist and commentator. His hashiah on Sharh al-Wiqayah became widely used in Ottoman madrasas. Understanding his life and work helps situate the later Hanafi commentary tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and lineage
Locate the scholar's complete name: Yusuf ibn Junayd al-Tawqati, known as Ahi Jalabi. Note that 'Jalabi' means 'my master' in Ottoman custom.
Attribution to Tawqat (a town in Anatolia) is important for geographical context.
2
Identify his teachers and their significance
List the teachers mentioned: Sayyid Ahmad al-Qarimi (student of the author of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyyah), Salah al-Din (teacher of Sultan Bayezid), and Muhammad ibn Framuz (Mullah Khusraw).
These teachers connect him to major Hanafi scholarly chains.
3
Note his hashiah's title, timeline, and dedication
The hashiah is titled Dhakheerah al-Uqba, begun in 891 AH, completed in 901 AH, dedicated to Sultan Bayezid II.
The timeline places him in the late 9th/early 10th century AH.
4
Recognize the sources that record his biography
The passage cites 'Aalam al-Akhyar' and 'al-Shaqa'iq' for his life, and 'Kashf al-Zunun' for his death year (905 AH).
These are standard biographical dictionaries for Ottoman Hanafi scholars.
5
Place his work in the context of Hanafi legal literature
His hashiah comments on Sharh al-Wiqayah, itself a commentary on al-Wiqayah. This chain reflects the layered commentary tradition in Hanafi fiqh.
Understanding this chain helps navigate later Hanafi references.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم : يوسف جلبي ؛ حاشيته متداولة بين الطلبة مشهورة بـ«ذخيرة العقبى» : أوّلها الحمد لله الذي شرح صدر الشريعة الغراء...الخ، ذكر فيها اسم سلطان عصره ببلاد الروم : السلطان بایزید خان بن محمد خان بن مراد خان، وذكر في آخرها أنه ابتدأ فيها سنة إحدى وتسعين وثمانمئة وختمها بختام ذي الحجة من سنة إحدى وتسعمئة. وهو يوسف بن جنيد التوقاتي، نسبة إلى توقات بلدة من بلاد الروم الشهير بأخي جلبي، ومعنى جلبي في عرفهم : سيدي. أخذ العلم عن السيد أحمد القريمي، تلميذ صاحب «الفتاوي البزازية»، ثم قرأ على صلاح الدين معلّم السلطان بايزيد خان، ثم على محمد بن فراموز، بمولى خسرو، وهار مدرّساً بمدارس. كذا ذكره في «أعلام الأخيار»، و«الشقائق»، وكانت وفاته على ما في «كشف الظنون» سنة خمس وتسعمئة.
Among them is Yusuf Jalabi; his hashiah is widely circulated among students, known as Dhakheerah al-Uqba: its beginning is 'Praise be to Allah who opened the breast of the noble Shariah...' etc. He mentioned in it the name of the sultan of his time in the land of Rum: Sultan Bayezid Khan ibn Muhammad Khan ibn Murad Khan, and he mentioned at its end that he began it in the year 891 AH and completed it at the end of Dhu al-Hijjah of the year 901 AH. He is Yusuf ibn Junayd al-Tawqati, attributed to Tawqat, a town in the land of Rum, famously known as Ahi Jalabi, and the meaning of 'Jalabi' in their custom is 'my master'. He acquired knowledge from Sayyid Ahmad al-Qarimi, a student of the author of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyyah, then studied under Salah al-Din, the teacher of Sultan Bayezid Khan, then under Muhammad ibn Framuz, Mullah Khusraw, and became a teacher at various madrasas. Thus he is mentioned in 'Aalam al-Akhyar' and 'al-Shaqa'iq', and his death, according to 'Kashf al-Zunun', was in the year 905 AH.

Commentary
This is a biographical passage about Yusuf Jalabi (Ahi Jalabi), a Hanafi jurist and commentator on Sharh al-Wiqayah. The passage identifies his famous hashiah titled 'Dhakheerah al-Uqba', which he began in 891 AH and completed in 901 AH. It notes his lineage: Yusuf ibn Junayd al-Tawqati, and explains the honorific 'Jalabi' means 'my master'. His teachers include Sayyid Ahmad al-Qarimi (student of the author of al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyyah) and others, and he taught at several madrasas. The sources cited are 'Aalam al-Akhyar' and 'al-Shaqa'iq', and his death year is recorded as 905 AH in 'Kashf al-Zunun'.

Key Terms
حاشية (hashiyah): A super-commentary or gloss on a text; here it refers to Yusuf Jalabi's commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah.
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): The commentary on al-Wiqayah by Sadr al-Shariah; a central Hanafi fiqh text.
جلبي (Jalabi): An Ottoman honorific meaning 'my master', used for Yusuf Jalabi.

Biography of Hasan Jalabi al-Fanari: A Hanafi Scholar
Biographical entry on the Hanafi scholar Hasan Jalabi al-Fanari and his works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Hasan Jalabi al-Fanari and identify his major works within the Hanafi educational tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar's lineage and teachers are the chain of knowledge transmission—knowing them strengthens the reliability of his works.

In the Hanafi tradition, knowing the biographies of key scholars (tarajim) is essential for understanding the chain of transmission (isnad) and the authority of their works. This lesson introduces you to Hasan Jalabi al-Fanari, a prolific commentator whose hashiahs are widely studied. By examining his life, teachers, and writings, you will appreciate how later Hanafi scholarship built upon earlier foundations.

Guided Path
1
Identify Lineage and Title Origin
Read the first part of the passage to extract the full name of the scholar and the story behind the title 'al-Fanari'. Note the connection to the king of Rum and the gift of a lantern (fanar).
The title al-Fanari originates from the Persian word 'fanar' (lantern).
2
Identify Teachers and Education
Locate the names of his teachers (Mulla Ali al-Tusi and Mulla Khusraw) and the subjects in which he excelled (theology, Arabic, rational sciences, principles).
His teachers were prominent Hanafi scholars of the Ottoman era.
3
List Major Works and Their Status
Read the list of his authored hashiahs (e.g., on Sharh al-Mawaqif, al-Mutawwal, etc.) and note the overall assessment: 'all his works are accepted' (جميع تصانيفه مقبولة).
A 'hashiyah' is a super-commentary; his works are authoritative in Hanafi study circles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم : حسن جلبي بن شمس الدين محمد شاه بن مؤلف «فصول البدائع» شمس الدين محمد بن حمزة الرومي الشهير كسلفه بالفناري، وهو لقب لجدّ أبيه؛ لأنه فيما قيل : لما قدم على ملك الروم أهدى له فيناراً، فكان إذا سئل عنه يقول : ابن الفنري، فعُرف بذلك. ولد حسن سنة أربعين وثمانمئة، وأخذ العلم عن ملا علي الطوسي، وملا خسرو، حتى برع في الكلام والعربية، والمعقول والأصول، وألف «حاشية شرح المواقف»، و«حاشية المطوّل»، و«حاشية التلويح»، و«حاشية تفسير البيضاوي»، و«حاشية شرح الوقاية»، وغير ذلك، وجميع تصانيفه مقبولة، وكانت وفاته سنة ست وثمانين وثمانمئة.
Among them is Hasan Jalabi ibn Shams al-Din Muhammad Shah ibn the author of 'Fusul al-Bada'i' Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Rumi, famously known like his predecessors as al-Fanari, which is a title for his grandfather; because, it is said, when he came to the king of Rum, he gifted him a fanar (lantern), so when asked about him, he would say 'Ibn al-Fanari', thus he became known by that. Hasan was born in the year 840 AH, and acquired knowledge from Mulla Ali al-Tusi and Mulla Khusraw, until he excelled in theology, Arabic, rational sciences, and principles, and authored 'Hashiyah Sharh al-Mawaqif', 'Hashiyah al-Mutawwal', 'Hashiyah al-Talwih', 'Hashiyah Tafsir al-Baydawi', 'Hashiyah Sharh al-Wiqayah', and others, and all his works are accepted. He was born in 840 AH, studied under prominent teachers like Mulla Ali al-Tusi and Mulla Khusraw, and mastered various disciplines. He authored numerous hashiahs on key texts, including one on Sharh al-Wiqayah. His death in 886 AH is recorded, and all his works are regarded as high quality.

Key Terms

حاشية شرح الوقاية (Hashiyah Sharh al-Wiqayah): Hasan Jalabi's super-commentary on the Sharh al-Wiqayah of Sadr al-Shariah.

Correction: Dhakheerah al-Uqba Not by Hasan Jalabi
Refuting misattribution of a Hanafi hashiah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the chronological and textual evidence that proves Dhakheerah al-Uqba was authored by Yusuf Jalabi, not Hasan Jalabi.

Core Idea
Scholarly attribution must respect chronology: a work completed in 901 AH cannot be written by an author who died in 886 AH.

Many scholars mistakenly attributed the Hanafi hashiah Dhakheerah al-Uqba to Hasan Jalabi, the author of glosses on al-Talwih and al-Mutawwal. This passage corrects that error using two clear proofs: the date of completion of the work and a reference in its preface. Understanding this correction sharpens your ability to evaluate textual attributions in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
State the misattribution
Identify what was mistakenly believed: that Hasan Jalabi (d. 886 AH) authored Dhakheerah al-Uqba.
This error is attributed to 'short-sightedness' (qasr al-nazar).
2
Apply chronological proof
Compare the death date of Hasan Jalabi (886 AH) with the completion date of Dhakheerah al-Uqba (901 AH). 15 years gap makes authorship impossible.
3
Examine the internal textual evidence
The preface of Dhakheerah al-Uqba refers to Mulla Khusraw (d. 885 AH) as 'Shaykhuna' (our teacher). This phrase is expected from a student like Yusuf Jalabi, not a contemporary like Hasan Jalabi.
4
Identify the correct author
Based on the evidence, the true author is Yusuf Jalabi, a student of Mulla Khusraw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت : قد ظنّ كثير من أفاضل عصرنا ، وبعض من سبقنا أنّ «ذخيرة العقبى» من تأليف حسن جلبي، مؤلّف حواشي «التلويح» و«المطوّل» وغيرها، وهو غلط منهم نشأ من قصر النظر ؛ وذلك لأن وفاة حسن كان سنة ست وثمانين وثمانمئة، وختام «ذخيرة العقبى» كان سنة إحدى وتسعمئة (٦) ، فكيف يمكن أن يكون مؤلفه هو؟! وأيضاً ذكر في ديباجة ذخيرة العقبى»: «إنّ من جملة معتبرات الفقه «شرح الوقاية» لصدر الشريعة، وقد تصدى بعض من علماء الزمان نحو حل مغلقاته... الخ. وكتب على قول بعض من علماء الزمان : أعني شيخنا مولانا خسرو، ومولانا ...
I say: Many of the distinguished scholars of our time, and some before us, thought that 'Dhakheerah al-Uqba' was authored by Hasan Jalabi, author of the hashiahs of 'al-Talwih' and 'al-Mutawwal' and others. This is a mistake arising from short-sightedness. That is because the death of Hasan was in 886 AH, while the completion of 'Dhakheerah al-Uqba' was in 901 AH. So how could he be its author? Also, in the preface of 'Dhakheerah al-Uqba' it mentions: 'Among the respected books of fiqh is Sharh al-Wiqayah by Sadr al-Shariah, and some scholars of the time have undertaken to solve its difficulties...' and he wrote on the statement 'some scholars of the time': specifically, our teacher Mulla Khusraw, and our teacher...
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a critical correction by the author of 'Umda al-Ri'ayah' (likely Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi) refuting a common error. Many scholars mistakenly attributed the hashiah 'Dhakheerah al-Uqba' to Hasan Jalabi (d. 886 AH), but the author demonstrates that this is impossible because the work was completed in 901 AH, 15 years after Hasan's death. Furthermore, the preface of 'Dhakheerah al-Uqba' refers to Mulla Khusraw (d. 885 AH) as 'Shaykhuna' (our teacher), which would be appropriate for a student like Yusuf Jalabi, not for Hasan Jalabi who was a contemporary. The correction is based on chronological and textual evidence, underscoring the importance of careful attribution in scholarly works.

Key Terms
ذخيرة العقبى (Dhakheerah al-Uqba): A hashiah (super-commentary) on Sharh al-Wiqayah by Yusuf Jalabi, completed in 901 AH.
مؤلف (mu'allif): Author; here it is argued that Yusuf Jalabi is the true author, not Hasan Jalabi.
حسن جلبي (Hasan Jalabi): A Hanafi scholar (d. 886 AH) known for hashiahs on al-Talwih and al-Mutawwal, mistakenly thought to be the author of Dhakheerah al-Uqba.
شيخنا (Shaykhuna): Our teacher; a term used by a student for his teacher, pointing to Yusuf Jalabi as a student of Mulla Khusraw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hasan Jalabi died before the work was completed
B) The work's style differs from his other writings
C) It was written in Persian, not Arabic
D) It is a fatwa collection, not a hashiah

Key Takeaway
Chronological proof is decisive in establishing or refuting authorship of classical texts.

Correcting a Scholarly Error: The Authorship of Dhakirat al-'Uqba
Biographical notices and correction of authorship error

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct author of Dhakirat al-'Uqba and explain the three pieces of evidence al-Lakhnawi uses to disprove the mistaken attribution.

Core Idea
A scholar's death date and teacher references in his own preface can prove or disprove authorship.

This biographical note from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya not only provides valuable life details of Hanafi commentators but also serves as a model of scholarly criticism. The author, Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, corrects a widely held error regarding who wrote the important hashia Dhakirat al-'Uqba on Sharh al-Wiqaya. By carefully examining historical dates, textual evidence, and stylistic quality, he demonstrates that the true author is Akhi Chalabi Yusuf, not Hasan Chalabi al-Fanari.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars confused
Al-Lakhnawi notes that many mistakenly attribute Dhakirat al-'Uqba to Hasan Chalabi al-Fanari (d. 886 AH), but the true author is Akhi Chalabi Yusuf (d. after 901 AH).
Hasan Chalabi and Akhi Chalabi are distinct scholars; one is often confused with the other.
2
Note the death date discrepancy
Hasan Chalabi died in 886 AH, but the completion date of Dhakirat al-'Uqba is 901 AH. A person cannot complete a work after his death, so this alone disproves the attribution.
This is the strongest evidence because it is objective and irrefutable.
3
Analyze the preface of Dhakirat al-'Uqba
In the preface, the author lists 'our teacher Mulla Khusraw' and also includes 'Mulla Hasan Chalabi al-Fanari' among those who attempted to solve difficulties. If Hasan Chalabi were the author, he would not refer to himself in the third person.
This internal textual evidence is explicit and often overlooked.
4
Consult external biographical works
Standard works like Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya, al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya, and Kashf al-Zunun all attribute Dhakirat al-'Uqba to Akhi Chalabi Yusuf, not to Hasan Chalabi.
These are authoritative references in Hanafi biography.
5
Consider stylistic comparison
Al-Lakhnawi adds that Hasan Chalabi's works are known for profound investigations and subtle clarifications, while Dhakirat al-'Uqba lacks such depth, further supporting that it is not his work.
Stylistic evidence is supplementary and less objective than dates or explicit text.

سماها «هدية المهتدين». وأيضاً من له قوة إدراك وتمييز يعلم من مطالعة ذخيرة العقبى»، ومن مطالعة تصانيف حسن جلبي أنها لغيره ؛ فإنّ تصانيف حسن جلبي كلها مشتملة على تحقيقات منيعة، وتوضيحات لطيفة، تشهد بتبحر مؤلفها، وتوقد طبع مرصفها ، بخلاف «ذخيرة العقبى»، فإنه ليس فيها ما يروي الغليل ويشفى العليل، فضلاً عن تلك التحقيقات والتوضيحات، وفيها ما يشهد على أنّ مؤلّفها ليست له ملكة راسخة، ولا قوة كاملة. ومنهم : المولى محيي الدين محمّد، الشهير بخطيب زاده الرومي، قرأ على والده تاج الدين وعلي الطوسي وخضر بيك، وغيرهم من أفاضل بلاده، وصار مدرساً بإحدى المدارس الثمان بقسطنطينية ، ثم جعله السلطان محمد خان معلماً لنفسه، توفي سنة إحدى بعد تسعمئة ، وله: «حواش على حاشية السيد المتعلقة بشرح التجريد»، و«حواش على حاشية الكشاف» للسيد ، و«حــواش علـى حاشية شرح المختصر للسيد ، و «رسالة في بحث الرؤية والكلام»، و«حواش

The eighth study: Biographies of the commentators of Sharh al-Wiqaya (2). 'A'lam al-Akhyar', and 'al-Shaqa'iq' ( ), and his death according to 'Kashf al-Zunun' (3) was in the year 905 AH. And among them: Hasan Chalabi bin Shams al-Din Muhammad Shah, son of the author of 'Fusul al-Bada'i' Shams al-Din Muhammad bin Hamza al-Rumi, known like his forefathers as al-Fanari, which is a nickname for his grandfather; because it is said: when he came to the king of Rum, he gifted him a lantern (fanar), so when asked about him he would say: Ibn al-Fanari, and thus became known. Hasan was born in the year 840 AH, and sought knowledge from Mulla 'Ali al-Tusi, Mulla Khusraw, until he excelled in theology, Arabic, rational sciences, and principles, and authored 'Hashiyat Sharh al-Mawaqif', 'Hashiyat al-Mutawwal', 'Hashiyat al-Talwih', 'Hashiyat Tafsir al-Baydawi', 'Hashiyat Sharh al-Wiqaya', and others. All his works are acceptable. His death was in the year 886 AH. So stated in 'al-Daw' al-Lami' (4), and 'A'lam al-Akhyar', and 'al-Shaqa'iq' (5). I say: Many of the virtuous of our time, and some before us, thought that 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' was authored by Hasan Chalabi, author of the commentaries on 'al-Talwih' and 'al-Mutawwal' and others, but this is a mistake arising from short-sightedness. That is because Hasan's death was in 886 AH, and the completion of 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' was in 901 AH (6), so how could he be its author? Also, in the preface of 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba', it says: 'Among the esteemed works of fiqh is Sharh al-Wiqaya by Sadr al-Shari'a, and one of the scholars of the time undertook to solve its difficulties... etc.' And he wrote on the statement of 'one of the scholars of the time': 'I mean our teacher Mulla Khusraw, and Mulla... and others.' This is explicit that the author of 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' is not Hasan Chalabi. Also, anyone who reads 'Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya' by al-Kafawi, 'al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya', and 'Kashf al-Zunun' and others would definitely know that the author of 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' is not Hasan Chalabi, because they mention Hasan Chalabi and count among his works 'Hashiyat al-Mutawwal' and others, and they mention Akhi Chalabi Yusuf and attribute 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' to him, and a treatise collecting issues related to disbelief named 'Hidayat al-Muhtadin'. Also, one who has strong perception and discernment knows from reading 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' and from reading the works of Hasan Chalabi that it is by someone else. For the works of Hasan Chalabi all contain profound investigations and subtle clarifications bearing witness to the depth and acute nature of their author, unlike 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba', which does not quench thirst nor cure the ill, let alone those investigations and clarifications. It contains evidence that its author lacks a firm mastery and complete strength. And among them: al-Mulla Muhyi al-Din Muhammad, known as Khatibzada al-Rumi, studied under his father Taj al-Din, 'Ali al-Tusi, Khidr Bek, and other eminent scholars of his land, became a teacher at one of the eight schools in Constantinople, then Sultan Muhammad Khan appointed him as his personal tutor. He died in the year 901 AH. He authored: 'Hawashi 'ala Hashiyat al-Sayyid al-muta'alliqa bi-Sharh al-Tajrid', 'Hawashi 'ala Hashiyat al-Kashshaf' by al-Sayyid, 'Hawashi 'ala Hashiyat Sharh al-Mukhtasar' by al-Sayyid, 'Risala fi Bahth al-Ru'ya wa al-Kalam', 'Hawashi 'ala Sharh al-Mawaqif', 'Hawashi 'ala al-Muqaddimat al-Arba' min al-Tawdih', and others. He authored a 'Hashiya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya' but did not complete it. So stated in 'al-A'lam' and 'al-Shaqa'iq' ( ). And among them: Muhyi al-Din Muhammad bin Ibrahim bin Husayn al-Naksari al-Rumi, was an expert in the religious sciences and rational arts, and studied under Husam al-Din al-Tawqati, and Yusuf... our teacher... It appears that this statement is from the glosses of Akhi Chalabi on 'al-Dhakhira', but I did not come across it; for these glosses are not written on my copies of 'al-Dhakhira' which I have, both being Indian lithographs. And Allah knows best. (1) 'A'lam al-Akhyar' (Q 383/b). (2) 'al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya' (pp. 90-91).
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the hashiya 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, detailing the lives of commentators on Sharh al-Wiqaya. The author, 'Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, provides corrected attributions and accurate death dates. He first notes a scholar who died in 905 AH (source: Kashf al-Zunun), then discusses Hasan Chalabi al-Fanari (d. 886 AH), a prolific Hanafi scholar who wrote hashias on several key works including al-Talwih, al-Mutawwal, and Tafsir al-Baydawi. Al-Lakhnawi then corrects a widespread error: that 'Dhakirat al-'Uqba' was by Hasan Chalabi. He proves this by noting the death date of Hasan (886 AH) vs completion date of Dhakirat al-'Uqba' (901 AH). Additionally, the preface of Dhakirat al-'Uqba' refers to its author's teacher Mulla Khusraw (a later generation). He further cites authoritative biographical works (Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya, al-Shaqa'iq, Kashf al-Zunun) that attribute Dhakirat al-'Uqba' to Akhi Chalabi Yusuf, not Hasan. He contrasts the quality of Hasan's works (deep investigations) with Dhakirat al-'Uqba' (less rigorous). Then he introduces Khatibzada al-Rumi (d. 901 AH), a scholar who taught at the eight schools of Constantinople and served as tutor to Sultan Muhammad Khan. Khatibzada wrote hashias on many works and began a hashia on Sharh al-Wiqaya but did not complete it. Finally, he begins the biography of Muhyi al-Din al-Naksari, mentioning his teachers. The author notes that a particular gloss (minhawa) from Akhi Chalabi on Dhakirat al-'Uqba' was not available in his copies.

Key Terms
حاشية (hāshiyah): A supercommentary or gloss on a main text, often providing explanation and critical refinement.
شرح الوقاية (Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah): A commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a on al-Wiqaya, a fundamental Hanafi fiqh text.
ذخيرة العقبى (Dhakīrat al-ʿUqbā): A hashia on Sharh al-Wiqaya by Akhi Chalabi Yusuf, often mistakenly attributed to Hasan Chalabi.
أخي جلبي يوسف (Akhi Chalabi Yusuf): Hanafi scholar, author of Dhakirat al-'Uqba on Sharh al-Wiqaya.
ملّا خسرو (Mulla Khusraw): Prominent Hanafi scholar and teacher of both Hasan Chalabi and Akhi Chalabi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Accurate attribution of classical texts requires careful examination of historical dates, internal textual references, and external biographical sources.

Biographies of Hanafi Glossators of Sharh al-Wiqayah
Biographical listing of Hanafi glossators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi scholars who authored glosses on Sharh al-Wiqayah and state their contributions to the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The glosses of these Hanafi scholars form the layered tradition of fiqh commentary.

This passage is a biographical section from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, listing thirteen Hanafi scholars who wrote glosses (hawashi) on Sharh al-Wiqayah. Each entry provides the scholar's name, teachers, key works, and death date, drawn from authoritative sources like al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. Understanding who these scholars are and their relationships helps us appreciate the chain of transmission and the depth of Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage type
Recognize that this is a biographical listing (tarjama) from a later commentary. It is not a legal ruling but a historical record of scholars.
The author is compiling names to document the tradition.
2
Note the scholars' names and death dates
Scan the Arabic text and locate each scholar's name and year of death. This helps place them chronologically.
Death dates range from 891 AH to 954 AH.
3
Identify teachers and students
For each scholar, note who they studied under and who their students were. This shows scholarly chains (isnad).
For example, Husamzada studied under Mulla Khusraw.
4
Recognize key works
Each scholar authored glosses (hawashi) on Sharh al-Wiqayah and often other works. Note the titles to understand their breadth.
Some wrote on Tafsir al-Baydawi or Sharh al-Mawaqif.
5
Understand the significance
These glosses represent later layers of commentary. They are cited in fatwa collections and show the living tradition of Hanafi fiqh.
Ya'qub Pasha's glosses influenced Hasan Jilabi.

The Eighth Section: Biographies of the Glossators of Sharh al-Wiqayah. Bali ibn Muhammad al-Fanari, and Muhammad ibn Armaghan and others, authored 'Tafsir Surat al-Dukhan', and 'Hawashi Sharh al-Wiqayah', and glosses on 'Tafsir al-Baydawi', and his death was in Constantinople, in the year 901 AH. Thus in al-Alam and al-Shaqa'iq. And among them: Yusuf ibn Husayn al-Karmasani; he studied under Khawajazada and other scholars of his time, excelled in the sciences, became a teacher in Constantinople, then a judge in the city of Edirne, and authored 'Hawashi Sharh al-Wiqayah', and 'Hawashi al-Mutawwal', and others, he died around the year 900 AH. Thus in al-Shaqa'iq. And among them: Muhyi al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Ajami, was a virtuous scholar, a teacher in one of the eight madrasas, then a judge in Edirne and died there, authored a 'Risala on the Chapter of the Martyr from Sharh al-Wiqayah', and glosses on 'Sharh al-Sirajiyya' by al-Sayyid. Thus in al-Alam. Thus in al-Alam. And among them: Muhyi al-Din Muhammad Shah ibn Ali ibn Yusuf Bali ibn Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Fanari, studied under his father and under Khatibzada, became a teacher in Bursa, then in Constantinople, then a judge in Constantinople, then in Edirne, then was given the military judgeship in the province of Anatolia, then in the province of Rumelia, and died there while a youth in the year 929 AH. He authored glosses on 'Sharh al-Mawaqif' by al-Sayyid, and on his 'Sharh al-Sirajiyya', and on the beginning of 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'. Thus in al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. 10. Thus in A'lam al-Akhyar. 11. And among them: Muhyi al-Din Jilabi Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Yusuf Bali al-Fanari, read under his father and under Khatibzada, became a teacher at madrasas, and a judge, he has commentaries on 'Sharh al-Miftah' by al-Sayyid, and on al-Hidaya, and on the beginning of 'Sharh al-Wiqayah', and died in the year 954 AH. Thus in al-Alam. 12. Thus in al-Alam. 13. And among them: Ya'qub Pasha ibn Khidr Bek ibn Jalal al-Din al-Rumi, acquired knowledge from his father, became a verifier in the arts, and died while a judge in Constantinople in the year 891 AH. He authored 'Hawashi Sharh al-Wiqayah', wherein he included subtleties and questions with conciseness in expression, and on 'Sharh al-Mawaqif' fine questions, and most of 'Hawashi Hasan Jilabi' are taken from it. Thus in al-Shaqa'iq.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarjama) from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah', listing thirteen Hanafi scholars who authored glosses (hawashi) on 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'. The author provides each scholar's name, teachers, key works, and death dates, drawing from standard biographical sources like 'al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya' and 'Kata'ib A'lam al-Akhyar'. These glosses represent later layers of commentary on the Hanafi legal manual al-Wiqayah, and the scholars cited include figures from the 9th-10th centuries AH. For example, Bali al-Fanari (d. 901) wrote glosses on Sharh al-Wiqayah and Tafsir al-Baydawi; Muhyi al-Din al-Ajami wrote a treatise on the chapter of the martyr; and Ya'qub Pasha (d. 891) authored glosses that later influenced Hasan Jilabi. The passage also notes chains: Husamzada was a student of Mulla Khusraw, Qara Kamal studied under al-Khayali and Mulla Khusraw. This demonstrates the scholarly network and textual tradition of Hanafi fiqh in the Ottoman period.

Key Terms
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): A commentary on the Hanafi legal manual al-Wiqayah authored by Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi.
حواشي (hawashi): Glosses or super-commentaries written on the margins of a primary commentary.

The Scholarly Chain: Biographies of Hashiya Authors on Sharh al-Wiqaya
Biographical listing of Hanafi scholars who authored hashiyas on Sharh al-Wiqaya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of biographical literature in Hanafi fiqh and identify three scholars who wrote hashiyas on Sharh al-Wiqaya.

Core Idea
Biographies establish the scholarly chain that gives a text its authority and interpretive weight.

You have just read a list of scholars who wrote super-commentaries (hāshiyas) on 'Sharh al-Wiqāya', a key Hanafi text. These biographies are not mere historical footnotes; they are the backbone of the madhhab's transmission. Knowing who commented on a text and how they are connected helps you evaluate the strength of different interpretations. In this lesson, we will explore how these biographical entries serve as a tool for legal authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and its commentarial tradition
The passage focuses on 'Sharh al-Wiqāya'. Recognize that this is a commentary itself, and the hāshiyas are super-commentaries. This layered tradition shows the depth of Hanafi scholarship.
The base text al-Wiqāya by al-Marghinānī is a mukhtasar of al-Hidāya.
2
Extract key biographical data from each entry
For each scholar listed (e.g., Sa'dī ibn al-Nājī Bey, Muhyī al-Dīn al-Fanārī), note: name, teachers, positions, death date, and works. This data helps situate the scholar in time and geography.
Pay attention to the sources cited (e.g., 'al-Shaqā'iq al-Nu'māniyya') – they are themselves important biographical works.
3
Analyze the connections between scholars
Notice who studied with whom. For example, Ahmad al-Khayālī studied under Mawlā Khiḍr Bey and later taught others. These networks form the isnād (chain) of the madhhab.
The teacher-student links are crucial for evaluating the reliability of a hashya.
4
Consider the scope of their hashiyas
Some wrote on the entire 'Sharh al-Wiqāya', others on specific chapters (e.g., 'the Chapter of the Martyr'). This tells you which parts of the text were most debated or required clarification.
The mention of 'subtleties and questions' in Ya'qūb Pasha's hashya indicates a critical engagement.
5
Reflect on why this biographical information matters for fiqh
Knowing the author's background helps in weighing their opinions. A scholar who was a judge (qāḍī) might have a practical bent; one who was a teacher might focus on pedagogy.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that fatwā is based on the strongest evidence, but also considers the authority of the muftī.

للوزير محمود باشا: أليس هو الذي كتب «الحواشي على شرح العقائد» وذكر فيها

Thus in 'al-A‘lām'. 12. Thus in 'al-A‘lām'. 13. Among them: Ya‘qūb Pasha ibn Khiḍr Bey ibn Jalāl al-Dīn al-Rūmī, acquired knowledge from his father, became a researcher in the sciences, and died as a judge in Constantinople in the year 891 AH; he composed 'Hāshiyas on Sharh al-Wiqāya' in which he included subtleties and questions with brevity in editing, and 'Subtle Questions on Sharh al-Mawāqif', and most of 'Hāshiyas of Ḥasan Chalabī' are taken from them. Thus in 'al-Shaqā’iq'. 14. Among them: al-Mawlā Aḥmad al-Khayālī, author of the famous 'Hāshiyas on Sharh al-‘Aqā’id al-Nasafiyya', mentioned by the author of 'al-Kashf' among the commentators of 'Sharh al-Wiqāya'. Al-Kafawī said in 'A‘lām al-Akhyār': 'Aḥmad ibn Mūsā known as al-Mawlā al-Khayālī, his father was a judge so he read the fundamentals of the sciences under him. Then he entered the service of al-Mawlā Khiḍr Bey, and he was a teacher at the Sulṭāniyya in Bursa, and became a repetitor for his lessons, and the first repetitor was Khwājazāda, and al-Mawlā Muṣliḥ al-Dīn al-Qasṭallānī and al-Mawlā ‘Alā’ al-Dīn al-‘Arabī were among the attendees of the lesson. Then he became a teacher at some schools, then he moved to the school of Filiba, and he used to receive thirty dirhams daily. Then al-Mawlā Tāj al-Dīn Ibrāhīm known as Ibn al-Khaṭīb, the father of al-Mawlā known as Khaṭībzāda, died at the school of Iznīq, so al-Khayālī was presented for his position. Then Sulṭān Muḥammad Khān said to the vizier Maḥmūd Pasha: 'Is he not the one who wrote the 'Hāshiyas on Sharh al-‘Aqā’id' and mentioned in them...'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of scholars who wrote Hāshiyas (super-commentaries) on 'Sharh al-Wiqāya', a famous Hanafi fiqh work. The author of 'Umdat al-Ri'āya' is providing these biographies to contextualize the scholarly tradition. The entries start with a continuation from a previous page (probably entry 9), then list ten scholars (10–16). Each biography includes the scholar's name, teachers, positions, notable works, and death date. The scholars are Ottoman-era figures: Sa'dī al-Nājī (d. 922), Muhyī al-Dīn al-Fanārī (d. 954), Kamāl al-Dīn al-Qarāmānī (d. after 900?), Ya'qūb Pasha (d. 891), Sinān al-Dīn al-Rūmī, Sinān al-Dīn al-Shā'ir, and finally a detailed entry on Aḥmad al-Khayālī (d. 860?), the famous author of a Hāshiya on 'Sharh al-'Aqā'id al-Nasafiyya'. The passage gives insight into the scholarly network, patronage, and the multi-disciplinary nature of these scholars (fiqh, kalam, literature, astronomy). The Hanafi school's strength in the Ottoman period is evident. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each scholar's contributions and the sources of the information.

Key Terms
حواشي (hawāshī): Super-commentaries or glosses on a base text, here on 'Sharh al-Wiqāya'
المحشون (al-muhashshūn): The commentators who wrote hawāshī
الوقاية (al-Wiqāya): A famous Hanafi fiqh text by Burhān al-Dīn al-Marghinānī (d. 593 AH), often commented upon

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which scholar's hashya on Sharh al-Wiqāya is said to have been used extensively by later commentator Hasan Chalabi?
A) Ya‘qūb Pasha
B) Muhyī al-Dīn al-Fanārī
C) Kamāl al-Dīn al-Qarāmānī
D) Sinān al-Dīn Yūsuf al-Rūmī

Key Takeaway
Biographical entries about Hashiya authors are vital for tracing the chain of interpretation and authority within the Hanafi school.

Life of the Author
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Hashya Scholars and Their Biographical Significance
Biographical dictionary of Hanafi hashya writers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi commentators who wrote marginalia (hawashi) on Sharh al-Wiqaya and explain the significance of their biographical details in establishing scholarly authority.

Core Idea
The hashya literature on Sharh al-Wiqaya is a living chain of Hanafi authority, validated through the piety and learning of its authors.

This eighth study of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents a biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars who wrote glosses on Sharh al-Wiqaya. These scholars are not secondary figures; they are key nodes in the transmission of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding their lives, teachers, and works helps you evaluate the weight of their marginalia and the positions they transmit. The passage provides detailed accounts of al-Khayali, Mulla Khusraw, and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify each scholar and his works
List the scholars mentioned in the passage and note the titles of their commentaries and glosses. This establishes the scope of their scholarly output.
Pay attention to works on both fiqh and other disciplines (Arabic, morphology, astronomy) to see their versatility.
2
Trace the chain of transmission
For each scholar, identify his teachers and students. This shows the scholarly lineage (sanad) that connects the hashya to earlier Hanafi authorities.
For example, al-Khayali studied under Khidr Bek, who was a student of Taftazani, linking him to the broader Hanafi-Maturidi tradition.
3
Analyze biographical anecdotes
Consider why the author includes anecdotes about al-Khayali's asceticism and refusal of a lucrative position. These details reinforce the scholar's piety and independence, adding weight to his legal opinions.
Such anecdotes are common in Hanafi biographical works to establish moral authority.
4
Connect the hashya to its base text
Reflect on how the hashya relates to Sharh al-Wiqaya and to broader Hanafi fiqh. Recognize that these glosses often contain original ijtihad or critical clarifications.
For instance, Mulla Khusraw's glosses on al-Talwih are considered major contributions to usul al-fiqh.
5
Compare scholars for distinctive contributions
Contrast the scholarly profiles of al-Khayali and Mulla Khusraw. Note differences in style (conciseness vs. comprehensiveness), fields of expertise, and lasting impact on the madhhab.
This helps you appreciate the diversity within the Hanafi hashya tradition.

١٧. ومنهم: محمد بن فراموز الشهير بمولى خسرو ، وملا خسرو الرومي، مؤلّف «الغرر في الفقه» وشرحه «الدرر»، و«حواشي التلويح»، و«حواشي المطول»، و«مرقاة الوصول»، وشرحه «مرآة الأصول»، كان بحراً زاخراً، عالماً بالمعقول والمنقول، حاوياً للفروع والأصول، أخذ العلم عن برهان الدين حيدر، السَّعد التَّفْتَازَانِي. وصار مُدَرِّساً، ثمّ قاضياً للعسكر ، وكان أبوه من أمراء الفرسخة، وكان رومي الأصل، ثم أسلم، وكانت له بنت زوجها من أمير يسمى بخسرو، وابنه محمّد هذا كان في حجره، فاشتهر بأخي زوجة خسرو ، ثمّ بمولى ،خسرو، ثمّ غلب عليه خسرو،

(1) من «كتائب أعلام الأخيار (ق) ۱/۳۸۳) ، وينظر : ((الشقائق»(ص٨٥ - ٨٧). (۲) ينظر: «الضوء اللامع (۸) : (۲۷۹)، «الفوائد»(ص۳۰۲ – ۳۰۳).
The eighth study: Biographies of the commentators of Sharh al-Wiqaya. 14. Among them: Sinan al-Din Yusuf al-Rumi. He had skill in literary sciences. He authored a commentary on 'Mirah al-Arwah' in morphology, and 'Sharh al-Shafiyah', and 'Sharh Talkhis al-Jaghmini' in astronomy, and glosses on Sharh al-Wiqaya. As in 'al-Shaqa'iq', on the mention of scholars of the state of Muhammad Khan ibn Murad Khan. 15. Among them: [17 from?] Sinan al-Din Yusuf al-Sha'ir, student of Mulla Khusraw. Mentioned in 'al-Shaqa'iq' as scholars of the era of Bayezid Khan ibn Muhammad Khan. (2) al-Aqa'id: 1. Among them: al-Mulla Ahmad al-Khayali, author of the famous glosses on 'Sharh al-Nasafiyyah', mentioned by the author of 'Kashf' (3) among the commentators of Sharh al-Wiqaya. Al-Kafawi said in 'A'lam al-Akhyar': 'Ahmad ibn Musa, known as al-Mulla al-Khayali; his father was a judge. He read with him the foundations of the sciences. Then he reached the service of al-Mulla Khidr Bek, and was a teacher in Sultaniyya of Bursa, and became a repeater of his lesson, while the first repeater was Khwajah Zada. Al-Mulla Muslih al-Din al-Qastallani and al-Mulla 'Ala' al-Din al-'Arabi were among the students of the lesson. Then he became a teacher at some schools, then moved to the school of Filbah, and he had thirty dirhams per day. Then al-Mulla Taj al-Din Ibrahim, known as Ibn al-Khatib, father of al-Mulla [1] known as Khatib Zada, died at the school of Izniq. Al-Khayali was offered his place. Sultan Muhammad Khan said to the vizier Mahmud Pasha: 'Is he not the one who wrote the glosses on 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id' and mentioned your name in them?' He said: 'Yes, that is correct.' He said: 'He is deserving.' So he gave him the school and assigned him one hundred and thirty dirhams per day. Al-Khayali had prepared for Hajj and came to Constantinople. The vizier Mahmud Pasha informed him, and insisted on his acceptance of the said school. He said: 'If you give me your vizierate, and the sultan his sultanate, I will not abandon this journey.' So he went and became a teacher there after he returned. He remained only two years until he died in the early sixties and eight hundred [AH], and he was thirty-three years old. He was engaged in knowledge and worship, never separating from them for an hour. He used to eat once every day and night, contenting himself with little, and he was extremely thin, so much so that it is related that his index finger and thumb could enter his hand until reaching his upper arm. He has glosses on 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah' by al-Taftazani, in which he followed a path of conciseness and enigmas, and produced marvels approaching the rank of inimitability. He also has glosses on the beginnings of 'Hashiyat al-Tajrid', and 'Sharh Nazm al-'Aqa'id' by his teacher Khidr Bek. End. (1) Student. 17. Among them: Muhammad ibn Faramuz, known as Mulla Khusraw, and Mulla Khusraw al-Rumi, author of 'al-Ghurar' in fiqh and its commentary 'al-Durar', and 'Hawashi al-Talwih', and 'Hawashi al-Mutawwal', and 'Mirqat al-Wusul', and its commentary 'Mir'at al-Usul'. He was a vast ocean, learned in intellectual and transmitted sciences, encompassing branches and fundamentals. He acquired knowledge from Burhan al-Din Haydar, al-Sa'd al-Taftazani. He became a teacher, then a military judge. His father was among the commanders of the Parsakha, and was of Rumi origin, then converted to Islam. He had a daughter whom he married to an amir named Khusraw, and his son Muhammad was under his guardianship, so he became known as brother-in-law of Khusraw, then as Mulla Khusraw, then Khusraw became dominant. (2) His death was in the year 885 AH in Constantinople. As in 'al-A'lam' and others. 18. Among them: al-Mulla Muhammad ibn Muhammad, known as 'Arab Zada al-Rumi. He was among the greats of his time, and the most eminent of his age, a master of verification and precision. He became a teacher in the city of Bursa, then at the school of Mahmud Pasha in Constantinople, then at one of the eight schools there, then at the Suleymaniye School. Then he was appointed to the judgeship of Cairo, and his judgeship was such. He sailed the sea at an inappropriate time in a time (1) from 'Kata'ib A'lam al-Akhyar' (folio 1/383), and see: 'al-Shaqa'iq' (pp. 85-87). (2) See: 'al-Daw' al-Lami' (8): (279), 'al-Fawa'id' (pp. 302-303).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a biographical compilation from the eighth study of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, listing Hanafi scholars who wrote marginal commentaries (hawashi) on Sharh al-Wiqayah, a major Hanafi fiqh text. The author provides brief biographies of several scholars, including Sinan al-Din Yusuf al-Rumi (known for literary sciences), Sinan al-Din Yusuf al-Sha'ir (student of Mulla Khusraw), and a detailed account of al-Mulla Ahmad al-Khayali (famous for his glosses on Sharh al-'Aqa'id). The biography of al-Khayali is particularly rich, describing his pursuit of knowledge, his appointment as a teacher with a daily stipend of 130 dirhams, his asceticism, and his scholarly output. Then follow biographies of Mulla Khusraw (Muhammad ibn Faramuz), the celebrated Hanafi jurist and author of al-Ghurar and al-Durar, and 'Arab Zada al-Rumi, a judge and teacher. These biographies serve to establish the scholarly authority and transmission chain of the hashya literature on Sharh al-Wiqayah, underscoring the interconnectedness of Hanafi scholarship across generations and regions.

Key Terms
حواشي (hawāshī): Marginal commentaries or glosses written on a primary text, in this case on Sharh al-Wiqaya and other works.

Biography of al-Khiyali: A Hanafi Scholar and Glossator
Biographical entry of a Hanafi scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly profile of al-Khiyali and identify his contributions to Hanafi learning.

Core Idea
Al-Khiyali's dedication to learning and worship produced concise yet profound glosses that shape Hanafi theological discourse.

This passage introduces us to the life of al-Khiyali, a 9th-century Hanafi scholar whose glosses (hawashi) on key theological works remain influential. His story—from refusing a lucrative teaching post to his intense asceticism—illuminates the values of scholarship and piety in the Hanafi tradition. Understanding his works helps us trace how later scholars refined and transmitted core doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Identify key life events
Read the passage and note the major events: his refusal of a teaching post to perform Hajj, his later acceptance, his short tenure, and his early death.
Focus on the timeline and the decision-making process.
2
Examine personal qualities
Look for descriptions of his character: constant engagement in learning and worship, eating once daily, extreme thinness.
These details highlight his asceticism, but remember this is personal piety, not a legal requirement.
3
List his major works
Identify the three works mentioned: glosses on Taftazani's Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya, glosses on al-Tajrid, and a commentary on his teacher's Nazm al-Aqa'id.
These are all theological commentaries, showing his specialty in 'ilm al-kalam.
4
Understand the significance of his glosses
The passage notes his style: concise and puzzle-like, achieving marvels near inimitability. This reflects the Hanafi tradition of dense, precise commentary.
His hashiah is a supercommentary, refining and defending positions within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : نعم هو كذلك ، قال : إنه مستحق، فأعطاه المدرسة، وعين له كل يوم مئةً وثلاثين درهماً، وكان الخيالي تهيّأ للحج فجاء قسطنطينية، فأعلمه الوزير محمود باشا، فأبرم عليه قبول المدرسة المزبورة ، فقال : إن أعطيتني وزارتك، والسلطان سلطنته، لا أترك هذا السفر، فذهب وصار مدرساً بها بعدما رجع ، ولم يثبت إلا سنتين حتى مات في أوائل عشر الستين وثمانمئة ، وكان سنه ثلاثاً وثلاثين سنة. وكان مشتغلاً بالعلم والعبادة، لا ينفك عنهما ساعة، وكان يأكلُ في كلِّ يومٍ وليلة مرة واحدة، ويكتفي بالأقل، وكان نحيفاً في الغاية، حتى روي أنه كان سبابته وإبهامه يدخل فيها يده إلى أن ينتهي إلى عضده، وله حواش على «شرح العقائد النسفية للتفتازاني» سلك فيها مسلك الإيجاز والألغاز وأتى ببدائع تقرب رتبة الإعجاز، وله حواش على أوائل حاشية التجريد»، وله : «شرح نظم العقائد» لأستاذه خضر بيك». انتهى (1) تلميذ
He said: Yes, it is so. He said: He is entitled. So he gave him the school and appointed for him daily one hundred and thirty dirhams. Al-Khiyali had prepared for Hajj and came to Constantinople. The minister Mahmud Pasha informed him, so he confirmed upon him acceptance of the aforementioned school. He said: If you give me your ministry and the Sultan his sultanate, I will not abandon this journey. So he went and became a teacher there after he returned. He did not remain except two years until he died in the beginning of the sixties and eight hundred [AH], and his age was thirty-three years. He was occupied with knowledge and worship, never free from them for an hour. He used to eat once every day and night and suffice with the least. He was extremely thin, such that it was narrated that his forefinger and thumb would enter his hand until reaching his upper arm. He has glosses on 'Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya li-l-Taftazani' in which he followed a path of conciseness and puzzles, producing marvels nearing the rank of inimitability. He has glosses on the beginning of 'Hashiyat al-Tajrid', and he has 'Sharh Nazm al-Aqa'id' by his teacher Khidr Bey. Ended. (1) Student.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry detailing the life and scholarly output of al-Khiyali, a Hanafi scholar. It begins by recounting an incident where he was offered a teaching post with a generous stipend but declined it in favor of performing Hajj. His dedication to learning and worship is highlighted: he ate only once a day, was extremely thin, and continuously engaged in scholarship. His chief works are listed: glosses on al-Taftazani's commentary on al-Nasafi's creed, glosses on al-Tajrid, and a commentary on his teacher's poetic work on creed. The footnote 'Tilmīdh' indicates the source of this information.

Key Terms
الخيالي (al-Khiyali): A Hanafi scholar and commentator, known for his glosses on theological works, active in the 9th century AH.
حاشية (hāshiyah): A supercommentary or gloss; in this context, a critical commentary on a pre-existing work.

The Life and Legacy of Mullā Khusraw
Biographical entry of the renowned Hanafi jurist Mullā Khusraw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Mullā Khusraw, identify his major works, and explain the significance of his scholarly contributions in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Mullā Khusraw's works remain foundational in Hanafi jurisprudence and usul al-fiqh.

In this lesson, we explore the life of Muhammad bin Framuz, known as Mullā Khusraw, one of the towering Hanafi jurists of the 9th century AH. His writings, especially al-Ghurur and al-Durar, continue to be studied in traditional seminaries. Understanding his background helps us appreciate the authority of his texts in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The author introduces Mullā Khusraw by his full name and title. Note the terms 'Mawla Khusraw' and 'Mulla Khusraw al-Rumi' to distinguish him from other scholars.
He is not to be confused with other 'Khusraws' in Islamic history.
2
List his major works
Extract the titles of his authored books: al-Ghurur fi al-Fiqh, al-Durar (commentary), Hawashi al-Talwih, Hawashi al-Mutawwal, Mirqat al-Wusul, and its commentary Mir'at al-Usul. Recognize which ones are in fiqh and which in usul.
Al-Ghurur and al-Durar are the core fiqh texts; the others are in usul and other sciences.
3
Trace his scholarly lineage and career
He studied under Burhan al-Din Haydar and Sa'd al-Taftazani. He became a teacher and later a military judge (qadi al-askar). This shows he was both a scholar and a practicing jurist.
His military judgeship reflects the Ottoman practice of appointing scholars to judicial roles.
4
Understand his name's origin
The text explains how 'Mawla Khusraw' came about: his sister gave birth to a son who was raised by him, and he became known as brother-in-law of amir Khusraw, then 'Mawla Khusraw', and eventually just 'Khusraw'.
The evolution of his title shows the social context of Ottoman scholarly naming.
5
Note his death and legacy
He died in 885 AH in Constantinople. His works remain authoritative in the Hanafi school, especially for beginners in fiqh.
His fatwa and teaching have influenced later Hanafi scholarship extensively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
17. ومنهم: محمد بن فراموز الشهير بمولى خسرو ، وملا خسرو الرومي، مؤلّف «الغرر في الفقه» وشرحه «الدرر»، و«حواشي التلويح»، و«حواشي المطول»، و«مرقاة الوصول»، وشرحه «مرآة الأصول»، كان بحراً زاخراً، عالماً بالمعقول والمنقول، حاوياً للفروع والأصول، أخذ العلم عن برهان الدين حيدر، السَّعد التَّفْتَازَانِي. وصار مُدَرِّساً، ثمّ قاضياً للعسكر ، وكان أبوه من أمراء الفرسخة، وكان رومي الأصل، ثم أسلم، وكانت له بنت زوجها من أمير يسمى بخسرو، وابنه محمّد هذا كان في حجره، فاشتهر بأخي زوجة خسرو ، ثمّ بمولى ،خسرو، ثمّ غلب عليه خسرو، (۲) وكانت وفاته سنة خمس وثمانين وثمانمئة بقسطنطينية (٢). كذا في «الأعلام»، وغيره.
17. Among them: Muhammad bin Framuz, famous as Mawla Khusraw, and Mulla Khusraw al-Rumi, author of 'al-Ghurur fi al-Fiqh' and its commentary 'al-Durar', and 'Hawashi al-Talwih', and 'Hawashi al-Mutawwal', and 'Mirqat al-Wusul', and its commentary 'Mir'at al-Usul'. He was a vast sea, knowledgeable in rational and transmitted sciences, comprehensive in branches and principles. He acquired knowledge from Burhan al-Din Haydar, Sa'd al-Taftazani. He became a teacher, then a military judge. His father was among the commanders of the feudal levy and was of Rumi origin, then embraced Islam. He had a daughter whom he married to an amir named Khusraw, and his son Muhammad was under his guardianship, so he became known as brother-in-law of Khusraw, then as Mawla Khusraw, then Khusraw prevailed. (2) His death was in the year 885 AH in Constantinople. Thus in 'al-A'lam' and others.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage introduces Muhammad bin Framuz, famously known as Mullā Khusraw, a paramount Hanafi jurist of the 9th century AH. His major works include 'al-Ghurur fi al-Fiqh' and its commentary 'al-Durar', which became standard texts in Hanafi fiqh. He also wrote glosses on 'al-Talwih' (a work on usul al-fiqh) and 'al-Mutawwal' (rhetoric), as well as a work on usul al-fiqh 'Mirqat al-Wusul' with its commentary. His scholarly lineage includes studying under Burhan al-Din Haydar and Sa'd al-Taftazani. His career spanned teaching and serving as a military judge. The text explains how he acquired the name 'Mawla Khusraw' through his family connection to an amir named Khusraw.

Key Terms
مولى خسرو (Mawla Khusraw): Title of Muhammad bin Framuz, a Hanafi jurist; 'Mawla' indicates scholarly rank, and 'Khusraw' is an honorific derived from his relation to an amir.
الغرر في الفقه (al-Ghurur fi al-Fiqh): One of Mullā Khusraw's major works on Hanafi fiqh, summarized by his own commentary 'al-Durar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Biography of Arabzāda al-Rūmī: Scholar and Martyr
Biographical entry of a Hanafi scholar and judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key facts of Arabzāda's life and identify his contributions to Hanafi fiqh scholarship.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's life and martyrdom exemplify the tradition's scholarly chain.

This lesson introduces you to al-Mawlā Muhammad ibn Muhammad, known as Arabzāda al-Rūmī, a distinguished Hanafi scholar and judge from the Ottoman period. His biography illustrates the career path of a top-tier scholar: teaching at prestigious madrasas, serving as qadi, and authoring extensive glosses on core Hanafi texts. His death at sea is recorded as martyrdom (shahāda). Understanding his contributions helps appreciate the later layers of Hanafi commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and epithet
Locate his name: Muhammad ibn Muhammad, known as Arabzāda al-Rūmī. Note that 'Arabzāda' means 'son of an Arab' and 'al-Rūmī' indicates his Ottoman origin.
2
Trace his academic career
Follow his teaching posts: from Bursa to Mahmud Pasha school in Constantinople, then one of the eight schools, and finally the prestigious Suleymaniyya madrasa.
3
Note his judgeship and death
He was appointed qadi of Cairo but died on the voyage when his ship sank in a storm; the text calls him a martyr.
4
List his major works
He wrote glosses (hawāshī) on Sharh al-Wiqāya, al-Hidāya, al-‘Ināya, Fath al-Qadīr, and on rhetorical works like Sharh al-Miftāh and al-Mutawwal.
These are important later Hanafi commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
18. ومنهم : المولى محمد بن محمد الشهير بعرب زاده الرومي، كان من فحول عصره، وأكابر دهره، صاحب تحقيق وتدقيق، صار مدرساً بمدينة بروسا، ثمّ بمدرسة محمود باشا بقسطنطينية، ثمّ بإحدى المدارس الثمان بها، ثمّ بالمدرسة السليمانية. ثمّ قلّد قضاء القاهرة، وكان فيه قضاؤه ، فركب البحر في غير أوانه في زمان عتوه وطغيانه، فتلاطمت أمواجه وانكسرت سفینته فمات شهيدا، وكان ذلك سنة تسع وستين وتسعمئة ، وقد مضى من عمره (خمسون) سنة. له: «حاشية على شرح الوقاية»، وعلى «الهداية»، وعلى شرحها «العناية»، وعلى «فتح القدير»، وعلى شرح المفتاح للسيد ، وعلى المطوّل» وغير ذلك. كذا في العقد المنظوم في ذكر أفاضل الروم».
18. Among them: al-Mawla Muhammad bin Muhammad, famous as Arabzada al-Rumi. He was among the colossi of his age and the greats of his time, a master of verification and precision. He became a teacher in the city of Bursa, then at the school of Mahmud Pasha in Constantinople, then at one of the eight schools there, then at the Suleymaniyya school. Then he was appointed to the judgeship of Cairo, and his judgeship was there. He boarded the sea at an inopportune time, in a period of its rebellion and tyranny. Its waves surged, his ship broke, and he died a martyr. That was in the year 969 AH, and he had lived fifty years. He wrote: gloss on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya', and on 'al-Hidayah', and on its commentary 'al-Inayah', and on 'Fath al-Qadir', and on 'Sharh al-Mifta' li-l-Sayyid', and on 'al-Mutawwal', and others. Thus in 'al-‘Iqd al-Manzum fi Dhikr Afadil al-Rum'.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents the biography of Muhammad bin Muhammad, known as Arabzada al-Rumi, a distinguished Hanafi scholar of the 10th century AH. He taught at prominent institutions in Bursa and Constantinople, including the Suleymaniyya. Later he was appointed qadi of Cairo. His death is described as a martyrdom when his ship sank during a storm at sea. His scholarly output includes valuable glosses on key Hanafi fiqh works: 'Sharh al-Wiqaya', 'al-Hidayah', 'al-Inayah', 'Fath al-Qadir', as well as on rhetorical works. The source cited is al-‘Iqd al-Manzum.

Key Terms
عرب زاده (Arabzāda): A title meaning 'son of an Arab'; here it is the sobriquet of a Hanafi scholar from the Ottoman lands.
حاشية على شرح الوقاية (Hāshiyah 'alā Sharh al-Wiqāyah): A gloss on the commentary of al-Wiqayah, a central Hanafi fiqh work.

Biography of Tāj al-Dīn Ibrāhīm al-Humaydī
Biographical entry of a Hanafī scholar and his works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key contributions of al-Humaydi and explain the nature of his refutation of Ibn Kamal Pasha within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Scholarly refutation within the same madhhab reflects healthy ijtihad and the evolution of Hanafi thought.

Biographical entries in Hanafi texts are not mere records; they situate scholars within the chain of transmission and reveal the dynamic debates that shaped later jurisprudence. This lesson introduces Tāj al-Dīn Ibrāhīm al-Humaydī, a 10th-century Hanafi scholar known for his gloss on Sharḥ al-Wiqāya, in which he systematically responded to objections raised by the renowned Ibn Kamāl Pāshā. Understanding al-Humaydī's life and works helps us appreciate the culture of critical engagement within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Locate al-Humaydī's full name, nisba, and birth/death periods. Note his connection to his hometown Humayd and his migration to Constantinople.
The nisba 'al-Humaydī' indicates his origin; such attributions are common in biographical dictionaries.
2
Trace his educational journey
List the teachers he studied under (e.g., al-Mawlā Nūr al-Dīn) and the sequence of madrasas where he taught. This shows the typical scholarly path of the time.
His teaching posts reflect the Ottoman patronage of Hanafi learning.
3
Identify his major works
Name the three works mentioned: the gloss on Sharḥ al-Wiqāya, the gloss on Sharḥ al-Miftāḥ, and Sharḥ al-Marāḥ. Note their genres: two are ḥawāshī (glosses) and one is a commentary on a morphological text.
Glosses were common vehicles for engaging with earlier authoritative texts.
4
Understand the nature of his refutation
Analyze the text's description of his response to Ibn Kamāl Pāshā: he collected sixteen points of refutation and used strong language. Recognize this as an intra-madhhab debate, not a sectarian conflict.
Both scholars are Hanafī; such debates aim to refine positions, not reject the madhhab.
5
Relate to Hanafī tradition
Contextualize al-Humaydī's works within the later Hanafī tradition of supercommentary (ḥawāshī). His gloss on Sharḥ al-Wiqāya is part of a chain of commentaries on al-Marghīnānī's al-Hidāyah.
These works are essential for understanding the development of post-classical Hanafī fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
19. ومنهم : المولى تاج الدين إبراهيم بن عبيد الله الحميدي، نسبة إلى بلده حميد، دخل قسطنطينية، وتوطن بها، واشتهرت فضائله فيها، ألف «حاشية على شرح الوقاية أجاب فيها عن إيرادات ابن كمال باشا وكانت وفاته سنة ثلاث وسبعين وتسعمئة. كذا ذكره المحبي في «خلاصة الأثر»(۳) في ترجمة ابنه حيدر، وصاحب كشف الظنون (٤) وذكر صاحب «العقد المنظوم» له ترجمة حسنة ، ملخصها : «إنّه ولد على رأس تسعمئة ، في ولايه حميد، وخرج منها لطلب العلم، وأخذ العلم عن المولى نور الدين وغيره، ودرس بمدرسة إبراهيم الروّاس بقسطنطينية، ثمّ بمدرسة قصبة بلونه، ثمّ بمدرسة القاضي الأسود، ثم بمدرسة سليمان باشا بأزنيق. وكتب فيها «حاشية على شرح الوقاية»، وردّ فيها على ابن كمال، فلما انفصل تلك المدرسة كتب رسالة وجمع فيها من مواضع رده عليه ستة عشر موضعاً، عن وأغلظ عليه القول ، وله أيضاً «حاشية على بعض المواضع من شرح المفتاح» للسيد، ردّ في فيها على ابن كمال باشا ، وله «شرح المراح» في الصرف.
19. Among them: al-Mawla Taj al-Din Ibrahim bin Ubayd Allah al-Humaydi, attributed to his hometown Humayd. He entered Constantinople, settled there, and his virtues became famous. He authored a 'Gloss on Sharh al-Wiqaya' in which he answered the objections of Ibn Kamal Pasha. His death was in 973 AH. Thus al-Muhibbi mentioned it in 'Khulasat al-Athar' (3) in his biography of his son Haydar, and the author of 'Kashf al-Zunun' (4). The author of 'al-‘Iqd al-Manzum' provided a good biography, summarized: He was born at the beginning of 900 AH in the province of Humayd, left it seeking knowledge, studied under al-Mawla Nur al-Din and others, taught at the school of Ibrahim al-Rawwas in Constantinople, then at the school of the town of Bolu, then at the school of al-Qadi al-Aswad, then at the school of Sulayman Pasha in Iznik. And in it (Iznik) he wrote the 'Gloss on Sharh al-Wiqaya' and refuted Ibn Kamal therein. When he left that school, he wrote a treatise and collected sixteen places where he refuted him, and he reprimanded him and used harsh words. He also has a 'Gloss on some passages from Sharh al-Miftah' by al-Sayyid, in which he refuted Ibn Kamal Pasha, and he has 'Sharh al-Mirah' on morphology.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This entry details the life of Taj al-Din Ibrahim al-Humaydi, a Hanafi scholar from Humayd. He settled in Constantinople and taught at various madrasas. His most noted work is a gloss on 'Sharh al-Wiqaya' that specifically refutes criticisms made by Ibn Kamal Pasha (another prominent Hanafi scholar). The rivalry is evident: he later compiled a treatise listing sixteen points of refutation and used strong language. He also wrote glosses on al-Sayyid al-Sharif's 'Sharh al-Miftah' and a commentary on 'al-Marah' in morphology.

Key Terms
ابن كمال باشا (Ibn Kamāl Pāshā): A famous Hanafi scholar (d. 940 AH) whose views al-Humaydi refuted in his gloss.
حاشية على شرح الوقاية (Hāshiyah 'alā Sharh al-Wiqāyah): A gloss on the commentary of al-Wiqayah, here specifically answering Ibn Kamal's objections.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To summarize the text
B) To refute Ibn Kamal Pasha's objections
C) To translate the text into Turkish
D) To compare madhhabs

Key Takeaway
Al-Humaydi's life and works illustrate the dynamic and self-critical nature of Hanafi scholarship, where later scholars rigorously debated earlier authorities to refine the madhhab.

The Life and Works of Tāj al-Dīn al-Ḥumaydī
Biographical entry of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key contributions of Tāj al-Dīn al-Ḥumaydī and explain how his ḥāshiyah defended Hanafi fiqh against Ibn Kamāl Pasha's objections.

Core Idea
Scholar biography reveals the living chain of Hanafi transmission and the role of glosses in defending the madhhab.

This lesson introduces Tāj al-Dīn al-Ḥumaydī, a 16th-century Hanafi scholar active in the Ottoman Empire. His life illustrates the scholarly ethos of the time: intense engagement with core texts and respectful yet firm refutation of opposing views. Through his biography, we see how ḥāshiyah works functioned as both commentary and defense, ensuring the continuity of the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his context
Note his birthplace, lineage, migration to Constantinople, and the key figures in his education.
He was born around 900 AH in Ḥumayd and studied under Mawlā Nūr al-Dīn.
2
Trace his teaching career
List the madrasas where he taught, in chronological order, and observe the progression in salary and prestige.
Salaries increased from 25 to 100 dirhams, and he eventually joined one of the eight elite schools.
3
Identify his major work and its purpose
Locate the statement about his gloss on Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah and understand that it was written to answer Ibn Kamāl Pasha's objections.
The text explicitly states: 'ألف حاشية على شرح الوقاية أجاب فيها عن إيرادات ابن كمال باشا'.
4
Note his broader contributions
List his other writings: glosses on Sharḥ al-Miftāḥ and Sharḥ al-Mawāqif, a treatise gathering his refutations, and Turkish poetry.
He also translated Persian books into Turkish for Sultan Sulaymān.
5
Reflect on the significance of intra-Hanafi debate
Consider why a Hanafi scholar would refute another Hanafi scholar (Ibn Kamāl) and how this reflects the tradition's internal dynamism.
The separate treatise on sixteen points shows systematic scholarly critique.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۹. ومنهم : المولى تاج الدين إبراهيم بن عبيد الله الحميدي، نسبة إلى بلده حميد، دخل قسطنطينية، وتوطن بها، واشتهرت فضائله فيها، ألف «حاشية على شرح الوقاية أجاب فيها عن إيرادات ابن كمال باشا وكانت وفاته سنة ثلاث وسبعين وتسعمئة. كذا ذكره المحبي في «خلاصة الأثر»(۳) في ترجمة ابنه حيدر، وصاحب كشف الظنون (٤) وذكر صاحب «العقد المنظوم» له ترجمة حسنة ، ملخصها : «إنّه ولد على رأس تسعمئة ، في ولايه حميد، وخرج منها لطلب العلم، وأخذ العلم عن المولى نور الدين وغيره، ودرس بمدرسة إبراهيم الروّاس بقسطنطينية، ثمّ بمدرسة قصبة بلونه، ثمّ بمدرسة القاضي الأسود، ثم بمدرسة سليمان باشا بأزنيق. وكتب فيها «حاشية على شرح الوقاية»، وردّ فيها على ابن كمال، فلما انفصل تلك المدرسة كتب رسالة وجمع فيها من مواضع رده عليه ستة عشر موضعاً، عن وأغلظ عليه القول ، وله أيضاً «حاشية على بعض المواضع من شرح المفتاح» للسيد، ردّ فيها على ابن كمال باشا ، وله «شرح المراح» في الصرف.
وفي «العقد المنظوم في ذكر أفاضل الروم»: «كان أبوه من كبار زمـرة القضاة الحاكمين في القصبات، ونشأ مشغوفاً بالعلم وأربابه ، ومعجباً بالـفـضـل وأصحابه، فاهتم في التحصيل، ورغب في التكميل، وتشرف بمجالس السادة. وكان منه ما كان حتى صار ملازماً من المولى خير الدين، معلم السلطان سليمان. ثم درس في المدرسة السراجية بأدرنة بخمسة وعشرين، ثم بمدرسة مراد باشا بقسطنطينية بثلاثين، ثم بمدرسة محمود باشا بهذه المدينة بأربعين ، ثم صار وظيفته فيها خمسين، ثمّ ساعده الدهر وأعانه الزمان حيث وصل إلى إحدى المدارس الثمان بمهمة إياس باشا الوزير الكبير بتقدير العزيز القدير، ثمّ صار مأموراً من قبل السلطان سليمان بترجمة بعض الكتب الفارسيّة بالتركيّة، فأتمها في قليل من الزمان، فأعطاه مدرسة السلطان بایزید خان. ثمّ قلّد قضاء حلب، ثم عزل عنه ، وفوّض إليه تفتيش أحوال القاهرة ، فأصبحت بكمال استقامته عامرة، ثمّ قلّد قضاء دمشق الشام ، ثم نقل إلى قضاء . ذات الأهرام، ثم وجه إليه مدرسة أبي أيوب الأنصاري الله بمئة درهم، فعما قليل عيناه])، فتقاعد بوظيفته المزبورة. فلَمّا وصل العمر إلى حدود الثمانين» أباده الزمان، وأبلاه الدهر الخوان، وذلك سنة ثلاث وسبعين وتسعمئة ، وقد كتب حواش على شرح المواقف»، وعلى «شرح الوقاية لصدر الشريعة، وعلى شرح المفتاح للجرجاني، وله ديوان شعر بالتركي». انتهى كلامه (۲).
19. Among them: al-Mawlā Tāj al-Dīn Ibrāhīm ibn 'Ubayd Allāh al-Ḥumaydī, attributed to his town Ḥumayd. He entered Constantinople, settled there, and his virtues became famous there. He authored a 'Gloss on the Commentary on al-Wiqāyah' in which he answered the objections of Ibn Kamāl Pasha. His death was in the year 973 AH. This is how al-Muḥibbī mentioned him in 'Khuāṣat al-Athar' in the biography of his son Ḥaydar, and the author of 'Kashf al-Ẓunūn'. And the author of 'al-'Aqd al-Manẓūm' gave him a good biography, summarized: 'He was born around 900 AH, in the province of Ḥumayd, left it seeking knowledge, took knowledge from al-Mawlā Nūr al-Dīn and others, taught at the school of Ibrāhīm al-Rawwās in Constantinople, then at the school of Qaṣabah Balūnah, then at the school of al-Qāḍī al-Aswad, then at the school of Sulaymān Pasha in Izniq. He wrote there a 'Gloss on the Commentary on al-Wiqāyah', and refuted Ibn Kamāl in it. When he left that school, he wrote a treatise and gathered in it sixteen places where he had refuted him, and was harsh in his speech. He also has a 'Gloss on some passages of al-Miftāḥ' by al-Sayyid, in which he refuted Ibn Kamāl Pasha, and he has a 'Commentary on al-Marāḥ' in ṣarf.' And in 'al-'Aqd al-Manẓūm fī Dhikr Afāḍil al-Rūm': 'His father was among the great group of judging judges in the towns. He grew up passionate about knowledge and its people, admiring virtue and its companions. He strove in acquisition, desired completion, and honored the gatherings of nobles. He became what he became until he became a constant companion of al-Mawlā Khayr al-Dīn, teacher of Sultan Sulaymān. Then he taught at the Sirājiyya school in Edirne with twenty-five [dirhams?], then at the school of Murād Pasha in Constantinople with thirty, then at the school of Maḥmūd Pasha in this city with forty, then his position there became fifty, then time helped him and fortune aided him until he reached one of the eight schools via the mission of Ilyās Pasha the grand vizier by the decree of the Mighty and Powerful. Then he was appointed by Sultan Sulaymān to translate some Persian books into Turkish, and completed them in a short time, so he was given the school of Sultan Bāyazīd Khān. Then he was appointed judge of Aleppo, then dismissed, and entrusted with inspection of the affairs of Cairo, so it became prosperous by his perfect rectitude. Then he was appointed judge of Damascus, then transferred to the judgeship of Dhāt al-Ahrām (Egypt), then he was assigned the school of Abū Ayyūb al-Anṣārī with one hundred dirhams, and shortly his eyes [؟], so he retired with his mentioned position. When his age reached about eighty, time destroyed him and the treacherous time wore him out, and that was in the year 973 AH. He wrote glosses on 'Sharḥ al-Mawāqif', and on 'Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah' of Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah, and on 'Sharḥ al-Miftāḥ' of al-Jurjānī, and he has a collection of poetry in Turkish.' End of his words (2).
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This is a biographical entry presenting the life and works of Tāj al-Dīn Ibrāhīm al-Ḥumaydī, a Hanafi scholar from the 16th century CE (10th century AH). The passage opens by identifying his lineage and hometown (Ḥumayd). It highlights his migration to Constantinople (Istanbul), where he gained fame for his virtues. His most notable work is a gloss (ḥāshiyah) on ‘Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah’, written specifically to refute the objections raised by the prominent Ottoman scholar Ibn Kamāl Pasha. The author then cites two sources: al-Muḥibbī’s ‘Khuāṣat al-Athar’ and ‘Kashf al-Ẓunūn’ by Ḥājjī Khalīfah. A longer quotation from ‘al-‘Aqd al-Manẓūm fī Dhikr Afāḍil al-Rūm’ provides a detailed biography. It notes his birth around 900 AH, his early education under Mawlā Nūr al-Dīn, and his teaching positions at several madrasas in Istanbul, Bursa, and Izniq. During his tenure at one school, he wrote the ḥāshiyah on ‘Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah’. After leaving that post, he compiled a separate treatise cataloguing sixteen points of refutation against Ibn Kamāl. He also wrote a gloss on ‘Sharḥ al-Miftāḥ’ by al-Sayyid al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī. The extract continues with details of his father’s status, his own career advancement, and his appointment as judge in major cities (Aleppo, Damascus, Cairo). He also served as a translator for Sultan Sulaymān. The biography concludes with a list of his additional works: glosses on ‘Sharḥ al-Mawāqif’ (theology), ‘Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah’ by Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah, ‘Sharḥ al-Miftāḥ’ by al-Jurjānī, and a Turkish poetry collection. He died in 973 AH. The entry illustrates the scholarly environment of the Ottoman Empire, where gloss-writing was a key means of engaging with earlier Hanafi texts and defending the school against contemporary challenges.

Key Terms
حاشية (ḥāshiyah): A gloss or supercommentary, here specifically a commentary on ‘Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah’ that engages critically with Ibn Kamāl’s objections.
شرح الوقاية (Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah): A commentary by Ṣadr al-Sharī'ah on the Hanafi fiqh manual ‘al-Wiqāyah’ by Tāj al-Sharī'ah, a standard text in the Ottoman curriculum.
العقد المنظوم (al-‘Aqd al-Manẓūm): A biographical work by ‘Alī ibn Bālī (Manq) about distinguished scholars of the Ottoman Empire, used as a source for the biography.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tāj al-Dīn al-Ḥumaydī's biography exemplifies the living tradition of ḥāshiyah writing in the Hanafi school, where scholars actively defended core texts through rigorous commentary.
