Understanding Biographical Cross-References in Hanafi Commentaries
Brief biographical cross-reference in a commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of a cross-referential biographical note in a Hanafi commentary and explain its significance for the transmission of the school's authoritative texts.

Core Idea
Biographical cross-references link scholars to texts, showing the chain of commentary tradition.

In Hanafi commentaries, brief notes like this one serve as pointers, reminding readers that a scholar's full biography was given earlier. This passage introduces Muṣliḥ al-Dīn al-Qūjāwī (Shaykh Zādah) as one of the commentators on al-Wiqāyah. Understanding these references helps you navigate the dense network of scholars and texts that form the backbone of Hanafi learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar and His Epithet
Find the proper name and the famous title (Shaykh Zādah). This is how the scholar is commonly known in the tradition.
Shaykh Zādah means 'son of a shaykh' — a common honorific.
2
Note the Text He Commented On
The note mentions that he is among the 'shurrāḥ al-Wiqāyah'. Determine which text this refers to and its importance in the Hanafi curriculum.
Al-Wiqāyah is a core matn in Hanafi fiqh written by Tāj al-Sharī'ah.
3
Understand the Cross-Reference
The text says 'his mention has already passed in the previous study'. Recognize that this is not a full biography but a redirection.
Commentators often avoid repeating information, assuming the reader has seen earlier sections.
4
Recognize the Significance
Realize that such notes map the scholarly network. They show who contributed to explaining and transmitting a key text.
Commentaries on al-Wiqāyah are numerous; each commentator adds layers of interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۱. ومنهم : مصلح الدين القوجوي، المعروف بشيخ زاده ، وقد مرّ ذكره في الدراسة السابقة، عند ذكر شراح «الوقاية».
21. Among them: Muṣliḥ al-Dīn al-Qūjāwī, known as Shaykh Zādah, and his mention has already passed in the previous study, when discussing the commentators of al-Wiqāyah.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This is a short biographical entry that simply notes the existence of Muṣliḥ al-Dīn al-Qūjāwī, commonly known as Shaykh Zādah, as one of the commentators on al-Wiqāyah. The text tells us that he was already mentioned earlier in the book (in the previous study of commentators). This entry serves as a cross-reference, perhaps to avoid repeating his full biography. The reader is directed to that earlier section for more details. Shaykh Zādah is a well-known figure in the Hanafi tradition; his gloss on al-Wiqāyah is often cited.

Key Terms
شراح الوقاية (shurrāḥ al-Wiqāyah): Commentators of the Hanafi fiqh manual 'al-Wiqāyah' by Tāj al-Sharī'ah.
مصلح الدين القوجوي (Muṣliḥ al-Dīn al-Qūjāwī): Full name of the scholar, indicating origin from Qūjah (a place in Anatolia).
شيخ زاده (Shaykh Zādah): Honorific meaning 'son of a shaykh'; his common epithet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text refer the reader to an earlier section for more details about Muṣliḥ al-Dīn al-Qūjāwī?
A) Because he is not a Hanafi scholar.
B) Because his biography was already given in a previous study.
C) Because he died before the author.
D) Because he wrote on many subjects.

Key Takeaway
A cross-referential biographical note in a commentary assumes a sequentially reading student and reinforces the interconnectedness of Hanafi texts and scholars.

The Scholar Behind the Gloss: Ḥusām al-Dīn Ḥusayn
Biographical entry of a Hanafi scholar and judge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyse a Hanafi biographical entry to identify a scholar's teachers, career roles, authored works, and the significance of his glosses in the transmission of fiqh.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography reveals the chains of authority that authenticate the glosses shaping Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson examines the life of Ḥusām al-Dīn Ḥusayn, a Hanafi scholar whose glosses on key texts like 'Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah' contributed to the ongoing refinement of Hanafi rulings. By studying his biography, we uncover the networks of learning and the institutional roles that produced authoritative fiqh works in the Ottoman period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject
Read the opening line to establish the full name and title of the scholar. Note any honorifics like 'Ḥusām al-Dīn' (Sword of the Religion).
The name includes a patronymic lineage (ibn 'Abd al-Raḥmān).
2
Trace the Teachers
List the scholars from whom he 'took knowledge'. Recognise them as links in the Hanafi transmission chain. Here, Mu'ayyad Zādah and 'Alī Khwājah Zādah are prominent Hanafi figures.
The phrase 'أخذ العلم عن' indicates direct student-teacher relationship.
3
Map the Career Path
Identify the positions he held: teacher (mudarris) in Bursa and at one of the 'eight schools', and judge (qāḍī) in Edirne and Bursa. These reflect the standard Ottoman Hanafi career.
The 'eight schools' likely refers to prestigious madrasas in Istanbul.
4
Note the Date and Place of Death
Record the year (926 AH) and location (Constantinople). This situates the scholar in the early 10th century AH / 16th century CE.
This timeframe marks the mature Ottoman Hanafi tradition.
5
Analyse the Authored Works
Examine the types of works he wrote: glosses (ḥawāshī) on parts of 'Sharḥ al-Tajrīd' (logic/theology) and on 'Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah' (fiqh). Understand that glosses refine and defend school positions.
The scope 'awāʼil' (beginnings) suggests an incomplete or partial gloss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۲. ومنهم: حسام الدين حسين بن عبد الرحمن (۳) ، أخذ العلم عن عبد الرحمن، الشهير بمؤيد زاده ، وعلى خواجه زاده وصار مدرّساً ببروسا، وبإحدى المدارس الثمان، وقاضياً بأدرنة وبروسا ، ومات بقسطنطينية سنة ست وعشرين وتسعمئة، ألف «حواش على أوائل شرح التجريد»، وعلى «شرح الوقاية»،
22. Among them: Ḥusām al-Dīn Ḥusayn ibn 'Abd al-Raḥmān (3). He took knowledge from 'Abd al-Raḥmān, known as Mu'ayyad Zādah, and from 'Alī Khwājah Zādah, and became a teacher in Bursa, and at one of the eight schools, and a judge in Edirne and Bursa. He died in Constantinople in the year 926 AH. He authored glosses on the beginnings of 'Sharḥ al-Tajrīd', and on 'Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah'.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This biographical entry presents Ḥusām al-Dīn Ḥusayn ibn 'Abd al-Raḥmān, a Hanafi scholar active in the Ottoman Empire during the early 10th/16th century. The text notes his teachers: 'Abd al-Raḥmān al-Mu'ayyad Zādah and 'Alī Khwājah Zādah, both prominent scholars. He held teaching positions in Bursa and at one of the prestigious 'eight schools' (possibly referring to the eight madrasas of Istanbul). He also served as a judge (qāḍī) in Edirne and Bursa. His death occurred in Constantinople (Istanbul) in 926 AH. His authored works include glosses (ḥawāshī) on the opening sections of 'Sharḥ al-Tajrīd' (a work on logic or theology by al-Ṭūsī) and a gloss on 'Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah' (the Hanafi fiqh commentary). This entry illustrates the typical career path of an Ottoman Hanafi scholar: study under masters, teach at leading madrasas, serve as judge, and write glosses on key texts.

Key Terms
حواش (ḥawāshī): Plural of ḥāshiyah; glosses or supercommentaries that expand on earlier commentaries.
شرح التجريد (Sharḥ al-Tajrīd): A commentary on 'Tajrīd al-‘Itiqād' (or 'Tajrīd al-Manṭiq'), a work on logic or theology by Naṣīr al-Dīn al-Ṭūsī. The text specifies 'on the beginnings' (awāʼil), indicating a partial gloss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Ottoman Hanafi Scholar's Career and Hashiya Tradition
Biographical account of a Hanafi scholar's career

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the typical career trajectory of an Ottoman Hanafi scholar and identify the role of hashiyas in preserving and refining the Hanafi school's positions.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's career was a state-sponsored path from madrasa to judgeship, and his legacy often rested on hashiyas that refined earlier works.

This biographical passage from 'al-Aqd al-Manzum' provides a window into the life of an unnamed Hanafi scholar who flourished in the Ottoman Empire during the 10th century AH. Beyond mere dates and titles, the text reveals the institutional structure of Ottoman learning—the progression through madrasas, the patronage of sultans and viziers, and the intertwining of scholarly production with state service. The scholar's most enduring contribution is his set of hashiyas (super-commentaries) on key texts in theology, fiqh, and rhetoric, illustrating how Hanafi scholarship was transmitted and refined in the post-classical period.

Guided Path
1
Map the career stages
Identify the sequence of positions: from mulazim (assistant) to teaching at various madrasas of increasing prestige, then to judgeship (qadi) in major cities, and finally retirement. Note the salaries mentioned, which reflect the hierarchy.
The salaries increase from 25 to 100 dirhams, mirroring institutional prestige.
2
Identify the scholar's intellectual output
List the three works on which he wrote hashiyas: Sharh al-Mawaqif (theology), Sharh al-Wiqaya (Hanafi fiqh), and Sharh al-Miftah (rhetoric). Understand that a hashia is not a primary commentary but a gloss that often clarifies, critiques, or defends the original commentary.
Sharh al-Wiqaya by Sadr al-Shari'a is a foundational Hanafi fiqh commentary; the hashia on it is directly relevant to the present book 'Umdat al-Ri'aya'.
3
Analyze the role of the state in scholarship
The sultan commissioned translations of Persian books into Turkish, and the scholar was appointed and dismissed from judgeships by state authority. This illustrates the Ottoman practice of integrating scholars into the bureaucracy and using their linguistic skills for state purposes.
This relationship also ensured that scholarly output served practical needs, such as making texts accessible in Turkish.
4
Reflect on the significance of hashiyas in Hanafi tradition
Hashiyas were essential for keeping earlier commentaries alive and applicable. They often incorporated later rulings, resolved ambiguities, and defended the Hanafi school against critiques. This scholar's hashia on Sharh al-Wiqaya would have been used in madrasa teaching and fatwa-giving.
The 'hashiya' tradition shows the cumulative nature of Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي «العقد المنظوم في ذكر أفاضل الروم»: «كان أبوه من كبار زمـرة القضاة الحاكمين في القصبات، ونشأ مشغوفاً بالعلم وأربابه ، ومعجباً بالـفـضـل وأصحابه، فاهتم في التحصيل، ورغب في التكميل، وتشرف بمجالس السادة. وكان منه ما كان حتى صار ملازماً من المولى خير الدين، معلم السلطان سليمان. ثم درس في المدرسة السراجية بأدرنة بخمسة وعشرين، ثم بمدرسة مراد باشا بقسطنطينية بثلاثين، ثم بمدرسة محمود باشا بهذه المدينة بأربعين ، ثم صار وظيفته فيها خمسين، ثمّ ساعده الدهر وأعانه الزمان حيث وصل إلى إحدى المدارس الثمان بمهمة إياس باشا الوزير الكبير بتقدير العزيز القدير، ثمّ صار مأموراً من قبل السلطان سليمان بترجمة بعض الكتب الفارسيّة بالتركيّة، فأتمها في قليل من الزمان، فأعطاه مدرسة السلطان بایزید خان. ثمّ قلّد قضاء حلب، ثم عزل عنه ، وفوّض إليه تفتيش أحوال القاهرة ، فأصبحت بكمال استقامته عامرة، ثمّ قلّد قضاء دمشق الشام ، ثم نقل إلى قضاء ذات الأهرام، ثم وجه إليه مدرسة أبي أيوب الأنصاري [؟] بمئة درهم، فعما قليل عيناه [؟]، فتقاعد بوظيفته المزبورة. فلَمّا وصل العمر إلى حدود الثمانين أباده الزمان، وأبلاه الدهر الخوان، وذلك سنة ثلاث وسبعين وتسعمئة ، وقد كتب حواش على شرح المواقف»، وعلى «شرح الوقاية لصدر الشريعة، وعلى شرح المفتاح للجرجاني، وله ديوان شعر بالتركي». انتهى كلامه
And in al-Aqd al-Manzum regarding the virtuous of the Romans: 'His father was among the senior group of judges ruling in districts. He grew up devoted to knowledge and its people, admiring virtue and its companions. He exerted himself in acquisition and desired completion, and honored himself in the gatherings of masters. From him was what was until he became a permanent student (mulazim) of al-Mawla Khayr al-Din, teacher of Sultan Sulayman. Then he taught at al-Madrasa al-Sirajiyya in Edirne for twenty-five, then at the Madrasa of Murad Pasha in Constantinople for thirty, then at the Madrasa of Mahmud Pasha in this city for forty, then his salary became fifty. Then time aided him and fortune helped him until he reached one of the eight madrasas through the assignment of Ilyas Pasha, the grand vizier, by the decree of the Almighty. Then he was ordered by Sultan Sulayman to translate some Persian books into Turkish, completing them in a short time, so he gave him the school of Sultan Bayezid Khan. Then he was appointed judge of Aleppo, then dismissed from it, and entrusted with the inspection of the affairs of Cairo, which became prosperous due to his complete integrity. Then he was appointed judge of Damascus, then transferred to the judgeship of Dhat al-Ahram, then he was assigned the school of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari ... with one hundred dirhams, and soon his eyes ... so he retired with his mentioned position. When his life reached around eighty, time destroyed him and the treacherous age wore him out, in the year 973. He wrote hashiyas on Sharh al-Mawaqif, on Sharh al-Wiqaya by Sadr al-Shari'a, and on Sharh al-Miftah by al-Jurjani, and he has a collection of Turkish poetry.' End of his words.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a biographical quotation from the work 'al-Aqd al-Manzum fi Dhikr Afadil al-Rum'. It relates the life of an unnamed Hanafi scholar from the Ottoman period. The text emphasizes his scholarly lineage, his dedication to learning, and his career progression from student to teacher at various madrasas and finally to a judge. Notably, he translated Persian books into Turkish by order of Sultan Suleiman the Magnificent, indicating his linguistic ability and the state's need for scholarly works in the vernacular. His death in 973 AH (1565-66 CE) places him in the 10th century Hijri. His major contributions are hashiyas (commentaries) on three important works: Sharh al-Mawaqif (a theological work by al-Taftazani), Sharh al-Wiqaya (a Hanafi fiqh commentary by Sadr al-Shari'a), and Sharh al-Miftah (a work on rhetoric by al-Jurjani). The biography highlights the typical Ottoman scholarly career: madrasa education, appointment to various madrasas of increasing prestige, judicial service, and finally retirement. It also shows the connection between the state and scholars, as the sultan directly commissioned translations. The work on Sharh al-Wiqaya is particularly relevant to the present book, as 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is itself a hashia on Sharh al-Wiqaya.

Key Terms
حاشية (hashiya): Super-commentary or gloss on an earlier commentary; the scholar wrote hashiyas on several works.
ملازم (mulazim): A permanent student or assistant to a senior scholar, often receiving a stipend.
المولى (al-mawla): Honorific title for a high-ranking scholar or judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

This Ottoman scholar's biography exemplifies how Hanafi scholarship was sustained through state patronage, with hashiyas serving as a crucial mechanism for refining and transmitting the school's legal and theological positions.

Muslih al-Din al-Qujawi (Shaykh Zadah): A Cross-Reference in Hanafi Scholarship
Biographical cross-reference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of biographical cross-references in Hanafi compilations and identify how they connect different layers of scholarly work.

Core Idea
Cross-references link present works to earlier discussions, building a unified scholarly tradition.

This passage is a single-line biographical note on Muslih al-Din al-Qujawi, better known as Shaykh Zadah. Rather than repeating his biography, the author directs the reader to an earlier section. This technique is common in Hanafi works that compile multiple layers of commentary, allowing the author to avoid redundancy while acknowledging the scholar's place in the chain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Locate the name and nickname: Muslih al-Din al-Qujawi, known as Shaykh Zadah. Recognize that 'Shaykh Zadah' is an Ottoman honorific meaning 'son of a shaykh'.
Not to be confused with other scholars named Shaykh Zadah.
2
Understand the cross-reference
The phrase 'his mention has passed in the previous study' indicates that his full biography was given earlier in the same work. The author assumes the reader can look back.
Cross-references save space and tie the work together.
3
Analyze the function
This cross-reference preserves the continuity of the chain of commentators on al-Wiqaya. It shows that the present commentary (Umdat al-Ri'aya) is part of a larger network of scholarship.
Such references are common in sharh works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢١. ومنهم : مصلح الدين القوجوي، المعروف بشيخ زاده ، وقد مرّ ذكره في الدراسة السابقة، عند ذكر شراح «الوقاية».
21. Among them: Muslih al-Din al-Qujawi, known as Shaykh Zadah, and his mention has passed in the previous study, when mentioning the commentators of al-Wiqaya.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This is a brief biographical entry for Muslih al-Din al-Qujawi, who is famous as Shaykh Zadah. The author indicates that this scholar was already discussed in an earlier section of the book devoted to the commentators of al-Wiqaya. This suggests that the present work (Umdat al-Ri'aya) is part of a larger study that includes multiple layers of scholars associated with al-Wiqaya. The brevity of the entry implies that the reader should refer back to that earlier section for fuller details.

Key Terms
شيخ زاده (Shaykh Zadah): A nickname meaning 'son of a shaykh'; here it refers to Muslih al-Din al-Qujawi.

Mustafa ibn Khalil: A Hanafi Scholar and His Legacy
Biography of a scholar from a biographical dictionary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Mustafa ibn Khalil's teachers, students, major works, and his relation to the author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya.

Core Idea
Mustafa ibn Khalil's works, especially Sharh al-Wiqaya, bridge Hanafi fiqh and biographical literature.

This passage introduces Mustafa ibn Khalil, a 15th-16th century Hanafi scholar who taught in Bursa and Constantinople. He is primarily known as the father of Tashkuprizada, the famous biographer, but his own contributions to fiqh and tafsir were significant. Understanding his scholarly lineage and works helps contextualize the transmission of Hanafi knowledge in the Ottoman period.

Guided Path
1
Identify his scholarly network
List the teachers and students mentioned. This reveals the intellectual circles he belonged to.
Teachers include his father, maternal uncle, and Khwajah Zadah; his son is his most famous student.
2
Note his teaching career
He taught in Bursa and Constantinople, two major Ottoman centers of learning.
This indicates his recognized expertise and influence.
3
Catalog his authored works
The passage lists four works: a treatise on faraid, one on hadith resolution, one on Tafsir al-Baydawi, and a commentary on al-Wiqaya.
Sharh al-Wiqaya is particularly important for Hanafi fiqh study.
4
Correct the common misunderstanding
He is not the author of al-Shaqa'iq; his son is. This passage from his son's work clarifies the relationship.
The son Tashkuprizada authored the biographical dictionary al-Shaqa'iq.

٢٣. ومنهم : مصطفى بن خليل، والد مؤلّف الشقائق النعمانية»، تلميذ والده، وخاله محمد بن إبراهيم النكساري، ودرويش بن محمد، والمولى على العربي، و خواجه زاده، وصار مدرّساً ببروسا وقسطنطينية، وكانت ولادته بطاشكبري ، سبع وخمسين وثمانمئة ووفاته سنة خمس وثلاثين بعد تسعمئة ، له : «رسالة متعلقة بعلم الفرائض»، و«رسالة في حل حديثي الابتداء»، و«رسالة على بعض المواضع من تفسير البيضاوي»، و «شرح الوقاية». كذا ذكره ابنه في «الشقائق».
23. Among them: Mustafa ibn Khalil, the father of the author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. He was a student of his father, his maternal uncle Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Niksari, Darwish ibn Muhammad, al-Mawla Ali al-Arabi, and Khwajah Zadah. He became a teacher in Bursa and Constantinople. Commentary
This entry covers Mustafa ibn Khalil, who is notable as the father of the author of the biographical work al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya (Tashkuprizada). He studied under several prominent scholars, including his father, his uncle, and Khwajah Zadah. He taught in both Bursa and Constantinople. Born in 857 AH (1453 CE) in Tashkupri, he died in 935 AH (1528-29 CE). His writings include a treatise on the science of inheritance (faraid), a treatise on the resolution of two hadiths concerning 'al-ibtida' (perhaps meaning innovation or the beginning of something), a treatise on selected verses from Tafsir al-Baydawi, and a commentary (Sharh) on al-Wiqaya. The source for this information is his son's biographical dictionary.

Key Terms
علم الفرائض (ilm al-faraid): The science of inheritance shares in Islamic law.
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqaya): A commentary on al-Wiqaya, a Hanafi fiqh text.
الشقائق النعمانية (al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya): A biographical dictionary of Ottoman scholars by Tashkuprizada.

The Life and Works of Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi
Biography of Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly contributions and key positions of Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi and explain the significance of his work Takmilat Fath al-Qadir.

Core Idea
Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi's Takmilat Fath al-Qadir completes Ibn al-Humam's commentary on al-Hidaya, bridging a critical gap in Hanafi fiqh.

This biography introduces you to one of the most influential Ottoman Hanafi scholars, Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi. As both a judge and a teacher, he played a key role in shaping Hanafi jurisprudence in the Ottoman Empire. His most lasting contribution was completing the monumental commentary on al-Hidaya, known as Fath al-Qadir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Read the name and attributions: Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Badr al-Din, known as Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi. 'Qadi Zadeh' means 'son of a judge', indicating a family tradition of scholarship.
2
Note His Teachers and Training
He studied under prominent scholars like Juway Zadah and al-Mawla Sa'di (the commentator of Tafsir al-Baydawi). This pedigree locates him within the Ottoman scholarly tradition.
3
Recognize His Official Positions
He held teaching positions in Constantinople and Edirne, served as judge of Aleppo and judge of the army (qadi al-askar) in Rumelia, and was the head of fatwa and teaching in Constantinople. These roles show his high status.
4
Understand His Major Work
His commentary on al-Hidaya, known as Takmilat Fath al-Qadir, filled the gap from the chapter of Wakala to the end. It is a completion of Ibn al-Humam's Fath al-Qadir, a major Hanafi reference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٤. ومنهم : المولى شمس الدين أحمد بن المولى بدر الدين، المشتهر بقاضي زاده الرومي، قرأ على علماء عصره، كالمولى محمد المعروف بجوى زاده، والمولى سعدي محشي «تفسير البيضاوي ، وبرع في العلوم، وصار من الجهابذة، وفوض إليه تدريس المدارس بقسطنطينية وأدرنة ،وغيرهما، وقضاء حلب، وقضاء العساكر بروم ايلي. وفوض إليه أمر الفتوى والتدريس بقسطنطينية، ولم يزل عليه إلى أن مات سنة ثمان وثمانين بعد تسعمئة ، ألف شرح الهداية من كتاب الوكالة إلى الآخر، وهو المعروف بـ«تكملة فتح القدير»، و«حاشية على شرح المفتاح» للسيد، و«حاشية على أوائل شرح الوقاية»، و «حاشية على التجريد»، ورسائل كثيرة. كذا في «العقد المنظوم في ذكر أفاضل الروم».
24. Among them: al-Mawla Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn al-Mawla Badr al-Din, famous as Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi. He read upon the scholars of his time, such as al-Mawla Muhammad known as Juway Zadah, and al-Mawla Sa'di, the commentator of Tafsir al-Baydawi. He excelled in the sciences and became one of the geniuses. He was entrusted with teaching in the madrasas of Constantinople and Edirne and elsewhere, and the judgeship of Aleppo, and the judgeship of the troops in Rumelia. He was entrusted with the matter of fatwa and teaching in Constantinople, and he remained upon that until he died in the year 988. He authored a commentary on al-Hidaya from the book of Wakala to the end, known as 'Takmilat Fath al-Qadir', and 'Hashiya on Sharh al-Miftah' by al-Sayyid, and 'Hashiya on the Beginnings of Sharh al-Wiqaya', and 'Hashiya on al-Tajrid', and many treatises. Thus in al-Aqd al-Manzum fi Dhikr Afadil al-Rum.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This is a biography of Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi (Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Badr al-Din), a very prominent Ottoman Hanafi scholar. He studied under Juway Zadah and al-Mawla Sa'di (the commentator of Baydawi's tafsir). He became a leading teacher and judge, serving in high positions including the judgeship of the army (qadi al-askar) in Rumelia, and he was also appointed as the head of fatwa and teaching in Constantinople. He died in 988 AH (1580-81 CE). His most famous work is the completion of Fath al-Qadir (a commentary on al-Hidaya by Ibn al-Humam), which he wrote from the chapter of Wakala to the end, hence called Takmilat Fath al-Qadir. He also wrote hashiyas on Sharh al-Miftah (by al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani), on the beginning of Sharh al-Wiqaya (relevant to the present book), and on al-Tajrid (logic). The source is al-Aqd al-Manzum, a biographical dictionary of Ottoman scholars.

Key Terms
تكملة فتح القدير (Takmilat Fath al-Qadir): The completion of Fath al-Qadir; a supplementary commentary on al-Hidaya covering the latter parts.
قاضي زاده (Qadi Zadeh): Nickname meaning 'son of a judge'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sharh al-Wiqaya
B) Takmilat Fath al-Qadir
C) Hashiya on al-Tajrid
D) Sharh al-Miftah

Key Takeaway
Qadi Zadeh al-Rumi's completion of Fath al-Qadir was a major contribution to Hanafi fiqh scholarship.

Biography of Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Taftazani
Brief biographical entry on a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Taftazani and explain his connection to the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
A descendant of Taftazani and student of Ilyas Zadah, Ahmad al-Taftazani completed his hashia in 900 AH.

Biographical entries like this one from a Hanafi biographical dictionary offer a window into the scholarly chains that transmitted legal knowledge. Here we meet Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Taftazani, a little-known commentator whose work is mentioned in passing. Understanding his place helps us appreciate the interconnected network of Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and title
Read the Arabic name carefully. The title 'Shaykh al-Islam' indicates high religious authority, especially in Ottoman times. Note the lineage: Ahmad ibn Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The last part is his nisba, showing descent from the famous theologian Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani.
'Shaykh al-Islam' is not a personal name but an honorific.
2
Determine his scholarly product and its completion date
The author says he saw his hashia (super-commentary). The scholar noted in the colophon that he finished writing it in Rabi' al-Awwal 900 AH (approx. November 1494 CE). This gives us a firm date for his activity.
A hashia is a marginal commentary on an existing work, often expanding or critiquing.
3
Identify his teacher
The text states he was a student (min talamidh) of Ilyas Zadah. Ilyas Zadah himself wrote a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya, a key Hanafi primer. This links Ahmad al-Taftazani directly to the mainstream Hanafi educational tradition.
Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya is an abridgment of al-Wiqaya by Sadr al-Shari'a.
4
Note the context within the biographical work
This entry is numbered 25 among a list of scholars. The phrase 'as clarified in Bahth al-Wudu' suggests a cross-reference within the hashia or another work, indicating the author had seen the text.
5
Reflect on the significance of such brief entries
Even a short entry contributes to the chain of transmission (isnad) of Hanafi knowledge. It confirms that the scholarly lineage from Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani through Ilyas Zadah continued, and that a hashia existed, preserving interpretations.
Biographical dictionaries are crucial for verifying the reliability of sources in Islamic scholarship.

Source Text

He mentioned at its end: that he finished writing it in Rabi' al-Awwal of the year 900. Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This entry describes Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Yahya al-Taftazani, a descendant of the famous theologian and jurist Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. The author states that he saw his hashia (super-commentary). The scholar noted at the end of his work that he completed it in Rabi' al-Awwal 900 AH (November-December 1494 CE). He was a student of Ilyas Zadah, who himself wrote a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya (an abridgment of al-Wiqaya). The phrase 'as clarified in Bahth al-Wudu' likely refers to a cross-reference within that hashia or another work. This biography is very brief, indicating that the author may have only had limited information.

Key Terms
شيخ الإسلام (Shaykh al-Islam): An honorific title for the highest religious authority in the Ottoman Empire.
مختصر الوقاية (Mukhtasar al-Wiqaya): An abridgment of al-Wiqaya by Sadr al-Shari'a, a standard Hanafi fiqh primer.

The Chain of Commentators on Sharh al-Wiqayah
Biographical list of Hanafi commentators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi commentators on Sharh al-Wiqayah and explain how biographical chains (isnad) establish the authority of a commentary.

Core Idea
The chain of commentators on Sharh al-Wiqayah is the isnad of Hanafi fiqh transmission.

When you open a Hanafi fiqh commentary like Sharh al-Wiqayah, you are not just reading the author's words—you are standing at the end of a centuries-long chain of scholarship. This passage introduces the scholars who wrote hashiyas (supercommentaries) on Sharh al-Wiqayah. Knowing their names, teachers, and works helps you assess the reliability and school-authority of their annotations. This lesson trains you to read such biographical entries as legal documents, not mere history.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar's Name and Title
Start by noting the full name and honorific (e.g., 'Shaykh al-Islam', 'Mawla'). This indicates the scholar's stature in the Hanafi tradition.
Titles like 'Qadizade' or 'Shaykh al-Islam' often signal high scholarly rank.
2
Trace the Teacher-Student Chain
The passage often names teachers. This connects the scholar to earlier authorities, establishing the chain of transmission (isnad) for the text.
For example, Qadizade al-Rumi studied under Juyzadeh and Sa'di al-Baydawi.
3
List the Scholar's Works
Note which works are directly on Sharh al-Wiqayah (hashiya, sharh) and which are on other texts. This shows the scope of the scholar's expertise.
A scholar who wrote on both fiqh and usul (like al-Taftazani) carries more weight.
4
Note the Death Date
The death date (wafat) helps place the scholar in time and shows the chronological layers of commentary.
For instance, Mustafa ibn Khalil died in 935 AH, while Qadizade died in 988 AH.
5
Evaluate the Entry's Source
The passage often cites its own source (e.g., 'al-Shaqaiq', 'al-Aqd al-Manzum'). This allows you to check the reliability of the biography.
Cross-referencing sources is a skill of the muhaqqiq (critical editor).

The Eighth Study: Biographies of the Commentators on Sharh al-Wiqayah

Among them: Mustafa ibn Khalil, father of the author of al-Shaqaiq al-Numaniyah, student of his father and his maternal uncle Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Niksari, and Darwish ibn Muhammad, and Mawla Ali al-Arabi, and Khwajazadeh. He became a teacher in Bursa and Constantinople. His birth was in Taskopru, year 857 AH, and his death in 935 AH. He has: 'Risala on the Science of Faraid', 'Risala on the Solution of the Two Hadiths of Innovation', 'Risala on Some Passages of Tafsir al-Baydawi', and 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'. His son mentioned this in 'al-Shaqaiq' (r).
24. Among them: Mawla Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Mawla Badr al-Din, known as Qadizade al-Rumi. He studied under the scholars of his time, such as Mawla Muhammad known as Juyzadeh, and Mawla Sa'di commentator on Tafsir al-Baydawi. He excelled in the sciences and became a genius. He was entrusted with teaching in the schools of Constantinople and Edirne, and others, and the judgeship of Aleppo, and the judgeship of the military in Rumelia. He was entrusted with the office of fatwa and teaching in Constantinople, and continued until he died in 988 AH. He authored 'Sharh al-Hidayah' from the Book of Agency to the end, known as 'Takmilat Fath al-Qadir', and 'Hashiya on Sharh al-Miftah' by al-Sayyid, and 'Hashiya on the Beginning of Sharh al-Wiqayah', and 'Hashiya on al-Tajrid', and many treatises. As mentioned in 'al-Aqd al-Manzum fi Dhikr Afadil al-Rum'. 
25. Among them: Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Yahya ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani Mas'ud. I saw his hashia. He mentioned at its end that he finished writing it in Rabi' al-Awwal 900 AH. He is among the students of Ilyas Zadeh, commentator of 'Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah', as he stated clearly about him in 'Bahth al-Wudu'. (1) 'al-Shaqaiq' (p. 231). (4) 'al-Aqd al-Manzum' (pp. 496-498).
And among his works: 'Sharh al-Tahdhib', 'Hawashi al-Talwih', 'Sharh al-Faraid al-Sirajiyyah', and others. He was skilled and virtuous. When his father Qutb al-Din Yahya died on Monday, 24 Dhul-Hijjah 880 AH, and he was distinguished by the office of Islam from the end of the era of Mirza Shah Rukh ibn Timur to the era of Sultan Husayn, his positions were entrusted to him... He stayed in Khurasan for about thirty years teaching and benefiting until he was dismissed in 916 AH, and died in the same year. As mentioned in 'Habib al-Siyar'. I have expanded on his biography and the biography of his father and his grandfather Sa'd al-Taftazani in 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah' and its lofty notes (2).
26. Among them: Mawla 'Isam al-Din Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Isfara'ini, author of famous works such as 'Hawashi Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah', 'Hawashi Tafsir al-Baydawi', 'Sharh Talkhis al-Ma'ani' named 'al-Atwal', and others. His death according to 'Kashf' (3) was in 944 AH. The beginning of his hashia: 'We praise You, O He who is the gist of Your guidance is protection...' and he mentioned that he completed the first part of it in the first third of the night of Monday from the second half of Rabi' al-Awwal in 934 AH.
27. Among them: Qutb al-Din al-Marzifuni al-Rumi, teacher in the schools of Iznik and Constantinople. His death, according to what is mentioned in 'al-Shaqaiq' (4), was in 935 AH.
28. Among them: Husam al-Din, died in 1010 AH. He has acceptable annotations, and was a teacher in the schools of Edirne and others. As mentioned in 'Khulasat al-Athar fi A'yan al-Qarn al-Hadi 'Ashar' (5).

(3) 'Kashf al-Zunun' (2:2022). (4) 'al-Shaqaiq' (p. 286). (5) 'Khulasat al-Athar' (1:501). (6) In 'al-Shaqaiq' (p. 272): 'al-Qarabaghi'.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the introductory material of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah'. The author presents the Eighth Study (al-Dirasah al-Thaminah), which is devoted to the biographies of commentators (muhashshin) on Sharh al-Wiqayah, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. Understanding these scholars is crucial for appreciating the chain of transmission and authority in the Hanafi school. The passage lists several scholars with their teachers, works, positions, and death dates. Among them are Mustafa ibn Khalil, father of the author of al-Shaqaiq, who wrote a Sharh al-Wiqayah; Qadizade al-Rumi, known for his Takmilat Fath al-Qadir; and Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad al-Taftazani, who wrote a hashia. Others include 'Isam al-Din al-Isfara'ini, Qutb al-Din al-Marzifuni, Husam al-Din, and Muhyi al-Din al-Qarabaghi. The author emphasizes that he has provided more details on some scholars in his other works, like al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah. This section demonstrates the vibrant scholarly tradition of commentary and supercommentary on Hanafi texts, ensuring that students recognize the human chain behind the rulings they study.

Key Terms
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): A commentary on the Hanafi fiqh text 'al-Wiqayah' by Sadr al-Shari'ah; used as a base text for further commentaries.
حاشية (hashiyah): A supercommentary or gloss on a commentary, often providing marginal notes and scholarly refinements.

The Commentators of Sharh al-Wiqayah
Biographical dictionary of Hanafi glossators on Sharh al-Wiqayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi scholars who wrote glosses on Sharh al-Wiqayah and state the significance of their works in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The hawashi on Sharh al-Wiqayah are the scholarly backbone of Hanafi fiqh transmission.

This passage introduces us to the scholarly lineage behind one of the most important Hanafi fiqh texts: Sharh al-Wiqayah. Knowing who wrote its glosses and when helps us understand the chain of authority and the development of Hanafi legal thought. These commentators were not mere copyists; they were active jurists, teachers, and judges whose work shaped how later generations study fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars listed
Read through the entries (26-33) and note each scholar's name, death date, and key works mentioned. This establishes who they are and when they lived.
Dates are given in Hijri; convert if needed.
2
Categorize their works
For each scholar, identify whether their gloss (hawashi) is on Sharh al-Wiqayah itself or on other texts. Note the range of texts they commented on (e.g., Tafsir, Usul, Hadith).
Some scholars wrote on multiple texts; this shows their breadth.
3
Trace the scholarly chain
Notice how many scholars studied under or were connected to earlier Hanafi authorities (e.g., mentions of teachers and cities). This chain (sanad) is crucial for establishing the reliability of their glosses.
The chain often goes back to Sadr al-Shari'ah and beyond.
4
Assess the geographical spread
Map the cities mentioned (Khurasan, Azniq, Constantinople, Edirne, Cairo, Aleppo, Ankara, etc.). This shows the widespread study of Sharh al-Wiqayah across the Hanafi world.
The spread indicates the text's central role in Hanafi education.
5
Connect to modern fiqh study
Understand that these glosses are still used today in advanced Hanafi fiqh study. Knowing the commentators helps a student choose reliable editions and understand variations in rulings.
Many hawashi are printed alongside Sharh al-Wiqayah in modern editions.

وَمِنْ تَصَانِيفِهِ: «شَرْحُ التَّهْذِيبِ»، وَ«حَوَاشِي التَّلْوِيحِ»، وَ«شَرْحُ الْفَرَائِضِ السِّرَاجِيَّةِ»، وَغَيْرُهَا. كَانَ مَاهِراً فَاضِلاً. وَلَمَّا مَاتَ وَالِدُهُ قُطْبُ الدِّينِ يَحْيَى يَوْمَ الْإِثْنَيْنِ الرَّابِعِ وَالْعِشْرِينَ مِنْ ذِي الْحِجَّةِ سَنَةَ ثَمَانِينَ وَثَمَانِمِائَةٍ، وَكَانَ مُمْتَازاً بِمَنْصِبِ الْإِسْلَامِ مِنْ أَوَاخِرِ عَهْدِ مِرْزَا شَاهْرُخِ بْنِ تَيْمورَ إِلَى عَهْدِ السُّلْطَانِ حُسَيْنٍ، فَوُضِعَتْ إِلَيْهِ مَنَاصِبُهُ. سَبْعُ مَشْيَخَةٍ. فَأَقَامَ بِخُطَّةِ خُرَاسَانَ نَحْواً مِنْ ثَلَاثِينَ سَنَةً، يُدَرِّسُ وَيُفِيدُ إِلَى أَنْ عُزِلَ فِي سَنَةِ سِتَّ عَشْرَةَ بَعْدَ تِسْعِمَائَةٍ، وَمَاتَ فِي تِلْكَ السَّنَةِ. كَذَا فِي «حَبِيبِ السِّيَرِ»، وَقَدْ بَسَطْتُ الْكَلَامَ فِي تَرْجَمَتِهِ وَتَرْجَمَةِ أَبِيهِ وَوَالِدِ جَدِّهِ السَّعْدِ التَّفْتَازَانِيِّ فِي «الْفَوَائِدِ الْبَهِيَّةِ»، وَ«تَعْلِيقَاتِهَا السَّنِيَّةِ».
(٢) ٢٦. وَمِنْهُمُ: الْمَوْلَى عِصَامُ الدِّينِ إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدٍ الْإِسْفَرَائِينِيُّ، ذُو التَّصَانِيفِ الشَّهِيرَةِ؛ كَـ«حَوَاشِي شَرْحِ الْعَقَائِدِ النَّسَفِيَّةِ»، وَ«حَوَاشِي تَفْسِيرِ الْبَيْضَاوِيِّ»، وَ«شَرْحِ تَلْخِيصِ الْمَعَانِي» الْمُسَمَّى بِـ«الْأَطْوَلِ»، وَغَيْرِهَا. وَكَانَتْ وَفَاتُهُ عَلَى مَا فِي «الْكَشْفِ» سَنَةَ أَرْبَعٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ وَتِسْعِمَائَةٍ، أَوَّلُ حَاشِيَتِهِ: نَحْمَدُكَ يَا مَنْ هُوَ مُوجِزُ هِدَايَتِكَ وِقَايَةٌ.. الْخَ، وَذَكَرَ فِيهَا أَنَّهُ أَتَمَّ الْجُزْءَ الْأَوَّلَ مِنْهَا فِي الثُّلُثِ الْأَوَّلِ مِنْ لَيْلَةِ الْإِثْنَيْنِ مِنَ النِّصْفِ الْآخَرِ مِنْ رَبِيعِ الْأَوَّلِ فِي سَنَةِ أَرْبَعٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ وَتِسْعِمَائَةٍ.
٢٧. وَمِنْهُمُ: قُطْبُ الدِّينِ الْمَرْزِيفُونِيُّ الرُّومِيُّ، مُدَرِّسُ مَدَارِسِ أَزْنِيقَ وَقُسْطَنْطِينِيَّةَ، الْمُتَوَفَّى عَلَى مَا ذَكَرَهُ فِي «الشَّقَائِقِ» سَنَةَ خَمْسٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ بَعْدَ تِسْعِمَائَةٍ.
٢٨. وَمِنْهُمُ: حُسَامُ الدِّينِ، الْمُتَوَفَّى سَنَةَ عَشْرٍ بَعْدَ الْأَلْفِ، لَهُ تَحْرِيرَاتٌ مَقْبُولَةٌ، وَكَانَ مُدَرِّساً بِمَدَارِسِ أَدِرْنَةَ وَغَيْرِهَا. كَذَا فِي «خُلَاصَةِ الْأَثَرِ فِي أَعْيَانِ الْقَرْنِ الْحَادِيَ عَشَرَ».
٢٩. وَمِنْهُمُ: مُحْيِي الدِّينِ مُحَمَّدٌ الْقَرَهْبَاغِيُّ، قَرَأَ عَلَى عُلَمَاءِ بِلَادِهِ، ثُمَّ أَتَى بِلَادَ الرُّومِ، وَقَرَأَ عَلَى يَعْقُوبَ بْنِ سَيِّدِ عَلِيٍّ، شَارِحِ «شِرْعَةِ الْإِسْلَامِ»، وَصَارَ مُدَرِّساً بِأَزْنِيقَ، وَمَاتَ هُنَاكَ سَنَةَ ثَلَاثٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ وَتِسْعِمَائَةٍ. لَهُ تَعْلِيقَاتٌ عَلَى «الْكَشَّافِ»، وَعَلَى «تَفْسِيرِ الْبَيْضَاوِيِّ»، وَعَلَى «التَّلْوِيحِ»، وَعَلَى «الْهِدَايَةِ»، وَعَلَى «شَرْحِ الْوِقَايَةِ»، وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ. كَذَا فِي «الشَّقَائِقِ».
٣٠. وَمِنْهُمُ: الْقَاضِي شَمْسُ الدِّينِ أَحْمَدُ بْنُ حَمْزَةَ الْمَعْرُوفُ بِعَرَبِ جَلَبِي، قَرَأَ أَوَّلاً عَلَى مُوسَى جَلَبِي، وَغَيْرِهِ، وَارْتَحَلَ إِلَى الْقَاهِرَةِ، وَقَرَأَ هُنَاكَ كُتُبَ الْحَدِيثِ، ثُمَّ أَتَى بِلَادَ الرُّومِ، وَلَمْ يَزَلْ يُدَرِّسُ وَيُفِيدُ إِلَى أَنْ مَاتَ سَنَةَ خَمْسِينَ وَتِسْعِمَائَةٍ. كَذَا فِي «الشَّقَائِقِ».
٣١. وَمِنْهُمُ: الْمُفْتِي زَكَرِيَّا بْنُ بَيْرَامٍ، أَصْلُهُ مِنْ بَلْدَةِ أَنْقَرَةَ، وَقَدِمَ قُسْطَنْطِينِيَّةَ، وَأَخَذَ الْعِلْمَ بِهَا عَنْ عَرَبْزَادَةَ عَبْدِ الْبَاقِي، وَلِيَ قَضَاءَ حَلَبَ وَغَيْرِهِ، مَاتَ سَنَةَ عَشْرٍ بَعْدَ الْأَلْفِ، لَهُ حَوَاشٍ عَلَى «الْعِنَايَةِ»، وَعَلَى «شَرْحِ الْوِقَايَةِ». كَذَا فِي «خُلَاصَةِ الْأَثَرِ».
٣٢. وَمِنْهُمُ: الْمَوْلَى مُحْيِي الدِّينِ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ الْخَطِيبِ قَاسِمٍ.
٣٣. وَمُحَمَّدُ بْنُ بِيرْعَلِيِّ الْبِرِكْلِيِّ، نِسْبَةً إِلَى قَصَبَةِ بِرْكِلٍ، الْمُتَوَفَّى سَنَةَ إِحْدَى وَثَمَانِينَ وَتِسْعِمَائَةٍ، وَهُوَ مُؤَلِّفُ «الطَّرِيقَةِ الْمُحَمَّدِيَّةِ» وَغَيْرِهَا. ذَكَرَهُ عَبْدُ الْغَنِيِّ النَّابُلُسِيُّ فِي «الْحَدِيقَةِ النَّدِيَّةِ شَرْحِ الطَّرِيقَةِ الْمُحَمَّدِيَّةِ».
And among his writings: 'Sharh al-Tahdhib', 'Hawashi al-Talwih', 'Sharh al-Fara'id al-Sirajiyyah', and others. He was proficient and virtuous. When his father Qutb al-Din Yahya died on Monday the twenty-fourth of Dhu al-Hijjah in the year 880, and he was distinguished by the office of Islam from the late era of Mirza Shahrukh ibn Timur to the era of Sultan Husayn, his positions were entrusted to him. Seven shaykhdoms. So he resided in the region of Khurasan for about thirty years, teaching and benefiting until he was dismissed in the year 916, and he died in that year. Thus in 'Habib al-Siyar', and I have expanded on his biography and that of his father and his grandfather al-Sa'd al-Taftazani in 'al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah' and its 'Ta'liqat al-Saniyyah'.
(2) 26. Among them: al-Mawla 'Isam al-Din Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Isfara'ini, possessor of famous works such as 'Hawashi Sharh al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah', 'Hawashi Tafsir al-Baydawi', 'Sharh Talkhis al-Ma'ani' called 'al-Atwal', and others. His death was as in 'al-Kashf' in the year 944. The beginning of his gloss: 'Nahmaduka ya man huwa mujizu hidayatika wiqayah...' and he mentioned therein that he completed the first part of it in the first third of the night of Monday from the latter half of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 934.
27. Among them: Qutb al-Din al-Marzifuni al-Rumi, teacher at the schools of Azniq and Constantinople, who died as mentioned in 'al-Shaqa'iq' in the year 935.
28. Among them: Husam al-Din, who died in the year 1010. He has acceptable tahrirat and was a teacher at the schools of Edirne and others. Thus in 'Khulasat al-Athar fi A'yan al-Qarn al-Hadi 'Ashar'.
29. Among them: Muhyi al-Din Muhammad al-Qarabaghi, who studied under scholars of his country, then came to the land of Rum, and studied under Ya'qub ibn Sayyid 'Ali, the commentator of 'Shir'at al-Islam', and became a teacher at Azniq, and died there in the year 943. He has ta'liqat on 'al-Kashshaf', 'Tafsir al-Baydawi', 'al-Talwih', 'al-Hidayah', 'Sharh al-Wiqayah', and others. Thus in 'al-Shaqa'iq'.
30. Among them: al-Qadi Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Hamzah known as 'Arab Jilabi, who first studied under Musa Jilabi and others, and traveled to Cairo and studied the books of hadith there, then came to the land of Rum, and continued teaching and benefiting until he died in the year 950. Thus in 'al-Shaqa'iq'.
31. Among them: al-Mufti Zakariyya ibn Bayram, originally from the town of Ankara, and came to Constantinople, and studied there under 'Arabzadah 'Abd al-Baqi, and became judge of Aleppo and other places, and died in the year 1010. He has hawashi on 'al-'Inayah' and on 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'. Thus in 'Khulasat al-Athar'.
32. Among them: al-Mawla Muhyi al-Din Muhammad ibn al-Khatib Qasim.
33. And Muhammad ibn Bir 'Ali al-Birkili, from the town of Birkil, who died in the year 981, and he is the author of 'al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah' and others. Mentioned by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulusi in 'al-Hadiqah al-Nadiyyah Sharh al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah'.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a biographical dictionary (tarajim) section from the introduction of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah, listing notable Hanafi scholars who authored glosses (hawashi) on Sharh al-Wiqayah by Sadr al-Shari'ah. The author provides brief life accounts, including birth/death dates, teachers, works, and key positions. Each entry is numbered (26-33) and cites sources like Habib al-Siyar, al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyyah, and Khulasat al-Athar. This section serves to establish the scholarly lineage and authority of the commentaries used in the work. The scholars span the 9th-11th centuries AH and include figures like 'Isam al-Din al-Isfara'ini (d. 944 AH), Husam al-Din (d. 1010 AH), Muhyi al-Din al-Qarabaghi (d. 943 AH), and Muhammad al-Birkili (d. 981 AH). Their works are foundational for Hanafi fiqh study.

Key Terms
حواشي (hawashi): Glosses or supercommentaries written in the margins or as separate works to explain, annotate, or critique a base text.
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqayah): The commentary by Sadr al-Shari'ah on his own Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah, a Hanafi fiqh manual.
تعليقات (ta'liqat): Annotations or critical notes on a text, often more detailed than simple glosses.
تحريرات (tahrirat): Independent analytical writings or critical reviews of a text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which scholar wrote glosses (hawashi) on both 'al-'Inayah' and 'Sharh al-Wiqayah'?
A) Muhyi al-Din al-Qarabaghi
B) al-Mufti Zakariyya ibn Bayram
C) 'Isam al-Din al-Isfara'ini
D) Shams al-Din Ahmad ibn Hamzah

Key Takeaway
Knowing the commentators of Sharh al-Wiqayah, their dates, and their roles helps students assess the authority and context of the glosses used in Hanafi fiqh study.

Life of the Author
beginner
8 min
Biographies of Hanafi Glossators on Sharh al-Wiqaya
Biographical listing of Hanafi glossators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi scholars who wrote glosses on Sharh al-Wiqaya and explain the significance of their contributions to Hanafi fiqh scholarship.

Core Idea
Glossators (muhashshun) preserved and refined the Hanafi tradition — knowing them is knowing the chain of authority.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya presents a tarajim (biographical list) of scholars who composed hawashi (glosses) on Sadr al-Shari'ah's Sharh al-Wiqaya. These glosses are not mere annotations; they are critical works that clarify, expand, and sometimes correct the base text. Understanding who these scholars were, their teachers, and their works helps us navigate the Hanafi scholarly tradition and assess the authority of different positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and title
Recognize that this passage is from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya and lists muhashshi of Sharh al-Wiqaya.
The heading 'الدراسة الثامنة: تراجم محشي شرح الوقاية' indicates the genre.
2
Scan the list for key figures
Note names, dates, places, and works for each scholar. Focus on well-known ones like Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Birkili.
Use the death dates to place scholars chronologically.
3
Associate scholars with their glosses
Each scholar's hashia is a distinct commentary; note which one he wrote, e.g., al-Birkili's al-Tariqa al-Muhammadiyya.
Not all glosses are on Sharh al-Wiqaya alone; some wrote on multiple texts.
4
Understand the sources cited
The author uses al-Shaqa'iq, Kashf al-Zunun, etc. — these are historiographical sources that lend authority.
Knowing these sources helps verify scholarly claims.
5
Reflect on the purpose of such lists
They establish the chain of transmission and authority, showing who commented on key texts.
This is a form of sanad (chain) for the fiqh tradition.

Eighth Study: Biographies of the Glossators of Sharh al-Wiqaya. ... (list of scholars with brief biographies)

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing (tarajim) from the super-commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. It systematically enumerates Hanafi scholars who composed glosses (hawashi) on Sadr al-Shari'ah's Sharh al-Wiqaya. The list begins with earlier scholars and continues to later ones, providing each scholar's full name, key teachers, places of study or teaching, date of death, and major works. The sources cited include al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya, Kashf al-Zunun, and Khulasat al-Athar. The entry for Muhammad bin Pir Ali al-Birkili notes he authored al-Tariqa al-Muhammadiyya. The entry for 'Abd Allah bin Siddiq al-Harawi mentions his own gloss begins with al-hamdu lillah. This section serves as a reference for identifying the authoritative commentators on al-Wiqaya.

Key Terms
تراجم (tarajim): Biographical notices of scholars, used here specifically for those who wrote glosses on Sharh al-Wiqaya.
محشي (muhashshi): A scholar who writes a gloss (hashiya) on a text, here on Sharh al-Wiqaya.
شرح الوقاية (Sharh al-Wiqaya): A commentary by Sadr al-Shari'ah on al-Wiqaya, a standard Hanafi fiqh manual.

The Tradition of Glosses on Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah: A Biographical Overview
Biographical listing of scholars who authored glosses on Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of hāshiyah literature in the Hanafi tradition and list key scholars who contributed glosses on Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah.

Core Idea
A hāshiyah is a living commentary that refines, corrects, and expands upon earlier fiqh discourse, not an independent work.

This passage from ‘Umda al-Ri‘āya presents a list of scholars who wrote glosses (hawāshī) on the standard Hanafi text Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah. Such biographical listings are not mere catalogues; they establish the chain of transmission and indicate the intellectual lineage of the commentary tradition. Understanding the role of these glosses and their authors helps us appreciate how Hanafi fiqh developed through cumulative scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the function of a hāshiyah
Understand that a hāshiyah is a super-commentary, distinct from a sharḥ. It comments on the commentary, often resolving ambiguities or engaging with later debates.
Glosses are not independent works; they presuppose the base text and its commentary.
2
Note the numbering and provenance
The scholars are listed with numbers (34-45) and death dates; note the geographic range (Ottoman, Indian). This shows the spread of Hanafi scholarship across regions.
3
Examine the incipit and scope
Some entries give the opening words (incipit) of the gloss. This helps identify the work and confirms the author.
Incipits were commonly used to identify manuscripts before printed catalogs.
4
Observe cross-references to other works
The authors often wrote glosses on many texts across disciplines (tafsīr, uṣūl, fiqh, logic). This shows the breadth of a scholar's expertise.
For instance, Wajīh al-Dīn al-Gujarātī's list covers multiple fields.
5
Appreciate the tarjīḥ within glosses
The entry on ‘Ināyat Allāh al-Qādirī mentions a specific fiqh ruling (gesture in tashahhud is sunna). This exemplifies how glosses engage in juristic preponderance (tarjīḥ) within the Hanafi school.
Glosses often include legal reasoning and preferred positions.

The Mainstay of Care upon the Commentary of al-Wiqayah

40. And Sharaf al-Dīn Yahyā ibn Qarā Jā al-Ruhāwī. 967 AH. 41. And al-Shaykh Yahyā Bakhshī, died at the beginning of the tenth century. The author of Kashf al-Ẓunūn mentioned these. 42. And among them: ‘Abd Allāh ibn Ṣiddīq ibn ‘Umar al-Harawī, the beginning of his gloss: ‘Praise be to God, Lord of the worlds, and the [good] end is for the righteous...’, containing precious investigations and subtle points, and from studying it it is known that its author was a student of Muhammad ‘Awaḍ al-Wajīh, and a contemporary of al-Fādil Muḥibb Allāh al-Bahārī, author of al-Sullam and al-Musallam. 43. And among them: al-Shaykh Wajīh al-Dīn al-‘Alawī al-Gujarātī. Ghulām ‘Alī Āzād mentioned in Sabḥat al-Marjān fī Āthār al-Hindūstān: ‘His birth was in 911 AH, and his death in 998 AH, on Sunday, the 29th of Safar, and he authored many works, including: gloss on Tafsīr al-Bayḍāwī, Sharḥ al-Nukhba, gloss on Sharḥ al-Mukhtaṣar al-‘Aḍudī, gloss on al-Talwīḥ, gloss on Uṣūl al-Bazdawī, gloss on al-Hidāya, gloss on Sharḥ al-Wiqāya, gloss on al-Muṭawwal, gloss on al-Mukhtaṣar, gloss on Sharḥ al-Tajrīd by al-Iṣfahānī, gloss on Sharḥ al-‘Aqā’id by al-Taftāzānī, gloss on al-Qadīma by al-Dawānī, gloss on Sharḥ al-Mawāqif, gloss on Sharḥ Ḥikmat al-‘Ayn, gloss on Sharḥ al-Maqāṣid, gloss on al-Quṭbī, gloss on Sharḥ Mulakhkhaṣ al-Jaghmīnī, Sharḥ al-Tuḥfa al-Shāhiyya, Sharḥ Risālat al-Qūshjī on astronomy, gloss on al-Fawā’id al-Ḍiyā’iyya, Sharḥ al-Irshād by al-Shihāb al-Dawlatābādī, and others. And for details of his biography and those of other scholars of India to be mentioned later, one should consult my treatise Inbā’ al-Khillān bi-Anbā’ ‘Ulamā’ Hindūstān.
And among them: Shāh Luṭf Allāh, known as Mullā Zān ibn Aurangzīb, the beginning of his gloss: ‘Praise be to God who made His book...’, and its name is Ḥall al-Mushkilāt, containing many questions and answers related to the expressions of the text and the commentary and their meanings. 45. And among them: Abū al-Ma‘ārif Muḥammad ‘Ināyat Allāh al-Qādirī al-Qaṣūrī then al-Lahorī al-Shahṯārī. I studied his gloss named Ghāyat al-Ḥawāshī in two volumes, its beginning: ‘Praise be to God whose concise guidance is a protection from deviation from the straight path...’, containing many branches, and among his works is Multaqaṭ al-Daqā’iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā’iq, which he mentioned in the discussion of the gesture during the tashahhud, and he gave preponderance to its being sunna, as is the view of the verifying scholars.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list of scholars who wrote glosses (hawāshī) on Sharḥ al-Wiqāya, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author of ‘Umda al-Ri‘āya, a super-commentary, enumerates these scholars to establish the chain of commentary and to highlight sources for the glosses he may have consulted. Each entry provides the scholar's name, death date, and often the incipit of their gloss or other works. The list includes prominent Hanafi scholars from the Ottoman and Indian contexts, such as Sulayman al-Qaramanī, Muhammad al-Halabī, and Wajīh al-Dīn al-Gujarātī, the latter of whom wrote numerous glosses on major texts of tafsir, usul, fiqh, and logic. The passage also notes that the author, likely ‘Abd al-Ḥalīm al-Laknawī, has written an independent biographical work on Indian scholars. The mention of a gloss by ‘Ināyat Allāh al-Qādirī includes a specific fiqh ruling on the sunna status of the gesture during tashahhud, showing that these glosses often engage in legal reasoning and tarjih (preponderance). This biographical section serves as a scholarly apparatus, documenting the textual tradition and the intellectual lineage of the commentary.

Key Terms
حاشية (hāshiyah): A gloss or super-commentary written on a primary text (matn) or its commentary (sharḥ).
شرح الوقاية (Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah): A commentary by ‘Ubayd Allāh al-Maḥbūbī (d. 747 AH) on the text Wiqāyat al-Riwāyah by his grandfather, a major Hanafi fiqh manual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The list of glossators on Sharḥ al-Wiqāyah demonstrates the vibrant tradition of super-commentary in Hanafi fiqh, where later scholars refined, debated, and expanded upon earlier rulings.

Biography of a Hanafi Commentator: His Life and Scholarly Works
Biographical entry with list of works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details (birth, death, works) from a classical Hanafi biographical entry and explain the role of hashiah in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Hashiah are crucial tools in Hanafi scholarship, preserving and clarifying the madhhab's positions across generations.

This passage introduces us to the life and works of a Hanafi commentator whose hashiah (supercommentaries) on major texts like al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Wiqaya helped transmit and refine the madhhab. By studying this biography, you will learn how later scholars contributed to the Hanafi tradition through commentary literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's name and lifespan
Locate the birth (911 AH) and death (998 AH) dates given in the passage. Note that the scholar died on Sunday, 29th Safar.
Biographical entries often begin with birth and death years.
2
Extract the list of works
Read through the list of works, noting that most begin with 'Hashiyat' (supercommentary). Identify which base texts they comment on (e.g., Tafsir al-Baydawi, al-Hidayah, Sharh al-Wiqaya).
The large number of hashiah indicates the scholar's expertise across many Islamic sciences.
3
Classify the types of works
Categorize the works: those that are hashiah (supercommentaries) vs. those that are sharh (commentaries) or other genres. Note the diversity: fiqh, usul, tafsir, kalam, astronomy.
This shows the scholar's broad learning.
4
Understand the significance of hashiah in the Hanafi tradition
A hashiah is a gloss on a commentary. It clarifies ambiguous points, resolves disputes, and incorporates later ijtihad. This was a common method of scholarly contribution in later periods.
Hashiah were not mere repetition; they were original legal analysis.
5
Recognize the author's reference to his own work
The author mentions his own treatise 'Inba' al-Khillan' for further detail, noting it was never completed. This shows the chain of transmission and the importance of cross-referencing.
Many biographical works remain unfinished; later scholars rely on them nonetheless.

Shah Lutf Allah and His Hashiah 'Hall al-Mushkilat'
Biographical entry for Shah Lutf Allah with his work 'Hall al-Mushkilat'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Shah Lutf Allah and his contribution to Hanafi scholarship, and explain the purpose of his hashiah 'Hall al-Mushkilat'.

Core Idea
Shah Lutf Allah's 'Hall al-Mushkilat' resolves difficult textual issues, preserving the chain of Hanafi commentary.

This lesson introduces a key figure in the Hanafi commentarial tradition: Shah Lutf Allah, known as Mulla Zan. His hashiah on Sharh al-Wiqaya, titled 'Hall al-Mushkilat', is a work that systematically addresses problematic expressions and meanings in both the matn and sharh, reflecting the rigorous pedagogical method of the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Note the full name and title: Shah Lutf Allah, known as Mulla Zan ibn Aurangzeb. Recognize that 'Shah' denotes a respected figure.
2
Recognize the Hashiah Title
The hashiah is named 'Hall al-Mushkilat' (Solving the Problems). Understand the meaning: it aims to resolve difficult points in the text.
3
Understand the Content
The hashiah contains many questions and answers (su'al wa jawab) related to the expressions of the matn and sharh and their meanings.
This format is typical of hashiah literature.
4
Note the Transmission Chain
The footnote references other scholars who mention similar works: Mulk al-'Ulama, Ali al-Qari, and Ibn 'Abidin. This connects the work to the broader Hanafi tradition.

This is the 45th biographical entry in the author's list. It introduces Shah Lutf Allah, a commentator known as Mulla Zan, who wrote a hashiah on Sharh al-Wiqaya titled 'Hall al-Mushkilat'. The hashiah contains questions and answers about the matn and sharh. The footnote references other scholars who mention similar works: Mulk al-‘Ulama, Ali al-Qari, and Ibn Abidin.

Key Terms
حل المشكلات (Ḥall al-Mushkilāt): Title of a hashiah meaning 'Solving the Problems', focusing on resolving difficult points in the text.
متن (matn): The base text (here al-Wiqaya) being commented upon.
شرح (sharh): A commentary on the matn, explaining and expanding its content.
حاشية (hashiah): A super-commentary on a sharh or matn, often resolving difficult points or adding glosses.

Nur al-Din al-Ahmad Abadi: A Scholar of Hashiyah
Biographical entry with list of works and lifespan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, major works, and lifespan of Nur al-Din al-Ahmad Abadi, and identify the source of this biography.

Core Idea
He authored hashiahs on many key Hanafi texts; his life spans 1064–1155 AH.

This lesson introduces a lesser-known but prolific Hanafi scholar, Nur al-Din al-Ahmad Abadi. His extensive hashiahs on major works like Sharh al-Wiqaya and al-Talwih demonstrate deep engagement with the tradition. Knowing such scholars helps us trace the chain of commentary and understanding in the later Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar’s full name and lineage
Read the passage carefully to extract his full name: Shaykh Nur al-Din ibn Muhammad Salih al-Ahmad Abadi. Note that he is identified as a scholar (shaykh) and his father’s name is given.
The name shows he is from Ahmadabad (a city in Gujarat) – typical of Indian-born Hanafi scholars.
2
List the subjects of his hashiahs
The passage enumerates the works on which he wrote hashiahs. They include fiqh (Sharh al-Wiqaya), usul al-fiqh (al-Talwih, al-‘Adudi), balaghah (al-Mutawwal), tafsir (Tafsir al-Baydawi), kalam (Sharh al-Mawaqif, Sharh al-Maqasid), mantiq (Sharh al-Matali‘), and nahw (al-Fawa’id al-Diyaiyyah).
The breadth shows he was a multi-disciplinary scholar, trained in the standard Dars-e-Nizami curriculum.
3
Note his birth and death years
His birth was in 1064 AH, death in 1155 AH. Converting to CE: 1064 AH ≈ 1654 CE, 1155 AH ≈ 1742 CE. He lived about 91 years.
These dates place him in the late Mughal period, when many hashiahs were written.
4
Recognize the source of this biography
The passage ends with 'Thus in Sabhat al-Marjan'. This is a biographical work, likely a source for the compiler. Knowing the source helps in verifying the information.

46. ومنهم: الشيخ نور الدين ابن الشيخ محمد صالح الأحمد آبادي، صاحب التصانيف الكثيرة ، منها : حواش كل من «شرح الوقاية»، و«التلويح»، و«العضدي»، و«المطول»، و«تفسير البيضاوي»، و«شرح المواقف»، و«القديمة»، و«شرح المقاصد»، و «شرح المطالع»، و«الفوائد الضيائية»، وغير ذلك، كانت ولادته سنة أربع وستين وألف»، ووفاته سنة خمس وخمسين بعد الألف والمئة. كذا في «سبحة المرجان».
46. Among them: Shaykh Nur al-Din ibn Muhammad Salih al-Ahmad Abadi, author of many works, including hashiahs on Sharh al-Wiqaya, al-Talwih, al-‘Adudi, al-Mutawwal, Tafsir al-Baydawi, Sharh al-Mawaqif, al-Qadimah, Sharh al-Maqasid, Sharh al-Matali‘, al-Fawa’id al-Diyaiyyah, and others. His birth was in the year 1064, and his death in the year 1155. Thus in Sabhat al-Marjan.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is the 46th biographical entry. It presents Shaykh Nur al-Din al-Ahmad Abadi, a prolific writer of hashiahs on many standard Hanafi and theological works. His birth and death years are provided from the source 'Sabhat al-Marjan'.

Key Terms
سبحة المرجان (Subḥat al-Marjān): A biographical work mentioned as the source for these entries.
حواش (ḥawāshīn): Plural of ḥāshiyah; a type of commentary that is a supercommentary on a previous work, often on the margin of pages.

Life of the Author
beginner
10 min
Biography of Mufti Muhammad Yusuf al-Faranji Mahalli
Detailed biography of a Hanafi scholar with lineage and achievements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the lineage, teachers, and scholarly attributes of Mufti Muhammad Yusuf al-Faranji Mahalli as a model Hanafi scholar.

Core Idea
Mufti Muhammad Yusuf embodied both transmitted and rational sciences, tracing his lineage to a Companion.

This biography introduces Mufti Muhammad Yusuf, a luminary of the Hanafi school from Lucknow. As a student of his father and other masters, he mastered all branches of knowledge. His lineage connects him to the noble Companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, underscoring the spiritual and scholarly heritage of the Faranji Mahal tradition.

Guided Path
1
Trace the lineage
Identify the chain of ancestors from Mufti Muhammad Yusuf back to the Companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari. Note the names and death dates mentioned.
The text provides a detailed paternal genealogy.
2
Identify teachers and studies
List the individuals under whom he studied, including his father, Mufti Zuhur Allah, and his brother Mawlana Nur Allah. Note specific texts studied.
He read most standard books with his father and the Risalah al-Qushjiyyah with his brother.
3
Note scholarly attributes
Extract the qualities praised: beauty and perfection, comprehensive knowledge, spiritual struggle, worship, and unveiling (mukashafah).
The author describes him as 'the Joseph of his time'.
4
Recognize the author's own works
The author refers readers to his treatises 'Khayr al-‘Amal fi Tarajim Ahl Faranji Mahal' and 'Inba’ al-Khillan bi Anba’ ‘Ulama’ Hindustan' for further biographies.
These are additional sources for Hanafi scholars of Lucknow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
47. ومنهم : أستاذ أستاذي عم والدي، مولانا المفتي محمد يوسف بن المفتي محمد أصغر، المتوفى في التاسع عشر من رجب سنة خمس وخمسين بعد الألف والمئتين، يوم السبت، ابن المفتي أبي الرحم بن ملا محمد يعقوب بن مولانا عبد العزيز – المتوفّى لتسع خلون من ذي العقدة سنة ست وستين ، وقيل : سنة خمس وستين بعد الألف والمئة - ابن ملا سعيد بن ملاً قطب الدين الشهيد السهالوي – المتوفى في يوم الاثنين التاسع عشر من رجب سنة إحدى وقيل : ثلاث بعد الألف والمئة – ابن الشيخ عبد الحليم بن الشيخ عبد الكريم بن الشيخ أحمد بن الشيخ حافظ ، وهو من أحفاد الشيخ علاء الدين الأنصاري، وهو من أحفاد خواجه عبد الله الأنصاري، من نسل سيدنا أبي أيوب الأنصاري الصحابي . وليطلب تمام نسبه وتراجم ،آبائه، وكذا تراجم كثير من أعزّتي وأقاربي وعلماء بلدة لكنو المقيمين في محلة فرنجى محلّ، من رسالتي : (خير العمل في تراجم أهل فرنجى محل» التي جعلتها جزءاً لرسالتي «إنباء الخلان بأنباء علماء هندوستان».
كان رحمه الله يوسف عصره في الجمال والكمال، جامعاً للفروع والأصول، حاوياً للمعقول والمنقول ، ذا مجاهدة ورياضة، وعبادة ومكاشفة، متهجداً متعبداً، ولد في حياة جده سنة ثلاث وعشرين بعد الألف والمئتين، وقرأ أكثر الكتب الدرسية بحضرة والده، وقدراً منها بحضرة مولانا المفتي ظهور الله ، و«الرسالة القوشجيّة» بحضرة أخيه مولانا نور الله المرحوم.
وبايع على يد مولانا أحمد أنوار الحق المتوفّى في السادس والعشرين من شعبان - ست وثلاثين بعد الألف والمئتين - ابن مولانا أحمد عبد الحق – المتوفى في يوم الجمعة تاسع ذي الحجة من السنة السابعة والستين بعد الألف والمئة – ابن ملا سعيد بن
47. Among them: The teacher of my teacher, my paternal uncle, our master Mufti Muhammad Yusuf ibn Mufti Muhammad Asghar, died on the 19th of Rajab in the year 1255, on Saturday, son of Mufti Abu al-Rahm ibn Mulla Muhammad Ya‘qub ibn Mawlana Abd al-Aziz – died on the 9th of Dhu al-Qa‘dah in the year 1166, or as said: 1165 – ibn Mulla Sa‘id ibn Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Shahid al-Sahalawi – died on Monday the 19th of Rajab in the year 1101, or as said: 1103 – ibn Shaykh Abd al-Halim ibn Shaykh Abd al-Karim ibn Shaykh Ahmad ibn Shaykh Hafiz, and he is among the descendants of Shaykh Ala al-Din al-Ansari, and he is among the descendants of Khwaja Abd Allah al-Ansari, from the lineage of our master Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, the Companion. For the full genealogy and biographies of his forefathers, as well as biographies of many of my dear ones, relatives, and scholars of the town of Lucknow residing in the Faranji Mahal quarter, see my treatise 'Khayr al-‘Amal fi Tarajim Ahl Faranji Mahal', which I made a part of my treatise 'Inba’ al-Khillan bi Anba’ ‘Ulama’ Hindustan'.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, was the Joseph of his time in beauty and perfection, comprehensive in subsidiary and principal matters, encompassing rational and transmitted knowledge, one of struggle and spiritual exercise, worship and unveiling, a night-praying worshipper. He was born during the lifetime of his grandfather in the year 1223, and studied most of the standard books in the presence of his father, and some in the presence of our master Mufti Zuhur Allah, and the Risalah al-Qushjiyyah in the presence of his brother Mawlana Nur Allah, the deceased.
And he gave allegiance to our master Ahmad Anwar al-Haqq, who died on the 26th of Sha‘ban in the year 1236, son of our master Ahmad Abd al-Haqq – who died on Friday the 9th of Dhu al-Hijjah in the year 1167 – ibn Mulla Sa‘id ibn
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This is the 47th biographical entry, focusing on Mufti Muhammad Yusuf, a prominent Hanafi scholar from the Faranji Mahal area of Lucknow. The text traces his lineage back to the Companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, lists his teachers, spiritual guide, and praises his character. The author refers readers to his own works for further biographies. The entry cuts off mid-sentence at the end of the page.

Key Terms
فرنجى محلّ (Faranjī Maḥall): A locality in Lucknow, India, known for its Hanafi scholars.
إنباء الخلان بأنباء علماء هندوستان (Inbā’ al-Khillān bi Anbā’ ‘Ulamā’ Hindūstān): A biographical work by the author covering scholars of India.

Key Takeaway
Mufti Muhammad Yusuf al-Faranji Mahalli represents the ideal Hanafi scholar who combined spiritual discipline with comprehensive knowledge, supported by a noble lineage.
